1401 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Rose v. City & County of Denver


No. 97CA1683


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


990 P.2d 1120; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 162; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 3376



June 10, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Petition Denied December 20, 1999. Released for Publication January 19, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Connie L. Peterson, Judge. No. 95CV33.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, ORDER VACATED, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowner appealed a judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which dismissed her claims of discrimination, constitutional violations, malicious prosecution, and false imprisonment against defendants, a police officer, city and county municipalities. Plaintiff also appealed the trial court's denial of her motion to add a party and an award of attorney's fees to defendant police officer.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a lawsuit against defendants after she was arrested for disturbing the peace when she interfered with a tree cutting crew. Plaintiff's claims were dismissed. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err by directing a verdict on plaintiff's discrimination claim. The court stated that if the plaintiff persisted in conduct that alarmed the tree crew and prevented them from pursuing an activity in a safe manner that the plaintiff knew was lawful and authorized, then her conduct could have been properly characterized as a breach of the peace. The court also held that the plaintiff could not join another officer as a defendant because a one year statute of limitation applied and the relation-back doctrine did not apply. Her other claims were time-barred because she did not obtain court permission when she filed her amended answer. Lastly, the court held that the trial court erred when it awarded defendant officer attorney's fees based on state standards. A federal standard should have been applied. Therefore, the trial court's judgment was affirmed and the fee award was remanded.


OUTCOME: The trial court's dismissal of the plaintiff's discrimination and other claims against defendants was affirmed because the trial court did not err when it rejected her claims. The order denying plaintiff's motion to include another defendant was also affirmed because the one-year statute of limitation period had run. The order awarding fees to defendant police officer was remanded for a determination of fees under a federal standard.

 

1402 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Relative Value Studies, Inc. v. McGraw-Hill Cos.


No. 97CA2165


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


981 P.2d 687; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 145; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 3151



May 27, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Robert P. Fullerton, Judge. No. 96CV5359.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed an order from the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado) that granted summary judgment for defendant publisher in an action to collect a royalty percentage of the purchase price defendant received from the sale of rights to plaintiff's books and databases. Plaintiff claimed the order was void where the trial judge had moved outside his judicial district in violation of Colo. Const. art. VI, § 11.


OVERVIEW: In an action to collect a royalty percentage of the purchase price defendant publisher received from the sale of rights to plaintiff's books and databases, summary judgment for defendant was affirmed. Plaintiff argued that the parties' contract entitled it to a percentage of the purchase price and contended that the judgment was void for lack of subject matter jurisdiction because the trial judge had moved to a new residence outside the judicial district in which he was appointed in violation of Colo. Const. art. VI, § 11. The appellate court held that the trial court did not lack jurisdiction to enter the order based on the fact that the trial judge had moved outside the district. The judge did not lose authority to act because of the violation, and the judgment was not void. Summary judgment was appropriate where there was no genuine issue of material fact. The contract terms were not ambiguous and the trial court did not err in its construction of the contract. The phrase "publisher's net receipts from the annual revenues," on which plaintiff's royalties were calculated, did not include revenues received by defendant for assigning the entire contract to another publisher.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for defendant publisher was affirmed in an action to collect a royalty percentage of the purchase price defendant received from the sale of rights to plaintiff's books and databases. The trial court did not lack jurisdiction to enter the order, and summary judgment was appropriate where there was no genuine issue of material fact. The contract was not ambiguous and the trial court did not err in its construction.

 

1403 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Vigil


No. 96CA0426


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


983 P.2d 805; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 131; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 2662



May 13, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied September 13, 1999. Released for Publication September 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Larry J. Naves, Judge. No. 71CR64482.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which denied his Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c) motion for post-conviction relief from his conviction for issuing a bad check in 1971. Defendant sought the relief because the statute under which he was convicted was declared unconstitutional in 1972.


OVERVIEW: In March 1991, defendant filed a Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c) motion seeking to vacate his 1971 conviction, arguing that, because the statute under which he had been convicted had been declared unconstitutional, his conviction was void. Concluding that because defendant's motion was a direct attack rather than a collateral attack and the time-bar in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-5-40 (1998), did not apply, the trial court granted the motion. The state appealed, and the appellate court found defendant's motion was a collateral attack. On certiorari review, the supreme court remanded the case for further proceedings pursuant to § 16-5-402 to determine if defendant had established justifiable excuse or excusable neglect for the untimely filing On remand, after a hearing, the trial court found that defendant had not established justifiable excuse or excusable neglect and denied defendant's motion. After another appeal and remand, trial court ruled it had jurisdiction, § 16-5-402 was constitutional, and defendant's conviction was not void. On appeal again, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment that defendant did not show excusable neglect in filing his post-conviction motion for relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court holding that defendant had failed to establish justifiable excuse or excusable neglect for the untimely filing of his motion for post-conviction relief, and that the trial court's findings were supported by the record.

 

1404 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Diaz


No. 98CA1347


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


985 P.2d 83; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 136; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 2676



May 13, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied April 3, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 2487. Petition for Rehearing Denied June 17, 1999. Cert Petition Denied October 4, 1999. Released for Publication October 13, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Arapahoe County. Honorable James F. Macrum, Jr., Judge. No. 94CR1780.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the District Court of Arapahoe County (Colorado), which denied his Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c) motion for postconviction relief. Defendant contended that he was denied due process of law because Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-90-101 (1998) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of second-degree assault and reckless endangerment following an altercation with law enforcement officials. On appeal, a division of the appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction, but declined to address his constitutional challenges to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-90-101 (1998), because they had not been raised in the trial court. Defendant thereafter filed a Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c) motion raising the constitutional claims that the appellate court had declined to address on his direct appeal. The trial court denied defendant's motion without a hearing and upheld the constitutionality of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-90-101. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion, concluding that he had failed to assert a basis for affording him relief based on a violation of his constitutional rights. The court held that the arguments raised by defendant were without merit, that the supreme court had repeatedly held § 13-90-101 to be constitutional, and that a trial court was not required to use a balancing test before determining whether to permit impeachment evidence by prior felony convictions of a witness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying defendant's motion for post-conviction relief because defendant had not shown any basis for his assertion that admitting evidence of a witness's prior felony convictions violated his constitutional rights to due process and equal protection.

 

1405 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. A.C.


No. 98CA0552


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


991 P.2d 304; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 108; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 2388



April 29, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended May 27, 1999. Petition for Rehearing Denied May 27, 1999. Certiorari Petition Granted January 18, 2000. Released for Publication January 19, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable Peter W. Booth, Judge. No. 97JD921.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a juvenile, challenged a judgment from the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado), which denied his request for a jury trial in delinquency proceedings. The juvenile court found him guilty of possession of a handgun by a juvenile and of the commission of an act that would constitute criminally negligent homicide.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a juvenile, was found guilty of possession of a handgun by a juvenile and of the commission of an act that would constitute criminally negligent homicide. Appellant contended on appeal that he was entitled to a jury trial; that denial of a jury trial violated his constitutional rights because he was facing potential commitment for over six months; and that to the extent Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-2-107(2) precluded a jury trial, it was unconstitutional. The court, in holding Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-2-107 (1998) constitutional, found appellant did not qualify under the statute for a jury trial and juveniles are not automatically entitled to a jury trial. The court held that juvenile proceedings are designed to provide guidance and rehabilitation while protecting society, rather than determining guilt and punishment; and, that the express constitutional right to a jury trial afforded to an adult facing a serious criminal charge does not extend to a juvenile in delinquency proceedings, under the federal or state constitution, even when the consequences include possible commitment for over six months. The judgment of the trial court was, accordingly, affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying appellant a trial by jury and held that delinquency proceedings are unique and, because of that, not all rights afforded to adult offenders are automatically available to juvenile offenders. The court found that juvenile courts are permitted to authorize a jury trial in limited instances under Colorado law, but due process is not violated if a jury trial is not provided..

 

1406 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Scott v. Matlack, Inc.


No. 97CA1496


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


1 P.3d 185; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 91; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 2097



April 15, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and As Modified Petition for Rehearing DENIED June 3, 1999. Certiorari Petition Granted May 30, 2000. Released for Publication June 15, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Joseph E. Meyer, III, Judge. No. 94CV6546.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a trucking company and a refinery, appealed a judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado) in favor of plaintiffs, a driver and his wife, in an action for negligence and loss of consortium.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff driver worked as a leased operator under an agreement with defendant trucking company. He elected the contract provision for workers' compensation benefits under defendant's group policy. Plaintiff was injured when he fell off a trailer-truck while he was loading asphalt for defendant trucking company at defendant refinery. Workers' compensation benefits were awarded to plaintiff under the group policy. Plaintiff and his wife also brought action against defendants for negligence and loss of consortium. A jury returned a verdict in favor of plaintiffs on both claims. Defendants appealed and contended that the exclusivity provisions of the Workers' Compensation Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-40-101 et seq. (1998), barred the action. The court held that the action was not barred because § 8-40-301(5) overrode both §§ 8-44-102 and 8-40-302(5)(b) and provided that leased operators were not employees under the Act. However, the court reversed and remand because it found that the trial court abused its discretion by admitting plaintiffs' evidence of violations of the Occupational Safety and Health Act (OSHA), 29 U.S.C.S. § 653(b)(4), as a discovery sanction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment in favor of plaintiffs, a driver and his wife, in an action for negligence and loss of consortium. While the court held that the action was not barred by the exclusivity provisions of the Workers' Compensation Act, it found that the trial court abused its discretion by admitting plaintiffs' evidence of violations of the Occupational Safety and Health Act as a discovery sanction.

 

1407 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


In re A.P.E.


No. 98CA0588


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


988 P.2d 172; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 78; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1941



April 1, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended April 29, 1999. Released for Publication May 18, 1999.
Cert Petition Granted November 8, 1999. Released for Publication November 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable D. Richard Toth, Judge. Honorable Geoffrey H. deWolfe, Judge. No. 97JD1493.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado), which adjudicated him a delinquent after a bench trial finding him guilty of committing acts that would, if committed by an adult, constitute possession of an illegal weapon and unlawfully carrying a concealed weapon.


OVERVIEW: Because of defendant's conduct, a police officer contacted him and conducted a search. Defendant informed the officer that he was carrying a concealed knife. The officer examined the weapon, and defendant was later charged with one count of possession of an illegal weapon in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-12-102(4), and one count of carrying a concealed weapon in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-12-105. The lower court adjudicated defendant a delinquent, and this appeal followed. Defendant contended that his conviction for possession of an illegal weapon should be reversed because the lack of a definition of the phrase 'metallic knuckles' in the criminal code rendered Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-12-102(4) unconstitutionally vague as applied to him. The court disagreed. The court held that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-12-102(4) was neither facially void for vagueness as to its prohibition of possession of metallic knuckles, nor was it unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant and the particular weapon at issue here. Defendant next contended there was insufficient evidence to support either conviction. The court ruled there was sufficient evidence to support both convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court adjudicating defendant a delinquent because there was sufficient evidence to support defendant's convictions for possession of an illegal weapon and unlawfully carrying a concealed weapon and neither of the statutes were unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant.

 

1408 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Janssen v. Denver Career Serv. Bd.


No. 98CA0100


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


998 P.2d 9; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 81; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1812



April 1, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Nancy E. Rice, Judge. No. 96CV4318.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city employee appealed an order of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which affirmed a hearing officer for appellee administrative board's decision to uphold plaintiff's termination by appellee municipal department.


OVERVIEW: Appellee municipal department terminated plaintiff city employee for allegedly using marijuana in a city vehicle while on duty. Plaintiff appealed that decision to a hearing officer for appellee administrative board. The officer found no abuse of discretion by appellee department and denied plaintiff's appeal. Plaintiff did not request appellee board to reopen or to reconsider the hearing officer's decision, but instead, he sought judicial review under Colo. R. Civ. P. 106(a)(4). Defendants moved to dismiss and contended that plaintiff failed to exhaust his administrative remedies. The trial court initially denied the motion, but ultimately agreed with defendants' contention. Nevertheless, the trial court also considered the merits of plaintiff's complaint and then affirmed the hearing officer's decision. The court affirmed and held that plaintiff failed to exhaust his administrative remedies. The court found that the hearing officer's decision was subject to reopening and reconsideration under the Denver City Charter C5.25 because plaintiff contended that the hearing officer had erroneously interpreted personnel rules.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judicial order that affirmed an administrative order upholding plaintiff's termination by appellee municipal department. The court found that plaintiff failed to exhaust his administrative remedies as required under the city charter. The court said that plaintiff was required to request appellee board to reopen or to reconsider the hearing officer's decision before seeking judicial review.

 

1409 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Krupp v. Breckenridge Sanitation Dist.


No. 97CA1996


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


1 P.3d 178; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 82; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1796



April 1, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Petition Granted May 22, 2000. Released for Publication June 15, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Summit County. Honorable W. Terry Ruckriegle, Judge. No. 96CV59.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developers appealed an order of the Summit County District Court (Colorado), which denied them relief under Colo. R. Civ. P. 106(a)(4), granted summary judgment to defendant government entities on their constitutional claims, and denied their motion to amend their complaint.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff developers were assessed unequal permit fees to construct residential buildings. Defendant government entities' fees were affirmed on administrative review, and plaintiffs filed suit. Plaintiffs' relief under Colo. R. Civ. P. 106(a)(4) was denied, summary judgment was granted to defendants, and plaintiffs' motion to amend their complaint was denied, which resulted in plaintiffs' appeal. The court held defendants had no authority to condition plaintiffs' permits on the fee, which was directly related to the impact of the development, and thus did not take plaintiffs' property. The trial court properly affirmed the fee because it was supported by sufficient evidence. Colo. Rev. Stat. § 32-1-1001(1)(j) (1998), authorizing defendants to set service fees, was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority; the statute, along with local rules, prevented unnecessary exercise of discretionary power. The classifications used to set the fees were rationally based and did not violate equal protection. Plaintiffs' motion to amend their complaint was properly denied as untimely because there was no reason for the delay in requesting amendment. The orders were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order denying relief and granting defendant governmental entities' motion for summary judgment was affirmed. The defendants did not take plaintiff developers' property, and the permit fees did not violate equal protection. The statute authorizing defendants to set the fees was not an unconstitutional delegation of authority. The order denying plaintiffs' motion to amend their complaint was affirmed because it was untimely.

 

1410 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Jamison v. People


No. 98CA0782


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


988 P.2d 177; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 74; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1794



April 1, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied May 6, 1999. As Corrected May 13, 1999. Cert Petition Denied October 18, 1999. Released for Publication November 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Connie L. Peterson, Judge. No. 97CV7610.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the dismissal by the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), pursuant to Colo. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(5), of plaintiff's complaint for a declaratory judgment to determine whether Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 17-2-201(5)(g) and 18-3-412.5(1), requiring DNA samples and registration of convicted sex offenders, applied to him.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was convicted of attempted first degree sexual assault and adjudicated an habitual offender. One month before plaintiff was convicted, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-2-201(5)(g) (1998) took effect, requiring sex offenders to provide a blood sample for DNA testing. Six years later, Colo. Rev. Stat. 18-3-412.5(1) (1998) was enacted, requiring convicted sex offenders released after July 1, 1991 to register with local law enforcement agencies. Plaintiff filed suit seeking a declaratory judgment that these statutes did not apply to him because they were not in effect at the time he was alleged to have committed the offenses for which he was convicted and adjudged an habitual offender. He claimed the statutes were unconstitutional ex post facto laws and violated his right to equal protection. The court dismissed plaintiff's complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal, holding that, because the intent of the statutes was remedial and not punitive, they did not unconstitutionally enhance plaintiff's punishment and were not ex post facto laws. The court also held that there was no equal protection violation because the law treated similarly all persons similarly situated.


OUTCOME: Dismissal of plaintiff's complaint for declaratory judgment was affirmed. The court held that the statutes were not ex post facto laws because the intent of the statutes was remedial, not punitive, and they did not unconstitutionally enhance plaintiff's punishment. The court held that the laws did not violate equal protection law because they treated similarly all persons similarly situated.

 

1411 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Robertson v. City & County of Denver


No. 98CA0167


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


978 P.2d 156; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 65; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1625



March 18, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied April 15, 1999. Released for Publication June 21, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Federico C. Alvarez, Judge. No. 90CV603.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff gun vendors appealed the judgment from the District Court of the city and county of Denver (Colorado) which determined that a Denver ordinance banning assault weapons was not unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff gun vendors sued defendant municipalities claiming that a Denver ordinance banning assault weapons was unconstitutional. After the trial court found some parts unconstitutionally vague and severed portions which it determined were not unconstitutionally vague, plaintiffs appealed. On appeal, the court noted that the ordinance provided for criminal sanctions, did not contain a scienter requirement, and implicated the constitutional right to bear arms. The court affirmed judgment that the ordinance was constitutional because the trial court did not err in determining that the provisions stricken as vague were severable from the remaining provisions. The court added that plaintiffs presented no evidence of legislative intent that would indicate that Denver would not have passed the ordinance had it known that certain subsections of it were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment that the ordinance banning assault weapons was constitutional because the trial court did not err in determining that the provisions stricken as vague were severable from the remaining provisions of the statute.

 

1412 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Moran


No. 97CA1800


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


983 P.2d 143; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 47; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1228



March 4, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied September 13, 1999. Released for Publication September 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Mesa County. Honorable Nicholas R. Massaro, Judge. No. 96CR609.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, by the District Court of Mesa County (Colorado), of possession of a controlled substance and of marijuana, and failure to provide evidence of insurance. He contended that the trial court unconstitutionally permitted the prosecution to refer, on cross-examination and in closing argument, to alleged omissions from his statements to police, and that his indictment on the evidence of insurance charge was deficient.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for possession of a schedule II controlled substance and of less than one ounce of marijuana, and of failure to provide evidence of insurance. The court affirmed the conviction. It held that because defendant's statements to the arresting officer were a subject of his direct examination, he could constitutionally be subjected to cross-examination about those statements, and because the prosecutor's questions about alleged omissions from the statements were reasonably related to the subjects covered by the defendant's testimony, they were properly admitted; thus neither the questions nor the reference in closing argument to the omission was an improper comment on defendant's silence. The court also held that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-204(2) (1998), describing schedule II substances, did not create an additional element of proof as to quantity of the substances required for a stimulant effect. Furthermore, the information charging defendant with driving without proof of insurance was not deficient and stated a cognizable offense, and that several incidences of alleged prosecutorial misconduct did not affect the fundamental fairness of the trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant' s conviction. It held that because defendant's statements were the subject of his direct examination, the prosecution's references to alleged omissions in the statements were not improper comments on defendant's silence. The court further held that the evidence to sufficient to support the conviction of possession of a controlled substance, and that he information charging the insurance violation was not deficient.

 

1413 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Colorado Ltd. Gaming Control Comm'n


No. 97CA1542


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


1 P.3d 175; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 54; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1221



March 4, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and As Modified, Petition for Rehearing DENIED June 3, 1999. Released for Publication June 15, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Colorado Limited Gaming Control Commission.



DISPOSITION: ADOPTION OF RULE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of Colorado Limited Gaming Control Commission Regulation No. 47.1-1901 (Rule 19), 1 Colo. Code Reg. § 207-1, that was promulgated to define the boundaries of the area in which limited gaming was permitted in the city of Black Hawk. Appellant sought review of the adoption of Rule 19 pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-47.1-521 (1998), and Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-4-106 (1998).


OVERVIEW: Appellant owned a portion of vacant property in the city of Black Hawk, which included several mill sites. Pursuant to its authority under the Limited Gaming Act of 1991, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-47.1-101 et seq. (1998), appellee commission proposed Rule 19 to determine the limited gaming area district in the city of Black Hawk and held public hearings in compliance with Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-4-103 (1998). The issue of how much of appellant's property was situated within the district was presented. Appellee determined that only part of appellant's property was situated within the district, and appellant challenged the determination, claiming all of his property should be included. The court found that gaming was restricted by Colo. Const. art. XVIII, § 9 and Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-47.1-105(1998) to the commercial district as defined by the city ordinance adopted on May 4, 1978, which established city boundaries, that existing maps were difficult to read and ambiguous, and that appellee made a factual determination as to city boundaries, based on the information before it, which decision was affirmed because it was not arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that appellee complied with the rule-making requirements of the applicable statute, that there was factual support of its resolution of the gaming district boundary, and that appellee did not act unreasonably, arbitrarily or capriciously in adopting the rule determining the limited gaming area district. Accordingly, the court affirmed appellee's adoption of the rule.

 

1414 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Feigin v. Digital Interactive Assocs., Inc.


No. 95CA0387


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


987 P.2d 876; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 17; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 683



February 4, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied March 11, 1999. Cert Petition Denied October 18, 1999. Released for Publication November 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Nancy E. Rice, Judge. No. 94CV3218.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed an order of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado) that denied his summary judgment motion asserting qualified immunity as to a counterclaim by defendants in response to plaintiff's action against them alleging various violations of securities laws and for which plaintiff obtained an ex parte temporary restraining order freezing certain assets of defendants.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, the Colorado Securities Commissioner, filed a civil action against defendants, a venture capital firm and its corporate officers, alleging various violations of securities laws. Prior to the complaint, plaintiff obtained search warrants for the search of defendant firm's offices and banks. Plaintiff also obtained an ex parte temporary restraining order (TRO) freezing certain of defendants' assets. Defendants filed a counterclaim. Plaintiff filed a motion for summary judgment pursuant to Colo. R. Civ. P. 56 on grounds of qualified immunity, which the trial court denied. The trial court again denied summary judgment following a remand. On appeal, the court found plaintiff's conduct in omitting from his opinion, and his investigator's failure to also include a noteworthy case citation in the affidavit in support of issuance of the search warrant and TRO, was not an act or omission so clearly unconstitutional that any reasonable person would have known his conduct violated defendants' Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV, or other rights. Moreover, plaintiff's application for the TRO also did not violate a clearly established due process right. The order was reversed.


OUTCOME: Denial of plaintiff's summary judgment motion asserting qualified immunity in defendant's counterclaim to his action for violations of securities laws was reversed; the omission of a case citation in plaintiff's opinion and investigator's affidavit in support of a search warrant and temporary restraining order (TRO) did not violate defendants' constitutional, or other, rights. Neither did the TRO application violate any due process right.

 

1415 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gonzales


No. 97CA2102


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


973 P.2d 732; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 1; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 173



January 7, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Pueblo County. Honorable James H. Frasher, Jr., Judge. No. 88CR435.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the District Court of Pueblo County (Colorado), which denied his motion for postconviction relief after his parole was revoked and he was reincarcerated for the period remaining on his sentence for felony theft, without credit for his time served on parole, pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-22.5-403.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty in 1989 to felony theft in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-401(2)(c) and was sentenced to ten years in prison. He was released on parole in 1994. His parole was revoked in 1995, and he was reincarcerated for the period remaining on his sentence, without credit for his time served on parole, pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-22.5-403. Defendant filed a motion for postconviction relief, which the trial court denied. The court affirmed. The definition of "nonviolent felony offenses" in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-222.5-405(5) excluded the type of felony theft for which defendant was convicted, and thus he was not eligible to receive credit for his time served on parole under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-22.5-403. Defendant was not denied his right to equal protection because this statutory definition was not irrational or unrelated to legitimate governmental interests. The court rejected defendant's contention that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-22.5-403 was ambiguous and therefore had to be construed in his favor pursuant to the rule of lenity. Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-22.5-403 expressly denied him credit towards his sentence for the time served on parole.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed denial of defendant's motion for postconviction relief. Defendant was not denied equal protection by Colorado law excluding the offense for which defendant was convicted from those offenses for which an offender was eligible to receive credit for time served on parole because the exclusion was not irrational.

 

1416 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Boselli Invs., L.L.C. v. Division of Empl.


No. 98CA1536


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


975 P.2d 204; 1999 Colo. App. LEXIS 9; 1999 Colo. J. C.A.R. 177



January 7, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. DD No. 9721-1997.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer challenged the judgment of the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado, which sustained the holding denying petitioner's application for transfer of ratings experience under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-76-104(5)(g).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner employer had filed a request to transfer the ratings experience for businesses it had purchased. Respondent employment division denied the request because it was not made within the statutory thirty-day time limit for filing such requests. On appeal, petitioner contended that it had good cause for its untimely filing and that it was error to conclude that there was no good cause exception to the thirty-day time limit. The court held that under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-76-104(5)(g), the application for the transfer of ratings experience had to be filed within thirty days after the date of transfer of the business unit. Because the statutory directive was mandatory and did not contain a provision for excusing an untimely application upon a showing of good cause, there was no error in declining to read such a requirement into the statute. Moreover, respondent had a legitimate interest in administrative efficiency by enforcing the thirty-day limitation, which was rationally related to a legitimate government interest. Thus, petitioner's equal protection rights were not violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying petitioner employer's application for ratings transfer because under the plain language of the statute there was no good cause exception to the mandatory thirty-day limitation for filing such an application.

 

1417 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


County Rd. Users Ass'n v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 97CA2035


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


987 P.2d 861; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 318; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 6378



December 24, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and As Modified, Petition for Rehearing of Plaintiffs-Appellants Denied May 27, 1999. Petitions for Rehearing of Defendants-Appellees Denied. Cert Petition Granted November 1, 1999. Released for Publication November 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Archuleta County. Honorable Gregory G. Lyman, Judge. Honorable Al H. Haas, Judge. No. 95CV71.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff association sought review of the decision of the District Court of Archuleta County (Colorado) which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, the Archuleta County Board of County Commissioners and the Town of Pagosa Springs. Plaintiffs contended that the trial court erred in denying its request for a writ of mandamus because defendants had a duty to refer their petition to the electorate for a vote.


OVERVIEW: Defendant county had adopted a county wide sales tax with a specific distribution formula. Plaintiff association sought to amend the distribution formula. Plaintiff had submitted signed petitions for verification as required, which indicated that the proposal related to the sales tax which were verified and certified that they bore the requisite number of signatures. A writ of mandamus required a three-part test: (1) a plaintiff must have a clear right to the relief sought; (2) the agency must have a clear duty to perform the act requested; and (3) there must be no other available remedy. The court found that defendant commissioners had a duty to submit the matter to the electorate upon certification by the clerk and recorder is ministerial and not discretionary in nature. Therefore, the court concluded that plaintiff had a clear right to the remedy of mandamus, and that there was no other available remedy. Accordingly, the court held that relief in the nature of mandamus compelled defendant to place the initiative on the ballot and that reversal of the trial court's order to the contrary was required.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the cause was remanded with directions to enter an order directing the commissioners to place the initiative proposal on the ballot at the first and earliest opportunity.

 

1418 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Edwards


No. 97CA0232


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


971 P.2d 1080; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 327; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 6368



December 24, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication in Error February 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Nancy E. Rice, Judge. No. 96CR2588.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgment of District Court, Denver County (Colorado), which determined he was a habitual criminal under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-13-103 before sentencing him to life imprisonment for his first-degree assault conviction, contending habitual criminal statute was unconstitutional because it denied a defendant the right to jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree assault. In a hearing held pursuant to the habitual criminal statute, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-13-103, the trial court determined that defendant had six prior felony convictions. It then sentenced him to life imprisonment. Defendant appealed the judgment determining him to be a habitual criminal, contending the habitual criminal statute was unconstitutional on the ground that it denied a defendant the right to a jury trial on habitual criminal charges. The court affirmed the judgment. The right to a trial by jury for criminal defendants was protected by both U.S. Const. amend. VI and Colo. Const. art. II, § 516. Such right applied to trials on the issue of guilt or innocence, but did not extend to sentencing. The habitual criminal statute did not establish a substantive offense, but prescribed circumstances wherein a defendant convicted of a specific crime could be more severely punished because of his previous convictions. As such, the statute related only to sentencing enhancement for the underlying felony. Because criminal habitualness was a sentence enhancer, there was, therefore, no right to have a jury determine such status.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment determining that defendant was a habitual criminal. Right to a jury trial did not extend to sentencing and since a defendant's status as a habitual criminal was a sentence enhancer, not a separate offense, there was no right to have a jury determine such status.

Bruce v. City of Colorado Springs


No. 97CA1486


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


971 P.2d 679; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 300; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 6121



December 10, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable Thomas K. Kane, Judge. No. 97CV1644.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff challenged a judgment of the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado), which denied his request for a preliminary injunction and granted summary judgment in favor of defendant city. Plaintiff contested the constitutionality and validity of a mail ballot election.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied plaintiff's request for a preliminary injunction to prevent defendant city from submitting a zoning ordinance to a special election by mail ballot as provided for under the Mail Ballot Election Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 1-7.5-101, et seq. (1998) and granted summary judgment in favor of defendant. The court found that a compelling state interest existed in encouraging increased voter participation and mail ballot elections served to meet this interest; elections under § 1-7.5-101 were thus not unconstitutional. The court found that even if a voter was prevented from exercising his or her right to vote because of the lack of a stamp, such action did not constitute an unconstitutional poll tax in the absence of a willful intent to deprive the voter of the right by imposing such requirement. The court found that defendant's use of a single, tri-fold envelope substantially complied with the requirements of the statute because it concealed the voter's mark and protected the secrecy of the vote that was cast. The court affirmed and found that the date of the special election was valid because the issue did not concern a fiscal matter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that elections under the mail ballot election act were constitutional where a compelling state interest existed in encouraging increased voter participation and mail ballot elections served to meet this interest.

State v. Johnson


No. 96CA1743


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


987 P.2d 855; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 307; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 6107



December 10, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and As Modified, Petition for Rehearing DENIED February 11, 1999.
Cert Petition Denied November 1, 1999. Released for Publication November 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable John N. McMullen, Judge. No. 96CR21.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the District Court of the City and County of Denver, Colorado, of several offenses including two counts of first degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed: (1) the direct-file statute in effect, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-2-805(1) (1996), was unconstitutional; (2) the trial court erred in denying a mistrial; (3) a statement he made to police should have been suppressed; (4) statements by two witnesses should not have been admitted; and (5) he was erroneously convicted of two first degree murder counts for the death of one victim. The appellate court held: (1) the uniformity provision, Colo. Const. art. VI, § 19, only required uniformity in laws relating to the organization, jurisdiction, powers, proceedings, and practice of all courts of the same class, thus § 19-2-805(1) was constitutional; (2) the prosecutor's promise made to a witness of a shorter sentence than allowed did not rise to the level of conduct that was shocking to the universal sense of justice, and did not prejudice defendant, so denial of the mistrial motion was not an abuse of discretion; (3) evidence supported a finding of waiver of defendant's Miranda rights; and (4) the witnesses were not motivated to lie when the statements were made. However, the trial court did err in entering two murder convictions based on the same victim and a single act.


OUTCOME: With the exception of defendant's convictions for first degree murder, the judgment was affirmed. Defendant's convictions for first degree murder were vacated, and the cause was remanded for entry of a single first degree murder conviction.

People v. Bastian


No. 96CA1333


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


981 P.2d 203; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 295; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 5951



November 27, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied February 18, 1999. Certiorari Petition Denied August 16, 1999. Released for Publication August 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Larimer County. Honorable Steven E. Shinn, Judge. No. 95CR1227.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, SENTENCE VACATED, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of Larimer County (Colorado) of harassment by stalking, pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-9-111 (1998) and was sentenced to 10 years' incarceration. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's crime consisted of making a credible threat to another person and, in connection with such threat, repeatedly following the person, under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-9-111(4)(a)(I), (II) (1998). Effective July 1, 1995, the statute was amended to increase its penalty from that of a misdemeanor to that of a felony. Prior to July 1, 1995, defendant initiated the crime by writing threatening letters to the victim from prison. In August of 1995, he was released from prison and consummated the crime by following the victim on a number of occasions. Because the crime was not committed until all the elements were complete, the felony sentence was applicable to him. However, the sentence imposed was not statutorily authorized. Defendant's sentence was increased under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-105(9)(a) because he was on parole when the crime was committed. This increase took the sentence outside of the presumptive range, so the habitual criminal sentencing statute, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-13-101(2), could not be applied to quadruple the already increased sentence. Defendant's maximum possible sentence was 6 years, rather than the 10 years imposed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. His sentence was reversed, and the matter was remanded for resentencing.

State v. Loeser


No. 97CA0939


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


981 P.2d 197; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 293; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 5954



November 27, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and As Modified, Petitions for Rehearing DENIED January 14, 1999.
Certiorari Petition Denied July 26, 1999. Released for Publication August 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Routt County. Honorable Richard P. Doucette, Judge. No. 96CR58.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Routt County (Colorado), which convicted and sentenced him for vehicular homicide while driving under the influence, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-106(1)(b). Defendant contended that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-106(1) violated his right to equal protection and due process.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of vehicular homicide while driving under the influence, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-106(1)(b). On appeal he contended that the statute violated his right to equal protection and due process, because Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-106(1)(c), provided for disparate sentences for persons convicted under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-106(1)(a) & (b). Specifically, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-106(1) classified a conviction for vehicular homicide with a "reckless" mens rea as a class 4 felony but classified the same offense as a strict liability crime and a class 3 felony if it involves driving under the influence. When compared with persons convicted of vehicular homicide while driving recklessly, defendant was subjected to a greater penalty for identical conduct. The court affirmed, holding that the statutes did not violate equal protection, because the conduct punished was not identical, and the disparity was reasonably related to a legitimate governmental objective. The legislature could establish more severe penalties for vehicular homicide resulting from drunk driving than for vehicular homicide which resulted from reckless driving.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, the statutes did not violate equal protection because the conduct they punished were not identical and based on a real and reasonably related to a legitimate governmental objective.

People v. Maass


No. 96CA1070


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


981 P.2d 177; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 276; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 5733



November 13, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied December 10, 1998. Certiorari Petition Denied July 26, 1999. Released for Publication August 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Elbert County. Honorable Scott W. Lawrence, Judge. No. 95CR5.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Elbert County (Colorado) convicting him of first degree premeditated murder, first degree felony murder, conspiracy to commit first degree premeditated murder, conspiracy to commit first degree felony murder, and second degree kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a drug dealer, learned that the victim had become a police informant. After doing drugs with defendant, the victim left in defendant's car. The victim's body was later found, and she had been shot in the head. Defendant and codefendant were scheduled for trial together. They filed motions to sever their trials that were denied. Defendant's request that he and codefendant be granted the same number of peremptory challenges as the prosecutor was denied. After the jury was selected, but before evidence was presented, a severance was granted. Defendant claimed he was entitled to a new jury after the severance. The appellate court disagreed. Under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-10-104(1), defendant and codefendant were required to share peremptory challenges. After severance, a new jury need not be selected. Failure to grant a discretionary severance prior to jury selection was not improper, because the defenses asserted by defendant and codefendant were not antagonistic. The felony murder and conspiracy to commit felony murder convictions were vacated, because defendant's two conspiracy convictions were based on a single agreement, and thus, he committed only one crime.


OUTCOME: The convictions for first degree premeditated murder, conspiracy to commit first degree premeditated murder, and second degree kidnapping were affirmed. The first degree felony murder and conspiracy to commit felony murder convictions were vacated. The case was remanded.

People v. Loggins


No. 96CA0154


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


981 P.2d 630; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 272; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 5571



October 29, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and As Modified, Petition for Rehearing DENIED December 17, 1998. Certiorari Petition Denied August 16, 1999. Released for Publication August 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Arapahoe County. Honorable Harold Reed, Judge. No. 95CR483.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction of the District Court of Arapahoe County (Colorado), entered on a jury verdict finding him guilty of possession of a controlled substance. Defendant alleged numerous errors by the trial court, including its denial of his challenge for cause to a prospective juror and denial of his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession of a controlled substance after medical personnel treating him found a package containing the substance. Defendant was convicted of the offense and appealed his conviction on numerous grounds. The court affirmed his conviction and found that the actions of the medical personnel had not constituted a search and seizure under the Fourth Amendment or Colo. Const. art. II, § 7, but even if a search had occurred, the medical emergency exception created exigent circumstances, and thus, the denial of defendant's motion to suppress the evidence was still proper. The court held that the evidence did not have to be suppressed because it was delivered at the hospital to an officer outside his jurisdiction at the time, as the officer was from the jurisdiction in which defendant was found and was not pursuing or seeking to arrest defendant, but only followed him to the hospital. The court also found that the state's technical violation of discovery rules was not a sufficient basis for dismissal of the charges against defendant, as the information the state failed to turn over was not exculpatory to defendant, and a continuance was properly granted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of a controlled substance because the challenge for cause was properly denied, as the trial court was persuaded that the prospective juror could be fair and impartial, and there was no search or seizure within the meaning of the Fourth Amendment or the state constitution, so the motion to suppress was properly denied.

Vail Assocs. v. Eagle County Bd. of County Comm'rs


No. 97CA0265


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


983 P.2d 49; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 262; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 5590



October 29, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 27, 1998. Certiorari Granted September 13, 1999. Released for Publication September 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Colorado State Board of Assessment Appeals. No. 31483.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a decision of the Colorado State Board of Assessment, which granted the protest of appellee corporation, and removed the corporation's possessory interest in federally exempt land from the county's tax roll.


OVERVIEW: The corporation had a possessory interest in federal land which it used under non-exclusive special use permits. The county sent a notice of valuation for tax purposes to the corporation assessing the corporation's possessory interest. The corporation protested the county's attempt to assess taxes against it, and sought removal of its possessory interest in federally exempt land from the county's tax roll. The Colorado State Board of Assessment granted the corporation's protest and request for removal from the tax roll. The county appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 39-3-136, possessory interests in exempt property would be subject to property taxation only upon enactment of specific statutory provisions directing such taxation, and that the provisions of Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 39-1-102(14)(a), 39-1-102(14)(c) and 39-1-106 did not direct the taxation of possessory interests in real property. Finally, the court held that under the Supremacy Clause, U.S. Const. art. VI, federally owned lands were not subject to taxation by a state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the corporation.

People v. Webster


No. 97CA0872


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


987 P.2d 836; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 252; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 5371



October 15, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and As Modified, Petitions for Rehearing DENIED December 10, 1998.
Petition for Rehearing Denied December 10, 1998. Cert Petition Denied November 8, 1999. Released for Publication November 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Warren O. Martin, Judge. No. 96CR4812.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, SENTENCE REVERSED, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction rendered in the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), of attempted first degree murder and first degree assault. The defendant contended that the trial court's rulings on the evidence were improper, that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction, and that his sentence was illegal.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was convicted of shooting the victim. The court held that the trial court properly denied the defendant's motion to suppress because a photo line-up was not suggestive. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it admitted hearsay testimony of the defendant's gang activities because the evidence was limited to the one statement and it was relevant to the defendant's motive. The court held that the exclusion of a defense witness' hearsay statement was proper because no hearsay exception found in Colo. R. Evid. 803-804 was applicable. The court held that the prosecutor's remarks during closing argument constituted a proper comment on the defendant's characterization of the facts and theory of the case. The court held that the defendant's motion for acquittal was properly denied because the jury could have reasonably inferred that the defendant committed all the elements of the crimes charged. The court held that the imposition of an aggravated range sentence for attempted first degree murder was error because first degree assault was not a lesser included offense of attempted first degree murder.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed and the defendant's sentence was reversed. The case was remanded for resentencing. The trial court was instructed to enter separate sentences on defendant's convictions for attempted first degree murder and first degree assault.

People v. Washington

October 15, 1998, Decided

Released For Publication January 19, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Larry J. Naves, Judge. No. 91CR1986.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the City and County of Denver convicted defendant of distribution of a controlled substance in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-105 (1973) and sentenced defendant to four years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion seeking to set aside, for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, his prior conviction entered on a guilty plea. Defendant argued that the statute defining the crime was unconstitutional at the time of his defense because it lacked the enacting clause required by Colo. Const. Art. V, § 18. The court determined that the enacting clause as published in the Session Laws of Colorado satisfied the mandate of § 18 and its underlying policy. Consequently, the omission of the enacting clause from the Colorado Revised Statutes did not renter the statutes unconstitutional. Therefore, there was no constitutional deficiency in defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for distribution of a controlled substance.

McInerney v. Public Emples. Retirement Ass'n


No. 97CA0280


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


976 P.2d 348; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 245; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 5123



October 1, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended November 5, 1998. Rehearing Denied November 5, 1998. Released for Publication May 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Federico C. Alvarez, Judge. No. 95CV3198.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee challenged a judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which dismissed under Colo. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(5) his claims against defendant, Public Employees' Retirement Association (PERA) in his 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against PERA and associated defendants alleging that statutory amendments to the PERA benefit plan violated his procedural due process rights because he received insufficient notice.


OVERVIEW: After statutory amendments to the PERA benefit plan were enacted and took effect, the employee sought a declaration that the amendments were unconstitutional as violative of procedural due process and an award of damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. He also requested a mandatory injunction requiring that PERA sell him the necessary years of service credit and qualify him for full PERA retirement benefits, while he maintained his full-time employment. The court affirmed the dismissal under Colo. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(5) of the employee's action against PERA, holding that because the challenged legislation was of general applicability and merely changed statutory benefit levels, the failure to provide notice and an opportunity to avoid the change did not violate plaintiff's right to procedural due process. The legislative change having been validly enacted, the employee was provided all the process he was constitutionally due.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the employee's substantive due process claim against PERA.

People ex rel. Orange County v. M.A.S.


No. 97CA1556


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


962 P.2d 339; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 198; 98 Colo. J. C.A.R. 4244



August 6, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released For Publication September 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Larimer County. Honorable James H. Hiatt, Judge. No. 93DR1486.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant man sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Larimer County (Colorado), which was in favor of appellee woman in a paternity case.


OVERVIEW: The man appealed from the judgment of the trial court that determined that he was the natural father of the child and awarded child support. The man claimed that the necessary parties were not joined in the action. The court held that the child was not then an indispensable party because changes in procedural law were immediately applicable to existing causes of action. The court also held that the man waived any right he had to require that notice be given to the other presumed fathers, and therefore he could not complain of that asserted procedural deficiency on appeal. Further, the court also held that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-4-107(1)(b) did not require that another man's paternity, presumed for reasons other than marriage or attempted marriage, must be negated before an action to assert a parent and child legal relationship by another man can be commenced. Thus, the presumption of the paternity of the other presumed fathers was rebutted by clear and convincing evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the woman.

People v. Bielecki


No. 97CA0400


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


964 P.2d 598; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 194; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 4237



August 6, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 22, 1998. Released For Publication May 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Arapahoe County. Honorable Michael J. Watanabe, Judge. No. 95CR1536.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled not guilty by reason of insanity and impaired mental condition. The jury found defendant guilty of first degree burglary, second degree burglary, and third degree assault. The District Court of Arapahoe County (Colorado) entered judgment upon the jury verdict and sentenced defendant as a habitual criminal to concurrent terms of 48 years on the burglary counts and 2 years on the assault count. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that (1) the retroactive application of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-8-104.5, which required a single trial on sanity and guilt, and, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 1608-105.5, which set forth the required procedures after acceptance of a plea of not guilty by reason of insanity, did not violate constitutional proscriptions against ex post facto laws provided in U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and Colo. Const. art. II, § 11; (2) § 16-8-104.5 did not violate defendant's constitutional rights against self-incrimination, his rights to due process and a fair trial, and his federal and state constitutional rights to the effective assistance of counsel; (3) although the trial court erred by instructing the jury that if defendant was found guilty on any offense he could not be found not guilty by reason of insanity on any other offense, this error did not require reversal because it was invited by defendant; (4) the trial court properly admitted evidence of defendant's prior convictions in defendant's habitual offender adjudication; and (5) the second degree burglary and third degree assault were lesser included offenses of first degree burglary and merged into the first degree burglary conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed as to the convictions for second degree burglary and third degree assault, and the cause was remanded to the trial court with directions to enter a corrected mittimus vacating defendant's convictions and sentences on those counts. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

 

1431 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. High-Tech Inst., Inc.


No. 97CA0385


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


972 P.2d 1060; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 176; 77 A.L.R.5th 755



July 9, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and As Modified. Rehearing Denied August 6, 1998. Released for Publication March 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Nancy E. Rice, Judge. No. 95CV3998.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant medical student sought review of an order from the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which, in an action for invasion of privacy premised on a theory of intrusion upon seclusion and for public disclosure of private facts, dismissed the claim under Colo. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(5).


OVERVIEW: While attending appellee medical school as a student, the student confided in a professor that he had tested positive for HIV. Later, during a mandatory blood test of all students for rubella, the professor requested an HIV test for the student, but not for anyone else. Pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 25-4-1402 (1997), the laboratory was required to report the student's name, address, and positive HIV status to the state department of health, and also informed the medical school of the test results. On review of the dismissal of the student's complaint, the court found that the two causes of action were distinct and separate causes from each other. The court found that the state recognized a cause of action for invasion of privacy based upon an unreasonable disclosure of private facts. The court held that a person had a privacy interest in his or her blood sample and in the medical information obtained from it, and an additional unauthorized test was sufficient to state a claim for relief for intrusion upon conclusion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order dismissing the student's complaint because the student sufficiently stated a claim for invasion of privacy.

 

1432 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Lot Thirty-Four Venture, L.L.C. v. Town of Telluride


No. 96CA2158


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


976 P.2d 303; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 153; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 3013



June 11, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 23, 1998. Released for Publication May 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of San Miguel County. Honorable Robert A. Brown, Judge. No. 94CV37.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation appealed from a decision of the District Court of San Miguel County (Colorado), which granted summary judgment on two of the corporation's claims against defendant city and dismissed three additional claims. The corporation's claims arose from the city's enactment of an ordinance that added affordable housing mitigation requirements for new developments within several zoning districts.


OVERVIEW: The city adopted an ordinance that amended the city's land use code. The city then enacted a second ordinance that added affordable housing mitigation requirements for new developments within several zoning districts. The corporation was the successor to entitlement agreements that previously defined its predecessor's obligations to provide affordable housing. The corporation contended that the predecessor's agreements satisfied all of the affordable housing requirements for its lots. The court reversed and remanded the summary judgment and dismissal of the corporation's action. The city's first ordinance was not invalid for failure to strictly comply with its land use code. The city substantially complied with the code and that was all that was required. The second ordinance violated Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-12-301 because the restrictions operated to reduce the number of options available to the corporation in the use of its property from its previous agreements. Thus, the ordinance was a rent control measure and violated the statute. The trial court erred in dismissing the corporation's claims for declaratory relief because there was a justiciable controversy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the summary judgment and dismissal of the corporation's claims against the city in connection with a city ordinance that added affordable housing mitigation requirements for new developments within several zoning districts.

 

1433 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Gallegos v. City of Monte Vista


No. 97CA0532


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


976 P.2d 299; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 145; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 2725



May 28, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 2, 1998. Released for Publication May 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Rio Grande County. Honorable O. John Kuenhold, Judge. No. 96CV10.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver appealed the order of the District Court of Rio Grande County (Colorado), which granted defendant city's motion to dismiss the driver's complaint alleging negligence in failing to take precautions against his suicide while in jail and a negligent disclosure of medical information. The trial court found that the one-year statute of limitations under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-80-103(c) barred the driver's claims.


OVERVIEW: The driver's complaint against the city alleged that the arresting officer was negligent in refusing to take precautions in the jail for the driver's health and safety and alleged a negligent disclosure of medical information. The city argued that the driver's claims were barred by the one-year statute of limitations of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-80-103(1)(c) (1997), which addressed actions against police officers, whereas the driver contended that the trial court erred in determining that his complaint against the city was barred by that limitation period. The court reversed because it found that the driver's allegations constituted claims against the city for the negligent operation of a jail. The court held that the doctrine of respondeat superior did not entitle the city to assert the procedural bar of a statute of limitations specifically applicable only to police officers and law enforcement personnel to prevent the maintenance of a claim against the city under a two-year statute of limitations. In this tort action, the court ruled, the doctrine of respondeat superior imputed only the negligent acts of the employee to the employer, not the shorter limitations period.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the cause to the trial court.

Kinder v. Industrial Claim Appeals Office


No. 97CA1762


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


976 P.2d 295; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 141; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 2729



May 28, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 2, 1998. Released for Publication May 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 4-270-378.



DISPOSITION: ORDER SET ASIDE AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner student appealed a decision from respondent Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado (appeals panel), which set aside an award of medical impairment benefits finding that the student did not fall within the provisions of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-40-202(1)(a)(IV) (1997).


OVERVIEW: While attending college, the student was working as an unpaid intern with the sponsoring employer. The student was injured at work and sustained permanent medical impairment of 12 percent. The college provided the student workers' compensation benefits, but denied liability for medical impairment benefits. The appeals panel set aside an award of medical benefits finding that the student did not fall within the provisions of § 8-40-202(1)(a)(IV). On appeal, the court set aside the decision and remanded with instructions to reinstate the order awarding the student medical impairment benefits. The court found that unpaid student interns fell within the provisions of § 8-40-202(1)(a)(IV) because Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-40-302(7)(a), which allocated liability for workers' compensation insurance, did not limit the types of benefits a student intern could receive. The phrase "except as provided by § 8-40-302(7)(a)" in § 8-40-202(a)(IV) created an exception to the presumption that the sponsoring school was the employer of a person receiving training in a program sponsored by a college. It did not purport to preclude a student intern from receiving medical impairment benefits.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the decision denying the student medical impairment benefits and reinstated the order awarding the student medical impairment benefits.
