Kilbourn v. Fire & Police Pension Ass'n


No. 97CA0308


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


971 P.2d 284; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 160; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 2720



May 28, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing June 25, 1998. As Amended October 8, 1998. Released for Publication February 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Arapahoe County. Honorable James F. Macrum, Judge. No. 95CV2036.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Arapahoe County (Colorado), which upheld the discontinuation of his occupational disability pension by defendant, the Fire and Police Pension Association, as affirmed by the association's board of directors.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was formerly employed as a city police officer and was awarded an occupational disability pension. The claimant's occupational disability ceased to exist when he resumed full-time employment in a position having duties directly involved with police protection. Consequently, the association discontinued the occupational disability pension. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the amended Colo. Rev. Stat. § 31-31-806 (1997) provided an alternative remedy for determining a claimant's continuing eligibility for occupational disability benefits. Because § 31-31-806 was remedial in nature, its retroactive application was permissible. The court found no evidence that the legislature sought permanently to extend occupational disability benefits to claimants employed in positions having duties directly involved with the provision of police protection. To the contrary, the legislature intended to revoke occupational disability benefits to claimants who returned to employment in such positions. Additionally, the claimant knew that his continued eligibility for benefits was contingent upon his incapacity to perform the duties of a police officer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the association.

Colonial Bank v. Colorado Fin. Servs. Bd.


No. 97CA0436


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


961 P.2d 579; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 126; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 2353



May 14, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 18, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Connie L. Peterson, Judge. No. 95CV5663.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant banks sought review from an order of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which affirmed a decision of the Colorado Financial Services Board (board) to approve an application of appellee credit union to amend its bylaws and add a community field of membership to its existing employment-based field of membership. The banks asserted that the board exceeded its authority and abused its discretion.


OVERVIEW: The credit union served employees of a certain corporation and affiliate companies. The credit union subsequently filed an application with the board requesting approval of an amendment to its bylaws to add a community field of membership to its existing employment-based field of membership. The proposed membership would comprise persons living in a certain metropolitan area of a city. The banks filed written protests opposing the application. The board granted the application, which was affirmed by the district court. On appeal, the court also affirmed judgment and held that: (1) the board's decision to permit the combination proposed by the credit union was based on a permissible construction of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 11-30-103(2); (2) the board did not abuse its discretion when it approved a community field of membership in excess of the limitation in § 11-30-103(2); (3) the board's determination that the credit union's application was politically, geographically, socially, or economically well-defined, as required in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 11-30-101.7(5)(c), was supported by substantial evidence and would not be disturbed on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment of the district court, which affirmed an order of the board granting the credit union's application to amend its bylaws to expand its existing employment-based field of membership.

Diamond Shamrock Ref. & Mktg. Co. v. Colorado Dep't of Labor & Empl.


No. 96CA1382


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


976 P.2d 286; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 131; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 2375



May 14, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 11, 1998. Released for Publication May 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Richard T. Spriggs, Judge. No. 95CV2882.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Colorado Department of Labor and Employment and Petroleum Storage Tank Committee, sought review from an order of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which entered judgment invalidating 6 Colo. Code Regs. § 1007-5 (Regulation 280.80(e) and 280.82(d)), which were promulgated by the department to restrict eligibility of owners of certain storage tanks from seeking reimbursement for clean-up costs.


OVERVIEW: The State of Colorado established an Underground Storage Tank Fund from which owners of underground tanks could seek reimbursement for costs of the cleanup of leakage of petroleum. The appellant Colorado Department of Labor and Employment promulgated 6 Colo. Code Regs. § 1007-5 (Regulation 280.80(e) and 280.82(d)) to restrict the eligibility of owners of the tanks to seek reimbursement from the fund, by establishing a cut off date. Appellee company sought reimbursement claims for costs associated with the cleanup of petroleum releases from two underground storage tanks, which were denied by appellants, department and the Petroleum Tank Advisory Committee. The district court invalidated the regulations at issue, and the department and committee sought review. The court held that the department was acting within its authority in promulgating Regulation 280-80(c) and 280-82(d), because the Resource Conservation and Recovery Act (act), 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 6991-6991I, charged the department with administering corrective action and cleanup aspects of the state program, and the act also granted the department broad discretionary power to promulgate rules and regulations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment and remanded the case to the district court with directions that it enter judgment in favor of the Colorado Department of Labor and Employment and Petroleum Storage Tank Committee.

United Airlines v. City & County of Denver


No. 97CA0151


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


973 P.2d 647; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 89; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 2132



April 30, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 25, 1998. Released for Publication April 12, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable John N. McMullen, Judge. No. 96CV1195.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff airlines appealed the judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which held that defendant municipality, pursuant to Denver, Colo., Rev. Mun. Code § 53-96(a), had the right to impose use taxes against the airlines. The district court was reviewing the decision of a hearing officer, who had found that the use taxes were constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The municipality imposed a use tax on rotable equipment used by the airlines, pursuant to Denver, Colo., Rev. Mun. Code § 53-92(c). Section 53-92(c) provided that if an out-of-state sales tax or use tax was levied by a municipality, then the airlines were given credit for those taxes, but if the out of state tax was levied by a state, no credit was given. Nonetheless, the municipality adopted a policy of giving credit to taxes levied on rotable equipment that were levied by foreign states. Denver, Colo., Rev. Mun. Code § 53-97(11) exempted from the use tax all payments that would offend state or federal constitutional provisions. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which held that the use tax was constitutional as applied, and the court reversed the imposition of penalties on the airlines. The court ruled that § 53-97(11) required the municipality to credit out of state taxes levied on their equipment because the municipality credited all foreign taxes; Denver, Colo., Rev. Mun. Code § 53-92(c) did not violate the United States Constitution. The court ruled that if the airlines demonstrated good cause for their failure to pay use taxes, they were exempt from penalties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the airlines were liable to the municipality for use taxes on rotable equipment, but the court reversed the trial court's judgment that the airlines were liable for penalties. The case was remanded to the hearing officer for a determination of whether good cause existed for the nonpayment of the use tax.

Colwell v. Mentzer Invs., Inc.


No. 96CA1014


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant company sought review after the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado) entered a judgment after a jury verdict finding it negligent and awarding damages to plaintiff customer. The company contended that the trial court erred by admitting expert testimony regarding the effect that stress could have in causing multiple sclerosis (MS) to become symptomatic and that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-101 (1997) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The customer's car caught fire after the company's predecessor inspected and repaired it. The husband stopped the car in front of their house and the customer and her husband tried to extinguish the fire. The jury awarded economic damages and noneconomic damages. The trial court added prejudgment interest. The court held that the customer's expert testimony satisfied the reliability inquiry of Colo. R. Evid. 702 and had the potential of aiding the jury in resolving the disputed issues. Property Tax Adjustment Specialists v. Mesa County Bd. of Comm'rs

COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer's agent appealed from an order of the Colorado State Board of Assessment Appeals (BAA), upholding a decision of the Mesa County Board of Commissioners (BCC), which denied the taxpayer's petition for an abatement of the taxes it paid on exempt property as barred by the two-year statute of limitations of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 39-10-114(1)(a)(I)(A).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a mutual ditch company providing irrigation and electrical service and, as a result of its operations, its property was exempt from separate taxation under Colo. Const. art. X, § 3(1)(d). In 1982, the Department of Property Taxation began assessing the taxpayer as an electric utility. The taxpayer paid the assessed tax until 1995 when it protested the tax and asserted its exempt status. The taxpayer filed a petition for an abatement of taxes paid prior to 1995. X, § 20, which provided a four-year period for recovery of taxes, because the taxpayer's claim arose from an error in classifying its property and not from a violation of the constitutional provision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the BAA upholding the denial of the taxpayer's petition for an abatement of taxes.

Young v. Industrial Claim Appeals Office


No. 97CA1165


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


969 P.2d 735; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 82; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1880



April 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 14, 1998.
Released For Publication January 19, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 4276722.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a workers' compensation proceeding, petitioner claimant sought review of an order of respondent, the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado (panel), which excluded per diem payments in the calculation of his average weekly wage.


OVERVIEW: The claimant argued that the exclusion of the per diem payments in the calculation of his average weekly wage as mandated by Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 8-40-201(19)(c), 8-42-102(2) (1997) violated the guarantee of equal protection. The court disagreed that the exclusion of per diem payments created an arbitrary distinction, which depended only upon the label used for such payments and, therefore, rejected the claim that the exclusion was unconstitutional. The claimant's testimony that the per diem payments were for reimbursement and that his taxable income equaled his "mileage minus the per diem" supported only the conclusion that the per diem payments did not exceed his actual expenses and, therefore, provided no economic benefit. Such reimbursable expenses were the type of costs incurred when an employee's job required travel. The exclusion of per diem payments did not result in the disparate calculation of wages, but rather, served to differentiate between payments intended to reimburse the employee for expenses incurred as a result of his employment and those meant to provide economic advantage. The court held that there was no violation of equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the panel, which excluded per diem payments in the calculation of the claimant's weekly wage.

Manor Vail Condo. Ass'n v. Bd. of Equalization


No. 96CA2132


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


956 P.2d 654; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 57; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1323



March 19, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 12, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Eagle County. Honorable William L. Jones, Judge. No. 95CV290.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer, a condominium association, sought review of the summary judgment granted by the District Court of Eagle County (Colorado), for appellee tax assessor, in taxpayer's challenge of the assessment of taxpayer's condominium units for the tax year 1995 that included the value of certain commercial improvements, consisting of each unit's proportionate share of the actual value assessed at the non-residential ratio of 29 percent.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court rejected taxpayer's contention that the restaurant and meeting rooms were erroneously classified as non-residential improvements taxable at a ratio of 29 percent, rather than as residential improvements which were taxable at the lower ratio of 10.36 percent, because the tax assessor's interpretation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-33.3-105(2) (1997) was more consistent with the overall legislative scheme that portions of a single building may have multiple uses and were to be apportioned and classified according to those respective uses. The restaurant and meeting rooms were open to and used by the general public and taxpayer, and their unprofitability was not a factor. The tax assessor complied with § 38-33.3-105(2), which required that the valuation of the common elements be assessed proportionately to each unit, because tax assessor did not carry the non-residential common elements as separately scheduled properties, nor did it issue separate notices of valuation or tax bills on the non-residential common elements. Because tax assessor did not tax the non-residential common elements separately, there was no breach of the earlier stipulation between the parties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Waddell v. Industrial Claim Appeals Office


No. 97CA0611


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


964 P.2d 552; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 10; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 353



January 22, 1998, Decided

Released For Publication October 20, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC Nos. 3-104-212 & 3-106-336.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant sought review of an order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado (panel) granting the claim of respondents employer and insurer for apportionment of liability in a workers' compensation proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was injured while working for the employer. The claimant had sustained previous injuries while serving in the United States armed services and one other injury while working for the employer. As a result of the combination of the injuries, it was determined that the claimant was permanently and totally disabled. Because the military injuries were non-industrial, the claimant's request for offset to respondent Subsequent Injury Fund (SIF) was denied, and the liability for disability compensation was distributed among the employer and the insurer. Thereafter, the panel granted the employer and the insurer's claim for apportionment of liability, and the claimant appealed the decision. As to claimant's argument regarding SIF, the court agreed with the panel's holding and held that it was bound by the precedential ruling regarding the scope of SIF's liability. Accordingly, because there was no SIF liability, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-42-104(2), apportioning damages, was properly applied. Finally, the court held that the claimant did not suffer disparate treatment by the application of the statute. The decision of the panel was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The panel's order apportioning disability compensation liability among the employer and the insured in a workers' compensation proceeding was affirmed.

People v. Gallegos


No. 96CA1093


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


975 P.2d 1135; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 13; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 351



January 22, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 2, 1998. Released for Publication May 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable R. Michael Mullins, Judge. Nos. 83CR2431 & 83CR2450.



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from an order of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which determined that the Department of Corrections' (DOC) application of the parole statutes to defendant violated the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was serving a cumulative 21-year sentence when he was granted a discretionary parole. He filed a post-conviction motion for a ruling that his sentence had been fully served. Before the motion was heard, defendant absconded. He was later captured, his parole was revoked, and he was ordered to serve the remainder of his 21-year sentence in prison. A hearing on the motion was ultimately held. The trial court did not find that defendant's sentence had been fully served, but it did find that a statute governing reincarceration after the revocation of discretionary parole had been applied to defendant in violation of the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws. The court reversed and remanded. The court found that defendant had "fair warning" of the reincarceration statute and that there was no ex post facto violation. The court also found that the statute under which defendant was paroled, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-22.5-303, authorized a reincarceration period of not more than five years. Because defendant was ordered to serve a sentence in excess of that, the court directed the trial court on remand to order that the reincarceration period be recalculated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order finding that the DOC's application of the parole statutes to defendant violated the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws, and it remanded to the trial court to recalculate defendant's reincarceration period.

Buckles v. Colo. Div. of Wildlife


No. 96CA2270


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


952 P.2d 855; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 5; 1998 Colo. J. C.A.R. 76



January 8, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Rio Blanco County. Honorable J. E. DeVilbiss, Judge. No. 94CV8.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED IN PART, AND JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed judgments from the District Court of Rio Blanco County (Colorado), which dismissed their claims of trespass, violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and inverse condemnation against defendants, State of Colorado, the Colorado Division of Wildlife, and the Board of Commissioners of the Colorado Division of Wildlife.


OVERVIEW: The landowners' claims were dismissed in two separate orders. The first order disposed of the trespass claim based on sovereign immunity under the Governmental Immunity Act. In dismissing the appeal as to this issue, the court held that the appeal was untimely. The court explained that although the order was interlocutory in nature, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-10-108 (1997) provided that a court's decision on a motion asserting sovereign immunity was a final judgment which was subject to interlocutory appeal. This right of appeal was subject to the time constraints of Colo. App. R. 4(a), and because the landowners had not met the deadline, the appeal was barred. The court affirmed the second order because the landowners' argument was based on a theory not raised in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal as to the dismissal of landowners' trespass claim against the state officials and entities and affirmed the judgment against the landowners on their inverse condemnation and civil rights claims.

 

1446 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. E.I.C.


No. 96CA1707


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


958 P.2d 511; 1998 Colo. App. LEXIS 3; 98 Colo. J. C.A.R. 74



January 8, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 19, 1998. Released for Publication July 21, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Juvenile Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Patti F. O'Rourke, Judge. No. 93JN43.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed from the Juvenile Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado) judgment terminating his parent-child legal relationship with his two minor children. He argued the relevant statutes were unconstitutional and that there was insufficient evidence to support termination.


OVERVIEW: The children were adjudicated dependent and neglected at 9 and 8 years old, respectively. The father had previously been convicted of several crimes, including first degree murder, and was serving two consecutive life sentences plus 144 years. At the time of the termination of his parental rights, the probabilities were substantial that he would never be available to assume a normal life with the children. Attempts made to place the children with family members of the father or the mother had failed. The father contended that the statutes under which his parental rights were terminated were unconstitutional for several reasons. The court rejected the arguments. He also argued there was insufficient evidence to support the termination. The court disagreed and affirmed the termination. The trial court properly took judicial notice of both the length of his sentences and the date the crimes were committed. There was clear and convincing evidence that no treatment plan could be devised to resolve his unfitness under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-3-604. The termination was a decision of last resort.


OUTCOME: The judgment terminating the father's rights was affirmed. There was no constitutional violation. There was clear and convincing evidence that no appropriate treatment plan could be devised to address the father's unfitness resulting from his incarceration for two consecutive life sentences plus 144 years. The record supported the conclusion that the trial court's termination of father's parental rights was a decision of last resort.

 

1447 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Carlson v. Industrial Claim Appeals Office, Dep't of Labor & Employ., Div. of Workers' Compensation


No. 96CA2199


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


950 P.2d 663; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 227; 1997 Colo. J. C.A.R. 2328



October 16, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Amended October 23, 1997. Petition for Rehearing Denied December 26, 1997, Released for Publication February 18, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. U.R. No. 95-37.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner medical provider sought review of an order from respondent Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado (panel), which affirmed an order of the Administrative Law Judge (ALJ), who changed the medical provider for claimant employee based upon the recommendation of a medical utilization review (MUR) committee.


OVERVIEW: An employee suffered a work-related injury and began treatment with the medical provider. The MUR panel agreed that the medical provider's care was not reasonably necessary to cure the employee, and the division of labor director ordered a change of physicians. On the medical provider's appeal, the ALJ concluded that the medical provider failed to overcome he director's order, and the panel affirmed. On further appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the panel. The court held that the medical provider had standing to challenge the panel's orders because he had standing to appeal the ALJ's order pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-43-501(5)(a) (1997). The court found that it necessarily followed that the medical provider had standing to seek further review of the ALJ's order. However, that statute was not unconstitutional nor did it deprive the medical provider of any liberty interests. The possibility of future harm to prospective employment was too intangible to be a constitutional deprivation of a protected liberty interest. The medical provider did not possess a statutory right to treat any claimant for his work-related injury or to continue to provide further treatment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the panel's order, which affirmed the MUR committee's recommendation to change the employee's physician.

 

1448 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Pena


No. 96CA0902


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


962 P.2d 285; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 220; 97 Colo. J. C.A.R. 2113



October 2, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable Jane Looney, Judge. No. 95CR1698.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado) that convicted him of vehicular eluding. Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence, contended that his conviction was in violation of his equal protection rights, and urged that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury on reckless driving as a lesser-included offense.


OVERVIEW: An arresting police officer testified at trial that he saw a car travel toward him at a high rate of speed, swerving across the center line as it passed his cruiser. According to the officer, when he activated his light and siren, the other car appeared to accelerate. Defendant was identified as the driver of the car. The passengers of the car testified at trial that they had not seen the police officer in pursuit. They also said that defendant had been trying to elude his girlfriend, rather than the police. The jury found defendant guilty of vehicular eluding. In reversing and remanding, the court agreed with defendant's contention that he was entitled to a new trial because the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury that reckless driving was a lesser-included offense of vehicular eluding. However, the court concluded that there was sufficient evidence to convince a rational juror beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant knew the police officer was pursuing him and that he knowingly attempted to elude the officer. Also, the court concluded that defendant's conviction of vehicular eluding did not violate his right to equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded defendant's conviction for vehicular eluding. The court agreed with defendant's contention regarding instructional error.

Stolworthy v. Clark


No. 97CA0255


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


952 P.2d 1198; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 210; 1997 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1999



September 18, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 3105328.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner workers' compensation claimant sought review of a final order from respondent Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado which granted respondents, an employer, its insurer, and the Colorado Subsequent Injury Fund (SIF), an offset for social security retirement benefits the claimant received.


OVERVIEW: The claimant sustained an industrial injury. The parties agreed that the claimant was permanently and totally disabled. The parties stipulated that claimant became eligible for social security retirement benefits a few months before the industrial injury and began receiving those benefits a few months later. The claimant's wife began receiving social security retirement benefits two years later, based on her husband's earnings. However, the claimant's application for social security disability benefits was disapproved because he did not meet the earnings requirement on or after the date he became disabled. The Administrative Law Judge disagreed and determined that the insurer and SIP could take an offset pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-42-103(1)(c)(II) (1997) based on claimant's and his wife's receipt of social security retirement benefits. The Panel affirmed the offset. Affirming, the court held that the claimant's failure to qualify for social security disability benefits affects only the provision limiting the amount of the offset, not the applicability of the offset itself.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

1450 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


BCW Enters., Ltd. v. Industrial Claim Appeals Office


No. 96CA1033


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


964 P.2d 533; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 215; 97 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1987



September 18, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 30, 1997.
Released For Publication October 20, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of the Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 4155609.



DISPOSITION: ORDER SET ASIDE AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, employer and its insurer, appealed the final order of respondent, the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado (panel), which in a workers' compensation proceeding upheld the denial of their request for penalties against counsel for respondent claimant. The insurer argued that fees were appropriate under Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 8-43-301(2), 8-43-211(2)(d) (1997).


OVERVIEW: While an appeal of a panel order denying claimant the right to change doctor's was pending, claimant applied for a hearing for penalties against the insurer for delaying medical care and the adjudication of her claim. The administrative law judge granted the insurer's motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court set aside the panel's decision denying the insurer's motion for fees. The order denying penalties was an appealable order. While the term "claimant" did not include an employer or its insurer, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-43-301(2) (1997) did not prohibit review of an order denying to them the recovery of a penalty. Such order was interlocutory, permitting appellate review, pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-43-307(1) (1997). Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-43-301(2) (1997) did not violate due process or equal protection rights by treating employers and insurers dissimilarly from employees because it furthered rational and legitimate state interests. The insurer could claim fees under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-43-211(2)(d)(1997). The issue of whether a bad faith appeal had been filed and the appropriate penalty was not ripe for determination until the appeal was ultimately resolved.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the lower court's order and remanded the cause for a determination of the attorney fees and costs to be awarded as a penalty.

People v. Fears


No. 93CA0720


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


962 P.2d 272; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 195; 97 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1470



August 7, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 18, 1997.
Released For Publication September 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Warren O. Martin, Judge. Honorable Robert P. Fullerton, Judge. Honorable William G. Meyer, Judge. No. 89CR2938.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the District Court, Denver County (Colorado) that rendered judgment on a jury verdict convicting him on two counts of first degree murder and denied his motion to dismiss the charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's jury trial on a capital crime was delayed for approximately 2 years due to a finding that the death penalty was unconstitutional and a subsequent appeal of that decision. After a final decision on the death penalty, defendant was tried, convicted, and sentenced to life imprisonment. Defendant contended that the lower court erred in denying his motion to dismiss the charges because of a violation of his statutory right to a speedy trial pursuant to Col. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-405 (1986). The court held that the statutory speedy trial period was tolled because the Colorado supreme court ultimately accepted jurisdiction to review the death penalty ruling. The court also held that the length of delay caused by an appeal of the death penalty ruling did not violate defendant's constitutional right to a speedy trial because the appeal was in good faith, even though the unconstitutionality of the death penalty was sustained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

Tepley v. Public Emples. Retirement Ass'n


No. 96CA1305


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


955 P.2d 573; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 187; 1997 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1480



August 7, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 23, 1997. Released for Publication June 16, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Larry J. Naves, Judge. No. 95CV4547.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant challenged the judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado) that dismissed his claim for disability retirement benefits under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and 42 U.S.C.S. § 12132 of the Americans with Disabilities Act (ADA) against defendant Public Employees' Retirement Association (PERA). The applicant also appealed the trial court's summary judgment in favor of PERA on his claim for a declaratory holding.


OVERVIEW: The applicant sought an injunction requiring PERA's Board of Trustees (board) to review his application for disability benefits pursuant to a procedurally proper process. The court held that: (1) The trustees' fiduciary duties to PERA members did not prevent them from performing quasi-judicial functions in determining a member's eligibility for disability benefits. The board's rules were not ultra vires, and the district court did not err in reviewing the board's decision pursuant to Colo. R. Civ. P. 106(a)(4); (2) The board used improper procedures that violated the applicant's right to procedural due process when it reviewed his application for disability benefits. It was improper for the board to consider arguments from the panel members as to how and why they had reached their decision; (3) The applicant proved no facts in support of his ADA claim to entitle him to relief thereon; (4) The applicant adequately stated a claim for injunctive relief under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 to compel the board to review his application pursuant to a process free from the procedural due process problems; and (5) The applicant's § 1983 claim was not barred because it sought damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the applicant's ADA claim and his claim for de novo review. The dismissal of the applicant's claim for injunctive relief and the trial court's determination that PERA had not abused its discretion were reversed. The cause was remanded for further proceedings with the instruction that discovery was to be permitted if relevant to demonstrate improper policies of PERA in addition to the due process violations.

People v. Vialpando


No. 94CA1068


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


954 P.2d 617; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 186; 1997 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1476



August 7, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 9, 1997. Released for Publication May 12, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Herbert L. Stern, III, Judge. No. 87CR2141.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which convicted him of first degree murder, robbery, escape, possession of contraband, and being a habitual criminal, on the grounds that the trial court erred in denying his request to represent himself and in admitting evidence of his silence in mental exams and of his prior bad acts and he was deprived of his right of access to the court.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's request to represent himself five days before trial and 18 months after counsel was appointed because the request was designed to disrupt the proceedings and would have resulted in delay. The court determined that defendant's access to legal counsel satisfied his Sixth Amendment right to access legal resources. The court found that defendant did not have standing to challenge statutory waiver of the confidentiality of mental status examinations. Any injury was speculative because defendant did not retain a defense psychiatrist. The court held that a psychiatrist's comment on defendant's silence during a mental status examination was relevant, admissible evidence. The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in permitting other acts evidence to be introduced to show defendant's history of escape attempts and his willingness to use force against law enforcement officers. The court also concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in determining that changed circumstances did not require it to follow its previous decision to sever the escape charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Reali


No. 96CA0806


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


950 P.2d 645; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 185; 1997 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1494



August 7, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied February 2, 1998. Released for Publication February 18, 1998.
Writ of certiorari denied Reali v. People, 1998 Colo. LEXIS 147 (Colo., Feb. 2, 1998)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Reali v. Abbot, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 3701 (10th Cir. Colo., Feb. 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable Jane Looney, Judge. No. 90CR2387.
Reali v. People, 1995 Colo. LEXIS 363 (Colo., May 8, 1995)



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado), which denied defendant's Colo. R. Crim. P. 35 motion for postconviction relief. In seeking review, defendant claimed that the trial court had erred in not granting a hearing on the motion and that Colorado's use immunity statute, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-90-118 (1987), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: As part of defendant's agreement to cooperate in the murder prosecution of the co-conspirator, defendant testified before a grand jury and at the co-conspirator's trial pursuant to a grant of use immunity for defendant's testimony. Thereafter, the same prosecutors who presented defendant's testimony against the co-conspirator presented the state's case against defendant. Following defendant's murder conviction and its affirmance on appeal, defendant moved for postconviction relief pursuant to Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c). When the trial court denied the motion without hearing, defendant sought review, claiming that the trial court had erred in not granting a hearing and that Colorado's use immunity statute, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-90-118 (1987), was unconstitutional. In affirming, the court held a hearing had not been required because the trial court had conducted the functional equivalent of such a hearing before trial, and thus, another hearing would have been unnecessarily duplicative. The court also held § 13-90-118 had not violated defendant's Fifth Amendment rights because the prosecutors' mere knowledge of defendant's immunized testimony had not prejudiced defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order denying defendant's motion for post conviction relief and rejected defendant's claims that the trial court had erred in not granting a hearing on the motion and that Colorado's use immunity statute was unconstitutional.

Walker v. Jim Fuoco Motor Co.


No. 96CA1594


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


942 P.2d 1390; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 175; 1997 Colo. J. C.A.R. 1220



July 24, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado WC No. 4-238-397.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee appealed a decision of respondent Industrial Claim Appeals Office, as affirmed by an administrative law judge, which awarded him permanent partial disability benefits based upon a scheduled impairment under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-42-107(2)(a) (Cum. Supp. 1996), rather than a whole person impairment under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-42-107(8) (Cum. Supp. 1996).


OVERVIEW: The employee sustained a shoulder and arm injury. The administrative law judge awarded permanent partial disability benefits based on a scheduled impairment. The employee contended that the injury was a whole person injury because the American Medical Association (AMA) in its guides considered the shoulder to be a part of the trunk of the body. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the AMA guides were not controlling. The court held that the treating physicians found no impairment beyond the shoulder and that, as a result, there was substantial evidence to support the administrative law judge's finding that the employee sustained a functional impairment listed on the schedule of disabilities. The court also held that the term "loss of use" in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-42-107(7)(b) (Cum. Supp. 1996), was not unconstitutionally vague because it was sufficiently precise to permit persons of common intelligence to understand its meaning.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the administrative law judge, which awarded the employee permanent partial disability benefits based upon a scheduled impairment rather than a whole person impairment.

In re Catholic Charities & Community Servs.


No. 96CA0835


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


942 P.2d 1380; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 172



July 10, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Juvenile Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Dana U. Wakefield, Judge. No. 95JR48.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, father and tribe, sought review of a decision of the Juvenile Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado) terminating the parental relationship between the father and his daughter pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-5-105 (1996 Cum. Supp.) and awarding custody to appellee diocese. Appellants asserted that the court erred in not applying the provisions of the Indian Child Welfare Act to the matter.


OVERVIEW: The trial court terminated the parental relationship between appellant father and his child, pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-5-105 (1996 Cum. Supp.), and placed custody of the child with appellee diocese. Appellant father and appellant tribe asserted that the lower court erred in not applying the provisions of the Indian Child Welfare Act (ICWA) to the matter. The court reversed and remanded the lower court's decision and asked it to make a determination whether appellant father's child was an American Indian and to make findings of fact and conclusions of law as to the applicability of the ICWA. The court rejected appellants' argument that appellant father's right to due process was violated when the court refused to transport him to all of the hearings because he was represented by counsel at those proceedings. Also, the court held that the lower court properly interpreted Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-5-105(3) (1996 Cum. Supp.) to mean that appellant father's inability to attend the proceedings prevented him from promptly taking custody of his daughter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the lower court's decision, finding that it had failed to make a determination whether appellant father's child was an American Indian and to set forth its findings on the applicability of the ICWA. The court found no indication that appellant father's right to due process was violated when the court refused to transport him to all of the proceedings because he appeared at the proceedings through counsel.

People v. Garlotte


No. 95CA0667


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


958 P.2d 469; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 160; 21 Colo. J. 959



July 3, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 7, 1997. As Corrected August 28, 1997. Released for Publication July 21, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Larimer County. Honorable James H. Hiatt, Judge. No. 84CR797.



DISPOSITION: CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Larimer County (Colorado), which revoked his conditional release and ordered his return to the Colorado State Hospital for violations of conditions imposed upon his release from the hospital. He had been committed to the hospital following his having been found not guilty by reason of insanity of the murder of a nurse.


OVERVIEW: The court held that (1) an insanity acquittee's conditional release could be revoked under Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 16-8-115.5 and 16-8-102(4.5) solely because a release condition had been violated, provided that the condition violated bore a substantial relationship to the prevention of recurring mental illness or the management of an insanity acquittee's existing mental illness, and to the prevention of future dangerousness arising from the mental illness; (2) the People had the burden of proving by a preponderance of the evidence that the condition violated was sufficiently related to these goals; (3) whether such burden was met was a factual determination for the committing court based on the totality of the evidence; (4) the People's evidence at defendant's revocation hearing showed a nexus between the conditions requiring that defendant abstain from drugs and alcohol and his ability to remain on conditional release without recurrence of his dangerous symptoms; and (5) remand was necessary because, despite the prosecution's evidence of defendant's mental illness and dangerousness, he did not have a full opportunity to present evidence regarding these issues.


OUTCOME: The cause was remanded with directions.

People v. Thomas


No. 93CA1209


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


962 P.2d 263; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 152; 21 Colo. J. 885



June 26, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and As Modified, Petition for Rehearing DENIED October, 23, 1997.
Rehearing Denied October 23, 1997.
Released For Publication September 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Adams County. Honorable Donald W. Marshall, Jr., Judge. No. 91CR0190.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgments of conviction, which the District Court of Adams County (Colorado) entered on jury verdicts finding him guilty of first degree murder after deliberation, first degree felony murder, first degree sexual assault, second degree burglary, aggravated robbery, and robbery of the elderly.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered the victim. The defense was that it was second degree murder because he was under the influence of drugs. After voir dire, defendant expressed dissatisfaction with this defense. Defendant wanted to receive the death penalty for first degree murder. Defendant chose not to be present at trial after voir dire. Defense counsel chose not to be present for the opening statement and first witness' direct testimony. The court held that defendant was not "deprived" of counsel. There was no reversible error in the denial of a continuance because there was no material prejudice. The prosecution's opening statement did not exceed the bounds of propriety. Defense counsel, upon reappearing, was permitted to respond with an opening statement. The first witness did not address state of mind. Cross-examination was not materially impacted by counsel's absence during direct. Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-8-107(1) (1997) was constitutional as defendant could have protected his privilege against self-incrimination, until he relied upon lack of mental capacity to commit the crimes, by remaining silent at the court-ordered examination and privately retaining a psychiatrist.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction for first degree murder after deliberation, first degree felony murder, first degree sexual assault, second degree burglary, aggravated robbery, and robbery of the elderly.

 

1459 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Hill v. City of Lakewood


No. 94CA0856


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


949 P.2d 107; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 153; 21 Colo. J. 889



June 26, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 24, 1997.
Released For Publication January 21, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Gaspar F. Perricone, Judge. No. No. 93CV1984.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff protestors filed an action against defendants, city and state officials, challenging the constitutional validity of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-9-122 (Cum. Supp. 1996). The court affirmed the district court's judgment in favor of defendants, finding that § 18-9-122 did not violate the First Amendment. The United States Supreme Court granted certiorari and remanded the action to the court for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: The protestors challenged the constitutionality of § 18-9-122, which created a buffer zones around health care facilities. The court affirmed the district court's judgment against the protestors. Thereafter, the supreme court announced a decision, which upheld that part of an injunction that created a fixed buffer zone and struck down that part of the injunction that created a floating buffer zone. In light of that decision, the supreme court remanded the protestors' action to the court for reconsideration. On remand, the court again affirmed the district court's judgment, holding that the supreme court decision did not compel the conclusion that §18-9-122 violated the First Amendment. The court held that § 18-9-122 was a content-neutral, generally applicable statute supported by a valid governmental interest. The governmental interest of ensuring easy access to those with physical disabilities by creating an eight-foot buffer zone within a 100-foot area was amply sufficient to justify § 18-9-122. Moreover, the court noted that alternate channels for communication other than leafleting were available within 100 feet of the entrance to the health care facility.


OUTCOME: On remand, the court affirmed the district court's judgment against the protestors' in their action that challenged the constitutionality of the statute that created fixed and floating buffer zones around health care facilities.

People v. McCoy


No. 96CA0698


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


939 P.2d 537; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 131



May 29, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 26, 1997, Certiorari pending (97SC575).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Arapahoe County. Honorable Michael J. Watanabe, Judge. Honorable Jack F. Smith, Judge. No. 94CR799.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the District Court of Arapahoe County (Colorado). The trial court revoked her sentence to the Youthful Offender System (YOS) and imposed a previously imposed sentence to the Department of Corrections (the Department).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with multiple felonies that she committed while under the age of 18. She pled guilty to a single court of robbery. The trial court imposed a stipulated four-year sentence to the YOS and also imposed and suspended defendant's 14-year sentence to the department of corrections pending her successful completion of the YOS sentence. The state subsequently filed a motion for revocation of the YOS sentence because of rule violations. The trial court granted the motion. The court affirmed. Although defendant was entitled to minimum due process protections at a YOS revocation hearing, she was not entitled to the full range of constitutional protections that an accused received at trial. A YOS revocation hearing required only the protections that were due for probation and parole revocation hearings. The admission of hearsay evidence was permissible, and the prosecution had to prove its burden by a preponderance of the evidence. Defendant was able to cross-examine the witnesses who presented hearsay testimony, and in so doing she admitted three of the violations. The trial court only had authority to impose the entire 14-year sentence that defendant originally received.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that revoked defendant's YOS sentence and imposed the original 14-year sentence to the department of corrections after defendant committed several rule violations.

 

1461 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Luke


No. 95CA1644


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


948 P.2d 87; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 137



May 29, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 26, 1997.
Released for Publication December 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Teller County. Honorable Donald E. Campbell, Judge. No. 95CR37.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with two offenses under the Colorado Limited Gaming Act. Following a preliminary hearing, the District Court of Teller County (Colorado) dismissed all charges. The People appealed that dismissal, and defendant filed a cross-appeal asserting constitutional arguments in support of the trial court order which were made to, but not relied upon by, the trial court.


OVERVIEW: A gaming application prompted an investigation during which the investigator became aware that defendant had become the applicant's chief operating officer. The court held that the trial court had erred in imposing a materiality requirement on Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-47.1-802 (1991) and Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-20-104 (1996) and reversed the dismissal as it related to defendant's representation about his relationship with certain individuals. The court concluded that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-47.1-802 and § 18-20-104 had not prohibited constitutionally protected speech and were not unconstitutionally overbroad. They were not unconstitutionally vague, as they clearly delineated the prohibited conduct. Because the applicant had an application pending for a license to operate a limited gaming establishment, it was not necessary that defendant have an individual key employee application pending or that the applicant be a licensee at the time the alleged false statement was made, or false or misleading information provided. The misrepresentation for the failure to report defendant's involvement as a party defendant in a civil action was properly dismissed for lack of evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing count one as to defendant's failure to report a civil case. The dismissal of the remainder of count one and all of count two was reversed and the cause was remanded.

People v. Thompson


No. 94CA0972


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


950 P.2d 608; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 114



May 8, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied February 2, 1998. Released for Publication February 18, 1998,


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Nancy E. Rice, Judge. No. 93CR2979.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which convicted him of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder for stabbing a drug dealer to death primarily by his wife's testimony. Defendant appealed his conviction contending that the trial court erred in upholding as constitutional the spousal privilege law, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-90-107(1)(a)(II) (1996), and he challenged several of the court's evidentiary rulings. The court affirmed. The court concluded that the trial court properly applied state law, where state statutes provided no directive for resolving choice-of-law issues in the context of spousal privileges. The court found that although the communication occurred in another state, it directly concerned a serious crime allegedly committed by defendant in this state. The court concluded that the wife's testimony was extraordinarily important evidence, and she appeared voluntarily. The court concluded that if confidential marital communications fell within a constitutionally protected zone of privacy, such a zone did not extend so far as to outweigh a state's interest in the voluntary testimony of a spouse about a murder committed by another spouse.


OUTCOME: The trial court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder concluding that the trial court did not err in admitting defendant's wife's testimony about his involvement in the murder where no state statute provided a directive for resolving choice-of-law issues in the context of spousal privileges, and where the wife's testimony was considered extraordinarily important, and she appeared voluntarily.

Fidelity Castle Pines v. State


No. 95CA1951


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


948 P.2d 26; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 79



March 27, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and As Modified Petition for Rehearing Denied July 3, 1997.
Released for Publication December 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Douglas County. Honorable Thomas J. Curry, Judge. No. 93CV324.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, owners of vacant land, sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Eighteenth Judicial District (Colorado) which entered summary judgment in favor of defendants, a county assessor and a county board of equalization, ruling that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 39-1-103(14)(b) (1994), which excluded indirect costs from consideration in determining actual value, was constitutional and that the owners' land was properly assessed.


OVERVIEW: Colo. Const. art. X, § 3(1)(a) required that real and personal property be uniformly assessed for property tax purposes. The owners contended that the failure to make an allowance for indirect costs in the present worth analysis of vacant land resulted in a substantial overstatement of the actual value of their vacant land and that § 39-1-103(14)(b) conflicted with the constitution both facially and as applied to the owners' land. The owners' property was assessed using the market approach and indirect costs were excluded from consideration in determining value. The owners also argued that the trial court erred in ruling that § 39-1-103(14)(b) did not violate Colo. Const. art. X, § 3 by creating a separate class of commercial property and that, by disregarding indirect costs, their land was substantially overvalued, thereby creating an unreasonable classification. The court held that the trial court did not err in upholding the constitutionality of § 39-1-103(14)(b) because all vacant land was valued without consideration of indirect costs. The court concluded that no special classes of land were created by § 39-1-103(14)(b) that violated Colo. Const. art. X, § 3.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1464 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Helmich


No. 95CA1658


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


937 P.2d 897; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 67



March 6, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 10, 1997. Released for Publication June 11, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Robert S. Hyatt, Judge. No. 87DR3113.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which found him in contempt for failure to pay child support and sentenced him to six months in the county jail.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's order stated that the father was not to be released early for any reason. The father argued that the contempt order could not stand because the district attorney was not notified of the proceeding as required under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-1002 (1996). The father also argued that he was entitled to have good time credited to his sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that § 18-1-1002 did not deprive the trial court of jurisdiction, and its noncompliance did not prejudice the father. Section 18-1-1002 was not intended as a protection for defendants in a contempt proceeding, but to provide notice to prosecutors in cases in which contempt proceedings could trigger double jeopardy concerns. The court remanded the case for the trial court to clarify the order so as not to preclude the allowance of good time credit. The court found that the father was entitled to the benefits of good time credits under Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 17-26-109, 17-26-115 (1986) because the trial court was without authority to sentence a defendant to "flat time," and the good time provisions applied to all county prisoners.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that found the father in contempt for failure to pay child support and remanded the cause for the trial court to clarify the order so as not to preclude the allowance of good time credit.

Childers v. Quartz Creek Land Co.


No. 96CA0075


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


946 P.2d 534; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 50; 21 Colo. J. 260



February 20, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, And As Modified, Petition for Rehearing DENIED May 1, 1997. Petition for Rehearing Denied November 10, 1997. Released for Publication November 28, 1997. Certiorari Denied January 19, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 598.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Gunnison County. Honorable David C. Johnston, Judge. No. 94CV22.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant land company sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Gunnison County (Colorado), which granted plaintiff landowner's petition in a private condemnation action brought under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-1-101 et seq. (1982 Repl. Vol. 16A) to provide access to certain landlocked real property. The company argued that the condemnation statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of the district court's judgment granting the landowner's petition for a necessary easement, the company challenged the constitutionality of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-1-102(3), which permitted easements of necessity for any purpose. The company argued that the statute conflicted with the state constitution, Colo. Const. art. II, § 14, which only permitted necessary easements for agricultural, mining, milling, domestic or sanitary purposes. The company also argued that the landowner's petition was barred by the statute of limitations. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the statute was not unconstitutional because the legislature had not intended to limit private easements of necessity in the manner alleged by the company. However, the court remanded the matter with instructions that the judgment be amended by providing that the easement would be terminated in the event alternate access to the landowner's property was subsequently established. The court also held that the landowner's action was not barred by the 18-year statute of limitations because the landowner had a right to bring a condemnation action so long as she held title to the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which granted the landowner's condemnation petition for a necessary easement. The court remanded the matter to the trial court with directions to amend the judgment to provide that the easement would be terminated if and when alternate access to the landowner's property was established.

Wilder v. Board of Educ.


No. 96CA0709


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


944 P.2d 598; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 22



January 23, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 23, 1997.
Rehearing Denied March 27, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of Dismissal of the Board of Education of Jefferson County School District R-1.



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner teacher appealed from the order of dismissal of respondent Board of Education of the Jefferson County School District (Colorado), which terminated his employment as a non-probationary teacher with the district.


OVERVIEW: The teacher asserted that the school board's order dismissing him for showing the film 1900 to his students, in contravention of the hearing officer's recommendation of retention, violated his constitutional rights to freedom of expression, and was arbitrary, capricious, and legally impermissible. The teacher also contended that the school board violated his constitutional rights to freedom of expression and due process of law by dismissing him for his showing of the film 1900. The court held that it did not agree that his use of the film was entitled to blanket constitutional protection, but did agree that, under the circumstances, his conduct was protected by the First Amendment because the teacher did not have prior notice of the policy and regulation concerning controversial learning resources. The court reversed the order of the school board and the cause was remanded to the school board with directions to reinstate the teacher to his position as a full-time, non-probationary teacher with no loss to him of any pay, seniority, or other employment benefits which he otherwise would have sustained as a result of the school board's decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the school board and remanded the cause with instructions to reinstate the teacher to his position as a full-time instructor.

Musso v. Musso (In re Estate of Musso)


No. 96CA0388


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


932 P.2d 853; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 7



January 9, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Pueblo County. Honorable Alex J. Martinez, Judge. No. 94PR97.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a probate action, respondent personal representative sought review of an order from the District Court of Pueblo County (Colorado), which determined that certain property was co-owned by the decedent and petitioner wife, awarded fees to respondent for his services, and awarded fees to the current personal representative.


OVERVIEW: In a probate action, the trial court had issued an order that determined certain property was co-owned by the decedent and the wife, awarded the personal representative fees for his services, and also awarded fees to the current personal representative. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order in all aspects, except it reversed the award of fees to the personal representative. The court agreed with the trial court's ruling that rejected the application of the rebuttable common law presumption that a husband solely owned all household goods. The court held that such an application it would have been unconstitutional under the Equal Rights Amendment, Colo. Const. art. II, § 29. Next, the court declined to disturb the trial court's determination that the decedent and the wife had co-owned the decanter collection because there was adequate support in the record for such a determination. Finally, the court did not find support in the record that justified awarding fees to the personal representative of $ 15 per hour for his services.


OUTCOME: In a probate action, the court affirmed the trial court's order that determined a certain property was co-owned by the decedent and the wife, and that awarded fees to the current personal representative, except it reversed the order that awarded fees to the personal representative for his services.

People ex rel. R.W.V.


No. 96CA0601


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


942 P.2d 1317; 1997 Colo. App. LEXIS 6



January 9, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied February 27, 1997. Released for Publication September 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Mesa County. Honorable Charles A. Buss, Judge. No. 94JD894.



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Mesa County (Colorado), which ordered deferred judgment and sentence after the entry of a guilty plea by appellee juvenile over the state's objection.


OVERVIEW: In the plea agreement the state and the juvenile agreed that the juvenile would receive probation and the state would not oppose deferred adjudication if it was recommended by the probation department. The probation department determined that deferred adjudication was not appropriate. Over the state's objection, the trial court ordered that the juvenile's judgment and sentence be deferred. The state appealed. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court found that although the period of deferred adjudication had expired, the appeal was not moot because the issue was capable of repetition and needed to be addressed by the court. The court found that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-2-702(1) clearly required the consent of the state for the trial court to impose a deferred sentence. Because the state objected to the deferred sentence, the trial court exceeded its authority. The court found that statutory sentencing requirements did not violate the separation of powers doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order for deferred sentencing and remanded the matter for resentencing of the juvenile.

People v. Geyer


No. 94CA2054


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


942 P.2d 1297; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 371



December 27, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified and as Modified Petitions for Rehearing DENIED February 13, 1997. Released for Publication September 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Summit County. Honorable Terry W. Ruckriegle, Judge. No. 94CR22.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Summit County (Colorado), which convicted him of third degree burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested shortly after he broke into a locked, glass display cabinet at a resort. Local retail merchants had rented space in the cabinet to display merchandise, such as leather jackets and jewelry. Defendant was convicted of third degree burglary, and the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that defendant's entry into the glass display case was prohibited by Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-204(1) (1986 Repl. Vol. 8B). The court found that the locked, glass case was similar to a depository incorporated into a building for the purpose of protecting valuable items on display from, among other things, theft. The court noted that the glass display cabinet was similar to a "vault," a room or area designed for the safekeeping of valuables. The court held that the phrase "other apparatus or equipment" was not unconstitutionally vague in its application to the facts of the case. The court rejected defendant's argument that his conviction had to be set aside for lack of evidence that a glass display was covered by § 18-4-204(1). The court held that the failure to include the elements of "knowingly" and "unlawful entry" in the jury instruction was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of third degree burglary.

People v. Thien Van Vo


No. 95CA1840


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


932 P.2d 849; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 354



December 12, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Ruthanne N. Polidori, Judge. No. 95CR737.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a sentence imposed by the District Court, First Judicial District (Colorado), which included two surcharges imposed in connection with defendant's sentence to probation following his guilty plea to second-degree sexual assault, a class four felony. The surcharges were imposed pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 18-21-103(1)(c); 24-4.2-104(1)(a)(II)(A), (B) (Cum. Supp. 1996).


OVERVIEW: The surcharge under § 24-4.2-104 was imposed for the specific crime of second-degree sexual assault. The other surcharge under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-21-103 was imposed on a person convicted of a class four sex offense. Defendant claimed that the imposition of the two surcharges violated the prohibition against double jeopardy under Colo. Const. art. II, § 18. He contended that it was a cumulative punishment arising from a single prosecution. On appeal, the court found no violation of the Double Jeopardy Clause because the legislature clearly intended to enhance the sanctions for class four felonies dealing with sex offenses, specifically the crime of second-degree sexual assault. Therefore, the cumulative punishment was authorized, and the surcharges were functionally the same as mandatory fines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence imposed by the trial court.

People v. 2896 W. 64th Ave.


No. 95CA0690


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


937 P.2d 873; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 275; 20 Colo. J. 1367



September 26, 1996, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Adams County. Honorable Harlan R. Bockman, Judge. No. 91CV624.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, owners and operators of spa, appealed a judgment from the District Court, Seventeenth Judicial District (Colorado), which on a complaint by plaintiff, the People, permanently enjoined the operation of the spa on the ground that it was a public nuisance, in violation of Adams County, Colo., Ordinance No. 1.


OVERVIEW: The owners operated a spa that offered paying customers the opportunity to take private nude whirlpool bathes with female spa employees, who also were nude. There was no evidence or allegations of sexual acts being committed at the spa. The spa was open 24 hours a day, 7 days a week. The People were granted an injunction based upon the spa's numerous violations of Adams County, Colo., Ordinance No. 1 (Ordinance), which pertained to "nude entertainment." On appeal, the court ruled that under U.S. Const. amend XIV, the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague in its definition of the term "entertainment," in that the Ordinance provided fair notice of the prohibited conduct, and a reasonable person could make a common sense evaluation of whether the ordinance regulated nude entertainment or just nudity, and there was evidence that the spa provided not only provided but advertised "nude entertainment" The trial court did not err by admitting evidence of events that were the subject of prior criminal proceedings against the spa, and if it was error, the error was harmless, under Colo. R. Crim. P. 61, because there was ample independent evidence to support the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.
