People v. Talley


No. 94CA1570


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


934 P.2d 859; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 266



September 5, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 15, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Frank Martinez, Judge. No. 82CR266.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the District Court for the City and County of Denver, Colorado, which denied his motion for post-conviction relief pursuant to Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c). The trial court found that defendant's motion was untimely pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-5-402 (1986) and concluded that the amendments to the habitual criminal statute reclassifying two of the predicate felonies to misdemeanors applied prospectively only.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his motion was not untimely because the time bar of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-5-402 did not apply to a post-conviction motion which challenged only the sentence. In the alternative, defendant argued that there was justifiable excuse or excusable neglect for the late filing and that the court should hear the motion. The court upheld the trial court's ruling. In so holding, the court found that: (1) defendant's contention that the time bar in § 16-5-402, which required that a defendant commence post-conviction proceedings within three years of the conviction, did not apply to proportionality reviews was without merit; (2) the limitation period of § 16-5-402 was applicable to a proportionality review of a sentence imposed pursuant to the habitual criminal statutes; (3) the trial court correctly concluded that the 1993 amendments to the habitual criminal statute had not application to defendant's sentence, as the legislature expressly stated that the new provisions applied prospectively only; and (4) defendant's motion for post-conviction relief was untimely and the trial court properly denied it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Freedom From Religion Found. v. Romer


No. 95CA0433


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


921 P.2d 84; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 202; 20 BTR 1044



June 27, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Frank Martinez, Judge. No. 93CV5624.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, foundation and individuals, challenged an order from the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which dismissed their complaint against appellee various government officials.


OVERVIEW: The foundation and individuals (foundation) filed an action against the various governmental official (officials) alleging violations of the First and Fourteenth Amendments of the Colorado Constitution basing its allegations on the authorized holding of religious services in the state parks during the Pope's visit constituted promotion of religion. The officials filed a motion to dismiss. The lower court granted the motion, determined that injunctive relief was moot, and that the officials had qualified immunity. The court affirmed the lower court and reasoned that the claims for injunctive and declaratory relief were moot, because the services already occurred. Further, the court determined that the officials were entitled to qualified immunity under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court interpreted the claims against the officials as seeking damages in their individual capacities. The court determined that the ministerial act exception to qualified immunity was narrow and did not apply because the foundation made no allegations that the officers were performing ministerial rather than discretionary functions, or that they were required by law to perform the offending acts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which dismissed the complaint of the foundation and individuals in their action against the various government officials.

Cappelli v. Demlow

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured sought review of a decision from the District Court of Jefferson County (Colorado), which dismissed his civil action brought pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and Col. R. Civ. P. 106 against defendant judge who had granted the state's motion seeking to obtain a mental competency evaluation of the injured in regard to his criminal case for arson and obstructing a fireman.


OVERVIEW: The injured was charged with arson and obstructing a fireman and the judge granted the state's request for a mental competency evaluation of the injured. The judge ordered the injured held by the sheriff pending such evaluation and the injured filed a civil complaint and a motion for a temporary restraining order against the judge. The injured appealed and the court affirmed, holding that Col. Rev. Stat. §§ 16-8-110 to -111 (1986 Repl. Vol. 8A) did not implicate the Fourth Amendment and that the judge's actions in ordering the injured involuntarily committed and evaluated were not in violation of the due process requirements or equal protection provisions of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court found that the state had a legitimate interest in ensuring that criminal defendants were mentally competent to stand trial and that any difference in standards between the civil and criminal commitment statutes was also rationally related to legitimate state interests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the injured's civil action against the judge.

People v. Schmidt


No. 94CA1683


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


928 P.2d 805; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 198; 20 BTR 1025



June 27, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 25, 1996. Released for Publication December 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable James D. Zimmerman, Judge. No. 93CR980.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the District Court of Jefferson County (Colorado), which, upon a jury's verdict, entered a conviction against him for felony theft, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-401(2) (1986 Repl.).


OVERVIEW: At defendant's trial for felony theft, the prosecution introduced the affixed price tags of the items of clothing stolen. Before trial, the defendant filed a motion requesting the trial court to declare the statute allowing admission of the price tags, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-414 (1995 Cum. Supp.) unconstitutional because it allegedly violated an accused's right to confront and cross- examine witnesses on the essential element of value, and it allowed the admission of hearsay evidence on the issue of value without a foundation and without any indicia of reliability. The trial court denied the motion and a jury found defendant guilty of felony theft, § 18-4-401(2). On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the General Assembly determined that a price tag affixed to an item offered for sale ordinarily was sufficiently trustworthy so as to speak for itself regarding that item's value and that the utility of confrontation was very remote. And, because the statute allowed an accused to rebut the presumption of value, § 18-4-414 did not violate the defendant's Sixth Amendment right to confront his accuser.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction.

People v. Lesslie


No. 94CA1947


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


939 P.2d 443; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 179; 20 BTR 916



June 13, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Hinsdale County. Honorable J. Steven Patrick, Judge. No. 93CR2.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the District Court of Hinsdale County (Colorado), which convicted defendant of conspiracy to commit eavesdropping in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-2-201.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for conspiracy to commit eavesdropping under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-2-201. In an effort to intercept conversations related to narcotics transactions, defendant cooperated with others to place a listening device on the windowsill of the men's restroom of a local bar and to monitor conversations from a nearby motel. While conversations were intercepted, no drug transactions were overheard. The bar owner discovered the devices and reported it to the district attorney. The trial court convicted defendant. On appeal, the court found that the occupants of the restroom had an objectively reasonable expectation of privacy, which could not be thwarted by use of a hidden transmitter that permitted surreptitious eavesdropping. Further, the court held that the trial court properly excluded the expert witness' testimony as unnecessary and as improperly usurping the function of the court. The court found that the factual findings were supported in the record, and would not be disturbed on appeal. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for conspiracy to commit eavesdropping because the occupants of the restroom had an objectively reasonable expectation of privacy, which could not be thwarted by use of a hidden transmitter that permitted surreptitious eavesdropping.

Hughey v. Jefferson County Bd. of Comm'rs


No. 95CA0971


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


921 P.2d 76; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 177; 20 BTR 935



June 13, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Colorado State Board of Assessment Appeals. No. 28120.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a tax lien purchaser, appealed the judgment of the Colorado State Board of Assessment Appeals, which denied her a refund for certain tax years.


OVERVIEW: The purchaser bought a tax lien on certain property. She paid the property taxes on the land for the tax years 1987-1990. She did not pay the property taxes for 1991, and the lien was sold to a third party, who paid the property taxes for 1991 and 1992. The purchaser applied for and received a treasurer's deed in 1993. She filed an abatement petition for the tax years 1987-1993. Respondent board of county commissioners denied the abatement, and she appealed to the Board. The Board ordered a refund for 1993 but denied a refund for 1987-1992, reasoning that the purchaser lacked standing to petition for the abatement. She appealed again, and the court agreed that she had no standing to petition for abatement for those years because the rights of tax lien purchasers did not expressly include the right to challenge property valuations for tax purposes. The purchaser also argued that the valuation of the parcel throughout the time she was a lienholder and owner was arbitrary and contrary to the statutory scheme. Limiting its review to the 1993 valuation, the court found that, because there was record support for the assessor's determination, the determination was binding upon the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board's order.

D & B Enterprises v. Commissioner of Ins.


No. 95CA1907


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released For Publication July 17, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Colorado Division of Insurance. No. 96008.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this administrative action concerning the application of new rates for workers' compensation insurance, petitioner insured employers appealed a determination from the Colorado Division of Insurance denying them a quasi-judicial hearing.


OVERVIEW: After the national licensed rating organization submitted a workers' compensation loss cost and rating values filing to the Colorado Division of Insurance, the Commissioner of Insurance placed the rate filing on public inspection, held a public hearing, and commissioned an independent expert to review the filing. The commissioner later approved the new rate as applicable only to policies as they were initiated or renewed, rather than to all outstanding policies. Arguing that failure to make the new rates applicable to outstanding policies disadvantaged them compared to other policy holders, certain insured employers requested a quasi-judicial hearing under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 10-4-407(3) (1994). The commissioner denied the request for a hearing. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that the commissioner's approval of the rate filing was a quasi-legislative act that did not violate equal protection. Further, in the absence of a recognized property right, there was no violation of the due process clause in denying them a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the commissioner of insurance denying the request of insured employers for a quasi-judicial hearing.

Spedding v. Motor Vehicle Dealer Bd.


No. 95CA0241


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


931 P.2d 480; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 154; 20 BTR 780



May 16, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified, Petition for Rehearing DENIED June 20, 1996. Certiorari Petition Granted January 27, 1997. Released for Publication February 18, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Motor Vehicle Dealer Board.



DISPOSITION: ORDER VACATED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent dealer appealed from a decision of appellee Colorado Motor Vehicle Dealer Board (board) that suspended its suspending its dealer's license for one day and imposed a fine upon it for violation of the Automobile Dealers Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-6-101, et seq., and of the Consumer Protection Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 6-1-105(1)(ii).


OVERVIEW: The dealer was charged with violating the Automobile Dealers Act and the Consumer Protection Act after failing to disclose to customers that vehicles they bought were salvaged vehicles. As a result, the dealer's license was suspended for one day, and it was ordered to pay a fine. The dealer appealed this decision, and the court vacated and remanded for further proceedings. The court found that the board erred when it determined that the Automobile Dealers Act did not require a finding that the dealer's failure to disclosure material particulars to a buyer be wilful. According to the plain meaning of the Automobile Dealers Act, a finding of willfulness was clearly required. The court further found that the dealer was denied a meaningful opportunity to respond to the charges against it because evidence of prior complaints against the dealer were considered by the board in determination of the sanction to be imposed, however, the dealer did not receive notice that this evidence would be introduced.


OUTCOME: The decision finding the dealer in violation of the Automobile Dealers Act and the Consumer Protection Act was vacated and remanded for further proceedings.

Stackhouse v. School Dist. No. 1


No. 95CA0592


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


919 P.2d 902; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 131; 20 BTR 740



May 2, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released For Publication July 17, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Robert P. Fullerton, Judge. No. 93CV3135.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teachers sought review of a judgment of the District Court, City and County of Denver (Colorado), which held that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 22-63-202(2)(a) (1995 Repl. Vol. 9), which allowed the deduction of expenses from the teachers' final paychecks, was constitutional and granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, a school district and a board of education, in an action for breach of contract.


OVERVIEW: The teachers were employed by the board until each voluntarily resigned from his position. Relying upon § 22-63- 202(2)(a), the board deducted $ 1,000 from each of the teachers' final paychecks for the expense of replacing the teachers. The teachers filed an action that alleged breach of contract. The trial court held that § 22-63-202(2)(a) was constitutional and granted summary judgment in favor of defendants. On appeal, the court affirmed the determination that § 22-63-202(2)(a) was constitutional and reversed the summary judgment in favor of defendants. The court remanded the case for the determination of the actual expenses incurred by the board in replacing the teachers. The court held that the board erroneously deducted the maximum amount allowed without having proven that it actually incurred such expense. The court ruled that § 22-63-202(2)(a) required the board to prove that the amount it withheld did not exceed the ordinary and necessary expenses incurred in securing a suitable replacement for a particular teacher. The court held that it rejected the board's assertion that it could withhold an amount estimated to cover the average training and orientation expenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the determination that § 22-63-202(2)(a) was constitutional and reversed the summary judgment in favor of defendants. The court remanded the case for the determination of the actual expenses incurred by the board in replacing the teachers.

Montezuma Well Serv. v. Industrial Claim Appeals Office


No. 95CA0793


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


928 P.2d 796; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 136; 20 BTR 742



May 2, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 20, 1996. Released for Publication December 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 3105877.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, Colorado Compensation Insurance Authority and the Subsequent Injury Fund, sought review of a final order of respondent Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado, which determined that respondent claimant's benefits did not terminate at age 65.


OVERVIEW: An administrative law judge awarded benefits to the claimant until he was 65 years of age. A division of the court of appeals found that the age provisions of Col. Rev. Stat. § 8-42-111(5) unconstitutional. The claims appeal office modified the decision so the benefits would not terminate at age 65, and petitioners appealed. During the pendency of the appeal, the state supreme court affirmed that § 8-42-111(5) was unconstitutional. Petitioners also challenged the validity of § 8-42-111(4). On appeal, the court affirmed and found no reason to sever retroactively § 8-42-111(4) from the Workers' Compensation Act. The court held that the Cost of Living adjustment under § 8-42-111(4) was severable from the age cap provision in § 8-42-111(5). The court noted that the statute contained a severablilty clause under 1991 Colo. Sess. Laws ch. 219. The court articulated that the severability clause created a presumption that the General Assembly would have been satisfied with the statute that remained after the offending provisions were stricken as unconstitutional. The court found that petitioners did not overcome the presumption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Wine & Spirits Wholesalers v. Colorado Dep't of Revenue, Liquor Enforcement Div.


No. 94CA1722


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Robert S. Hyatt, Judge. No. 94CV1654.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff liquor wholesalers sought review of the order from the Denver County District Court (Colorado), which affirmed the adoption by defendant, Liquor Enforcement Division of the Colorado Department of Revenue, of regulations prohibiting manufacturers, wholesalers, and importers of alcohol from selling alcoholic beverages to retailers below cost.


OVERVIEW: The Liquor Enforcement Division of the Colorado Department of Revenue adopted a regulation prohibiting manufacturers, wholesalers, and importers of alcohol from selling alcoholic beverages to retailers below cost. The liquor wholesaler filed an action seeking judicial review and the trial court affirmed the adoption of the regulation. On appeal, the court held that the General Assembly had not, either explicitly or implicitly, required that a grantor of financial assistance or credit must have intended to gain influence or control over a liquor retailer before the financial assistance was unlawful. The court held that the Liquor Enforcement Division properly based its action primarily on policy considerations without providing any factual support and could have rejected any adverse submissions by the public and adopted its rule so long as it was reasonable to do so. The court held that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-47-105 granted the Liquor Enforcement Division broad discretion in regulating the liquor industry and affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the trial court affirming the adoption of the regulation.

People v. Olson


No. 94CA1716


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


921 P.2d 51; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 112; 20 BTR 571



April 18, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 27, 1996. Released for Publication August 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Michael C. Villano, Judge. No. 94CR578.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Jefferson County (Colorado), which convicted him of driving while his ability was impaired by consumption of alcohol (DWAI), speeding, possession of a controlled substance, possession of marijuana, and possession of drug paraphernalia.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of DWAI, speeding, possession of a controlled substance, possession of marijuana, and possession of drug paraphernalia. Defendant's sole contention on appeal was that his conviction was barred by principles of double jeopardy because his driver's license was revoked in a civil proceeding for refusing to take a test for blood alcohol content. The court affirmed defendant's convictions, holding that in order to establish, for double jeopardy purposes, that multiple punishments were being imposed, a defendant must show that the penalties or sanctions in each of the separate proceedings could be considered punishment. The court found that under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 42-2-122.1, which governed revocation of driver's licenses because of a failure to submit to a breath or blood test, the sanction was intended to serve the remedial purpose of fostering the safety of the general public. The court concluded that an administrative license revocation imposed because of a refusal to take an alcohol test constituted a remedial sanction as opposed to punishment, therefore, the revocation did not violate double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for DWAI, speeding, possession of a controlled substance, possession of marijuana, and possession of drug paraphernalia.

Gwin v. Chesrown Chevrolet


No. 94CA1943


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


931 P.2d 466; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 117; 20 BTR 574



April 18, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 27, 1996. Certiorari Petition Denied February 18, 1997. Released for Publication February 18, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Adams County. Honorable Donald W. Marshall, Jr., Judge. No. 93CV0950.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Adams County (Colorado), which found defendant liable for the discriminatory and unlawful firing of plaintiff former employee. Defendant contended that the jury's verdicts were irreconcilably inconsistent, that an award of punitive damages was improper, and that it was entitled to a directed verdict.


OVERVIEW: Defendant employer fired plaintiff former employee after he demanded a refund of money paid to participate in a voluntary sales seminar. Plaintiff filed an action against defendant employer for alleged violations of 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000e-2 of Title VII of the Civil Rights Act of 1964, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1981, and Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-34-402.5 (Cum. Supp. 1995), and for outrageous conduct. The trial court entered a judgment for plaintiff and defendant appealed. The court affirmed the judgment against defendant. The court determined that the jury's finding that defendant fired plaintiff because of his race was not inconsistent with its finding that he was fired because of his lawful activity at the seminar. The court concluded that the award of punitive damages did not violate Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-102(1)(a) (1987) because there was no need to apportion the actual damages among plaintiff's claims based upon § 1981, § 24-34-402.5, and outrageous conduct. The court found that the denial of defendant's motion for directed verdict was not error because § 24-34-402.5 did not require plaintiff to prove that defendant adopted a specific restriction on plaintiff's lawful activities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against defendant employer. The jury's verdicts for plaintiff former employee were not inconsistent, the award of punitive damages did not violate a state statute, and the denial of defendant's motion for directed verdict was not error.

Villa at Greely, Inc. v. Hopper


No. 95CA1655


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


917 P.2d 350; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 109; 20 BTR 536



April 11, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released For Publication June 12, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] THIS OPINION IS NOT THE FINAL VERSION AND IS SUBJECT .Appeal from the District Court of Weld County. Honorable John J. Althoff, Judge. Honorable William L. West, Judge. No. 95CV61.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor citizen appealed the judgment of the District Court of Weld County (Colorado), which held that plaintiff developer had a vested property right in a site-specific development plan (PUD plan) approved by defendant Board of County Commissioners (board), reasoning that because a charter amendment was enacted subsequent to the board's approval of developer's PUD plan, it was inapplicable to the developer's vested property right.


OVERVIEW: The board approved a PUD plan submitted by the developer for construction of a pre-parole facility in the lower court's county. The citizen submitted petitions to the county calling for a referendum to give the electorate special authority to review siting decisions over various incarceration facilities. The developer was then granted a ruling construing its vested property right in the PUD plan development pursuant to the Vested Property Rights Act (Act), Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-68-101 et seq. (1988). The trial court ruled that developer had a vested property right, which precluded any zoning or land use action by a local government or pursuant to any subsequent initiated measure which would alter, impair, prevent, diminish, or otherwise delay the developer's development or use of its property as set forth in the PUD plan. The county's voters, through a referendum, then enacted a charter amendment, which precluded issuance of a certificate of occupancy for pre-parole facilities until the location and siting of the facility had been approved by a majority vote of the county electorate. The court reversed the lower court, finding error in the lower court's interpretation of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment and remanded the case to it. The trial court erred in interpreting the Vested Property Rights Act to preclude an initiated measure from affecting developer's vested right. The court found that the Act only created a vested right in the developer, subject to divestment upon proper exercise of a statutory exception.

People v. Gallegos


No. 93CA2135


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


926 P.2d 156; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 105; 20 BTR 476



April 4, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended July 11, 1996. Rehearing Denied May 23, 1996. Released For Publication November 4, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Mesa County. Honorable Charles A. Buss, Judge. Honorable Amanda D. Bailey, Judge. No. 92CR522.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Mesa County (Colorado), which convicted him of second degree murder and accessory after-the-fact to manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of second degree murder and accessory after-the-fact to manslaughter. Defendant claimed that he was denied his statutory right to a speedy trial. On appeal, the court reversed the convictions and remanded the case to the trial court to dismiss the charges with prejudice. The court ruled that the prosecution's pretrial appeal of the dismissal of the felony murder count was not within the scope of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-12-102(2) (1995 Cum. Supp.), Colo. App. R. 4.1, Colo. App. R. 21, or Colo. R. Crim. P. 7(h)(4), and was not an interlocutory appeal within the meaning of the speedy trial statute, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-405 (1986 Repl.). The court found that the time during which the appeal of the dismissal of the felony murder count was pending could not properly be excluded from the computation of the period of time during which trial must have been held pursuant to § 18-1-405. The court also found that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the prosecution's pretrial appeal. The court held that defendant's trial was, therefore, untimely and violated defendant's statutory right to a speedy trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had convicted defendant of second degree murder and accessory after-the-fact to manslaughter. The court remanded the case to the trial court with directions to dismiss the charges against defendant with prejudice and to discharge defendant from the sentence imposed.

People v. Gonzales


No. 94CA0099


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


926 P.2d 153; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 107; 20 BTR 480



April 4, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 9, 1996. Released for Publication November 4, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Richard T. Spriggs, Judge. No. 93CR439.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which convicted defendant of first degree assault on a peace officer and attempted second degree murder. Defendant contended that the verdicts were inconsistent, that the first degree assault statute, found at Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-202(1)(2) (1986 Repl. Vol. 8B), was unconstitutional, and that the sentences were excessive.


OVERVIEW: When a police officer entered an apartment in response to a disturbance call, defendant opened fire upon the officer. The officer was struck by one bullet. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The convictions for first degree assault and attempted second degree murder were not inconsistent because inconsistent verdicts of guilt and acquittal were not prohibited. Defendant's argument, that an intent to cause serious bodily injury was inconsistent with an intent to cause death, rested upon the incorrect assumption that a defendant guilty of attempted second degree murder must have specifically intended to cause the victim's death. In fact, defendant could be found guilty of attempted second degree murder even without the specific intent to cause death. Also, intent to cause serious bodily injury was not necessarily an intent to cause only serious bodily injury. The court also found that the first degree assault charge was not a less serious act than second degree assault, as prior case law dictated. The court found that the sentences were within the range required by statute. However, the mittimus reflected the wrong crime. Therefore, the case was remanded for correction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and the sentence, but remanded the case so that the mittimus could be corrected to reflect a conviction for attempted second degree murder.

Barela v. Beye


No. 94CA1500


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


916 P.2d 668; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 74; 20 BTR 387



March 21, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 21, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Paul A. Markson, Judge. No. 92CV7364.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Colorado Department of Social Services and its Executive Director (department), sought review of the judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which granted summary judgment to plaintiffs, recipients of home care allowance funds, and issued a preliminary injunction.


OVERVIEW: The recipients received funds to pay for unskilled services in their homes to provide for their basic needs through a home care allowance program authorized by Colo. Rev. Stat. § 26-2-122.3(1)(b). The department promulgated a rule that implemented the statute. The department reevaluated the eligibility of the lead plaintiff recipient and reduced his benefits. The department issued a final decision that affirmed an administrative law judge's initial decision that affirmed the reduction. The recipient sought judicial review of the decision, and a class of recipients was certified. The parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment. The trial court held § 26-1-111(2)(o)(1) was unconstitutional, that the rule exceeded the department's statutory authority, and was arbitrary and capricious. The court reversed, and held that: (1) the statute contained sufficient standards to guide the department in rational and consistent rulemaking and the standards provided for meaningful judicial review; (2) the department acted within its statutory authority in promulgation of the rule; and (3) the statute was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for further proceedings.

Sears v. Romer


No. 94CA1767


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


928 P.2d 745; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 75; 20 BTR 397



March 21, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 9, 1996. Released for Publication December 18, 1996.
Rehearing denied by, 05/09/1996
Writ of certiorari denied Sears v. Romer, 1996 Colo. LEXIS 636 (Colo., Nov. 18, 1996)
Related proceeding at McCool v. Sears, 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 675 (Colo. Ct. App., May 1, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Edward A. Simons, Judge. No. 93CV4895.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff outfitter brought a declaratory judgment action against defendants, State of Colorado, Department of Regulatory Agencies, and Division of Registrations, to challenge the constitutionality of the Outfitters and Guides Act (Act), Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12.55.5-101 et seq. (1991). The outfitter appealed from the summary judgment entered by the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado) for defendants.


OVERVIEW: The outfitter sought to enjoin enforcement of provisions in the Act after defendants notified him that complaints lodged about his conduct as an outfitter warranted a disciplinary hearing. The outfitter argued that the requirement that violators of the Act pay the costs of conducting an administrative proceeding violated equal protection. The outfitter also argued that the Act violated his guarantee of equal access to the courts by requiring him to pursue judicial review of agency decisions rather than granting "initial access" to the courts. The outfitter finally argued that defendants had no authority to prevent him from working as a "guide," and that they exceeded their rule-making authority by adding disciplinary grounds for outfitters not contained or implied in the Act. The court rejected the outfitter's arguments. The court reasoned that the challenged rules elaborated upon statutory provisions in the Act and were therefore expressly or impliedly authorized by the enabling legislation. The promulgation of the rules was also proper, and the rules did not modify or conflict with the Act. The rules did not constitute "agency legislation" and were therefore constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment entered for defendants in the outfitter's action to challenge the constitutionality of certain provisions in the Outfitters and Guides Act.

 

1491 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gurule


No. 94CA1613


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


924 P.2d 1164; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 84; 20 BTR 395



March 21, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 25, 1996. Certiorari Denied October 15, 1996 (96SC279). Cases Released for Publication on Tuesday, October 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Christopher J. Munch, Judge. No. 94CR139.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment entered by the District Court, First Judicial District (Colorado), which convicted him of the offense of possession of burglary tools, a violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-205 (1986), after a jury verdict to that effect.


OVERVIEW: A grocery store manager observed defendant placing packs of cigarettes in a pouch concealed underneath his clothing. That pouch consisted of a pair of bib overalls from which the bottom portion had been removed. A jury found defendant guilty of the offenses of possession of burglary tools and misdemeanor theft. The trial court entered a judgment convicting him of only the burglary tools offense. On appeal, that judgment was affirmed. The court found that defendant had adapted the overalls to a use other than their ordinary purpose, for purposes of § 18-4-205, which proscribed the possession of burglary tools. Moreover, when its words were accorded their plain meaning, § 18-4-205 adequately defined the proscribed conduct and was not unconstitutionally vague. Furthermore, possession had to be accompanied by an intent to commit burglary or theft by a physical taking. Section 18-4-205 did not violate equal protection because the conduct it proscribed was readily distinguishable from that prohibited by Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-104 (1986), which defined theft. Finally, the trial court fairly appraised defendant of the consequences regarding his decision to testify at his trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1492 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Buckley Powder Co. v. State


No. 94CA1584


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


924 P.2d 1133; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 65; 20 BTR 267



March 7, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 11, 1996. Certiorari Granted October 15, 1996 (96SC243). Certiorari Granted on the following issue: When the constitutionality of a statute is in issue, whether a Colorado trial court possesses the discretion to consider "useful purpose" of or "need" for class certification when determining whether to grant class certificatino under C.R.C.P. 23. Cases Released for Publication on Tuesday, October 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Lynne M. Hufnagel, Judge. No. 93CV450.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation challenged an order of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which denied the corporation class certification pursuant to Colo. R. Civ. P. 23, failed to provide it with a remedy, dismissed its declaratory judgment action against defendants, state and officials, and granted the state partial summary judgment with respect to the corporation's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims.


OVERVIEW: A corporation filed an action against the state and officials challenging the constitutionality of motor vehicle taxes imposed on trucks used in interstate commerce. The corporation sought to certify a class and alleged that the state violated 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and that it was entitled to a declaratory judgment. The trial court declared that the tax was unconstitutional, but declined to provide the corporation with any remedy. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. It held that the trial court erred in denying class certification because of a lack of need. There was no need requirement in Colo. R. Civ. P. 23 actions. After declaring the collected tax unconstitutional, the trial court was obligated to provide the corporation with a remedy. It was correct to grant the state's motion for summary judgment with respect to the corporation's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims. The claims were precluded because adequate state remedies were available. The corporation's tax liability involved the constitutionality of statutes, and therefore the trial court should have entered declaratory judgment its favor.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying the corporation class certification and a declaratory judgment in its action against the state and officials and remanded the cause for entry of an order granting declaratory relief and for further proceedings. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

 

1493 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Hall v. Zavaras


No. 94CA1761


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


916 P.2d 634; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 51; 20 BTR 206



February 22, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified Rehearing Denied March 28, 1996.
Released For Publication May 21, 1996. Certiorari DENIED October 15, 1996 (96SC285).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable David D. Parrish, Judge. No. 94CV1463.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed from a judgment of the District Court, Fourth Judicial District (Colorado), which dismissed his complaint under Colo. R. Civ. P. 106(a)(4) against defendants, employees and officials of the Colorado Department of Corrections (DOC), for denial of good time credits as a result of an unfounded allegation that he has refused to participate in a sex offender treatment program (SOTP) and violation of the ex post facto laws.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted in 1978 of first degree sexual assault and second degree assault. He filed a Colo. R. Civ. P. 106(a)(4) proceeding, contending that the DOC violated his due process rights by conditioning his right to obtain good time credit on his participation in SOTP. The court affirmed the dismissal of his complaint. The general assembly gave the DOC discretion in the grant or denial of good time credit. Thus, the inmate had no legitimate claim of entitlement to the award of meritorious good time credits. Because the DOC's grant or denial of good time credit was wholly discretionary, the decision to withhold or condition such credits did not constitute the imposition of additional punishment. Furthermore, the DOC did not act arbitrarily or abuse its statutory discretion by conditioning the inmate's earning of meritorious time credits upon his participation in the SOTP. Additionally, there was no ex post facto violation. The DOC did not retroactively apply to him the statutory criteria of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-22.5-302(1) (1986). Rather, the DOC was acting pursuant to its discretion under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-22.5-201 (1986).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1494 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Estes


No. 94CA1198


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


923 P.2d 358; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 58; 20 BTR 191



February 22, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified Rehearing Denied March 21, 1996. Certiorari Denied September 16, 1996 (96SC257). Released For Publication September 25, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Douglas County. Honorable Thomas J. Curry, Judge. No. 93CR140.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Douglas County (Colorado) which ordered him to pay $ 56,000 of restitution to the victim and her family after entering a guilty plea to a charge of felony theft.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered into a relationship with a married woman and borrowed $ 9,000 to buy a car. He then extorted $ 44,000 from her. He pleaded guilty to two counts of felony theft. The trial court ordered him to pay restitution of the $ 44,000 extortion money, the $ 9,000 auto loan, and $ 3,000 for counseling for the victim and her family, and further directed him to pay future counseling expenses that might be needed. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the restitution order did not penalize conduct that was not criminal due to the original extortion statute's being held unconstitutionally overbroad because the entry of his guilty plea was valid and it waived all his non-jurisdictional defenses. The court further held that the $ 9,000 auto loan was improperly included in the restitution amount because there was no evidence that the loan resulted from any criminal activity, and that the trial court erred in ordering restitution for undetermined future counseling expenses because no evidence appeared in the transcript revealing the need for future counseling. The amount of restitution needed to be based on actual pecuniary damages sustained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the restitution order in part, but reversed as to orders to pay an auto loan and undetermined expenses of future counseling, and remanded with instructions to vacate the reversed portions of the order.

 

1495 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Johnson


No. 93CA1361


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


923 P.2d 342; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 41; 20 BTR 175



February 15, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 28, 1996. Certiorari Denied September 23, 1996 (96SC274). Released For Publication September 25, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Richard T. Spriggs, Judge. No. 85CR2569.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate appealed from a judgment of the District Court, City and County of Denver (Colorado), which denied his Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c) motion attacking his 1990 conviction for first degree assault.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed a motion under Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c), challenging his conviction for first degree assault. The inmate contended that the first degree assault statute, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-202(1)(c) (1986), violated his right to equal protection of the law because it was not sufficiently distinguishable from the second degree assault statute, 1971 Colo. Sess. Laws 121, § 40-3-203, that was applicable at the time of the offense at issue. The court affirmed the denial of the motion. Even though the differences in the two statutes may have varied only in a matter of degree, the classification did not violate the guarantees of equal protection. The differences in language, and the nuances therefrom, constituted statutory discreteness in culpability that rendered the statutes categorically distinct and different based on real elements of mens rea and conduct. Moreover, the evidence was sufficient to convict the inmate of extreme indifference first degree assault. Also, since the jury indicated no confusion about the meaning of certain common phrases, the trial court's failure specifically to define them did not necessitate a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1496 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Motor Vehicle Div., Motor Vehicle Dealer Bd. v. Castro


No. 94CA1875


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


914 P.2d 517; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 39; 20 BTR 130



February 8, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released For Publication April 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Colorado Motor Vehicle Dealer Board.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Motor Vehicle Dealer Board summarily suspended the used motor vehicle dealer license of appellant automotive group. The automotive group filed a notice of appeal with the board and a complaint in the district court seeking injunctive and declaratory relief, which was denied. The board held an evidentiary hearing and suspended the automotive group's license for five years. The automotive group sought review.


OVERVIEW: The automotive group claimed that the board erred in suspending their dealer's license. They argued that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-4-104(4) was unconstitutional on its face and that it violated their due process rights. The court rejected these claims and affirmed the board's determination. The court found that procedural due process was based on fundamental fairness, which included adequate notice and an opportunity to be heard prior to state action. The court also found that when the state demonstrated the need for immediate action to protect legitimate interests, an adequate post-deprivation hearing satisfied due process. The court found that these requirements were met by the statute as a whole and as applied to the automotive group. The court found that the automotive group did not demand an earlier hearing date as permitted by Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-4-105(12). Thus, having failed to demand an immediate hearing, the court held that the automotive group could not complain of an error caused by their own actions. In addition, the court held that any vagueness in the term "promptly" was cured by a licensee's right to request an "immediate" hearing following an emergency suspension.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board's suspension of the automotive group's used motor vehicle dealer license for five years.

 

1497 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gaskins


No. 94CA0743


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION A


923 P.2d 292; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 1; 20 BTR 57



January 25, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 7, 1996. Certiorari Denied September 23, 1996 (96SC213). Released For Publication September 25, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Nancy E. Rice, Judge. No. 87CR1541.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, SENTENCE VACATED, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged an order from the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which found the life sentence imposed upon defendant after his adjudication as a habitual criminal to be disproportionate to defendant's crimes in violation of the cruel and unusual punishment clauses of the United States and Colorado Constitutions and resentenced him to eight years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of felony attempted theft and misdemeanor third degree assault. The jury found defendant to be a habitual criminal based on three prior felony convictions. The trial court sentenced him to life imprisonment as required by Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-13-101(2) (1986). The court vacated the life sentence and remanded for a proportionality review, a decision that was affirmed on certiorari review. The trial court found the sentence to be disproportionate to defendant's crimes and resentenced him to eight years in prison. On appeal, the court affirmed that the sentence was disproportionate but remanded for resentencing. Defendant's crimes were so lacking in gravity and seriousness as to give rise to an inference of sentence disproportionality. The sentence imposed was harsh as compared to the underlying crimes committed and the allowable sentencing for similar offenses in neighboring states. Defendant's sentence was constitutionally disproportionate. The trial court erred in not considering the range of sentences under the "little" habitual criminal statute, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-13-101(1). Sentencing under that statute was one option available to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that defendant's sentence was constitutionally disproportionate, but vacated the sentence imposed by the district court and remanded for resentencing to allow the district court to consider the "little" habitual statute.

 

1498 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Upshur


No. 94CA0551


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


923 P.2d 284; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 4; 20 BTR 53



January 25, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 29, 1996. Certiorari Denied September 3, 1996 (96SC204). Released For Publication September 25, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable Michael J. Heydt, Judge. No. 92CR3028.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of conviction by the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado), entered on a jury verdict, which found defendant guilty of violating the Colorado Organized Crime Control Act (COCCA), conspiracy to violate COCCA, theft, and second degree forgery. Defendant challenged the warrantless search of a storage locker.


OVERVIEW: Based upon reports of suspicious activity concerning a certain locker at a self-storage facility, a police officer was sent to the facility to investigate. The manager explained that defendant, the lessee, had been locked out of his storage unit for failure to pay rent. After consulting his superiors, the officer asked the manager's permission to enter the locker. Upon entry into the locker, the officer saw weapons, left the locker as it was, obtained a search warrant, and seized certain property. Defendant contended that the warrantless search was unreasonable in violation of his Fourth Amendment rights. The trial court found that the officer reasonably believed that the manager had the authority to consent to the search and denied the motion to suppress. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision, holding that the record adequately supported the trial court's ruling on the motion to suppress. The court determined that it was objectively reasonable for the officer to believe that the manager had the authority to enter the locker. The officer reviewed the files, which reflected a history of late payments, delinquent notices, preliminary lien notices, and unpaid rent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized as a result of the warrantless search of his locker.

 

1499 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Pueblo Sch. Dist. No. 70 v. Toth


No. 95CA0189


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


924 P.2d 1094; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 9; 20 BTR 89



January 25, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified Rehearing Denied May 2, 1996. Certiorari Denied October 15, 1996 (96SC315). Cases Released for Publication on Tuesday, October 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 3-878-236. WC No. 3-793-718.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, employer and its insurer, the Colorado Compensation Insurance Authority (collectively referred to as CCIA), sought review of a final order of the panel of the Colorado Industrial Claim Appeals that required CCIA to pay a penalty for its delay in reimbursing claimant employee for medical expenses.


OVERVIEW: The employee was disabled from work-related injuries, and was entitled to reimbursement from CCIA for over-the-counter pain relievers that were prescribed by her doctor. The CCIA regularly reimbursed the employee for the pain relievers, but then missed a requested reimbursement for $ 19.63. The CCIA admitted responsibility for the bill, but did not pay it for over two years. The employee requested a hearing concerning the matter, and the director imposed a penalty of $ 6450, $ 100 per day for 645 days, pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-53-116 (1986 repealed). The court affirmed the assessment of the penalty and held that the assessment was supported by substantial evidence. The court rejected the CCIA's challenge under the due process clause, holding that the CCIA as a government organization did not have standing, and even if it did, that there were adequate procedures for review through the administrative proceedings and the court. The court rejected CCIA's challenge to the penalty under the Eighth Amendment to the United States Constitution and under Article II of the Colorado Constitution, because the CCIA lacked standing and the penalty was not grossly disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the panel that assessed a penalty against the CCIA for refusing to reimburse the employee for a legitimate medical expense.

Stanley v. Creighton Co.


No. 94CA1620


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


911 P.2d 705; 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 19; 20 BTR 73



January 25, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released For Publication March 14, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable Steven T. Pelican, Judge. No. 93CV2412.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenants brought an action against defendant landlord for injuries sustained in a fall. The District Court of El Paso County (Colorado) entered summary judgment in favor of the landlord on the basis of an exculpatory clause included in the residential rental agreement. The tenants challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: In their complaint, tenants, who were husband and wife, alleged that the wife was injured when she slipped on a spot of clear ice and fell down the stairs. Specifically, the tenants alleged that the ice had formed on the landing in front of their apartment because of a negligently repaired leak in the roof. Both parties agreed that the Colorado Actions Against Landowners Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-115 et seq. (1995 Cum. Supp.) governed landlord-tenant premises liability actions. However, in its motion for summary judgment the landlord argued that an exculpatory clause in the lease modified its statutory duty and prohibited all claims except those resulting from gross negligence. The trial court granted summary judgment for the landlord on the ground that the tenants failed to plead or establish a triable issue of fact on that theory. On appeal, the tenants contended that the lease provision was invalid. The court held that the exculpatory clause in the parties' residential rental agreement was void as against the public policy in Colorado.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment rendered in favor of the landlord in the tenants' negligence action and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

Dove Valley Bus. Park Assocs. v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 94CA1883


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


923 P.2d 242; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 356; 19 BTR 1868



December 21, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 25, 1996. Certiorari Granted September 23, 1996 (96SC101). Certiorari Granted on the following issues: Did the court of appeals err in determining that the County's assessment against the taxpayer of redemption interest on erroneously assessed taxes is a constitutionally permissible taking of petitioners' property? Did the court of appeals err in determining that petitioners' equitable claim of unjust enrichment must fail because the county assertedly did not receive a benefit from the taxpayer, did not encourage or initiate the transaction which it benefited from, and is not typically the principal beneficiary of redemption interest? Released For Publication September 25, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Arapahoe County. Honorable Thomas Levi, Judge. No. 93CV2842.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, AND REVERSED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Arapahoe County, (Colorado) that had entered judgment in favor of appellee county officials in a dispute regarding property taxes.


OVERVIEW: Businesses sought review of a declaratory judgment entered by the trial court that dismissed their statutory, constitutional, and equitable claims for interest due from county officials on erroneously assessed property taxes. The businesses owners of commercial real estate failed to pay in a timely manner assessed property taxes. The county officials refused to pay any refund interest or to reimburse the businesses for penalty interest or redemption interest paid by the businesses on the erroneously levied taxes. The court agreed with the businesses that the county must reimburse them for any penalty interest the businesses had paid on the erroneously levied taxes. The court stated to the extent the businesses had redeemed their property, the county had to reimburse the businesses for penalty interest paid on the erroneously levied taxes. The court held when there has been a tax lien sale, refund interest accrues to the taxpayer for erroneously levied taxes and penalty interest, pursuant to statute, from the time that the treasurer received payment from the taxpayer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court relating to the ruling that the county was not obligated to reimburse businesses for penalty interest paid on erroneously levied taxes and affirmed the rest of the judgment, because the penalty interest had been paid on erroneously levied taxes.

Christie v. Coors Transp. Co.


No. 95CA0581


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


919 P.2d 857; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 332; 19 BTR 1754



December 7, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 25, 1996. Certiorari Granted July 1, 1996 (96SC66). Certiorari Granted on the following issues: Did the court of appeals err in failing to find that 8-40-201(16.5)(a), 3B C.R.S. (1995 Supp.), should be interpreted in light of the $4,000 ceiling on earnings in 8-43-303(3), 3B C.R.S. (1995 Supp.), and that under that standard, petitioner cannot earn "any wages"? Did the court of appeals err in failing to find that 8-40-201(16.5)(a), 3B C.R.S. (1995 Supp.), and 8-46-101(1)(a), 3B C.R.S. (1995 Supp.), should be read in pari materia; that petitioner is disabled under the standard set forth in 8-46-101(1)(a); and that if the sections are read instead to set different standards for determining disability under which petitioner is not found to be disabled, the distinction does not meet minimum rationality standards?
Released For Publication July 17, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 4110189.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant sought review of the order of respondent, Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado (Panel), which entered a judgment for respondent employer and denied his claim for permanent total disability (PTD) benefits.


OVERVIEW: The claimant sought PTD benefits after he sustained an industrial back injury. An administrative law judge (ALJ) concluded that the claimant's disability was not total because he retained access to employment opportunities. The Panel affirmed the ALJ's decision. The court held that substantial evidence supported the conclusion that the claimant was able to earn wages. Although the record contained conflicting evidence, the findings made by the ALJ concerning the weight and credibility of the evidence were binding on appeal before both the Panel and the court. Further, for the purposes of the claimant's equal protection claim, the court assumed that the claimant was similarly situated to other claimants who had a PTD, and that he was treated dissimilarly. However, the different legislative classifications for claimants who received a PTD award were rational. Thus, it followed that the adoption of different standards that accounted for those differences was also rational. Accordingly, the definition of a PTD in 1991 Colo. Sess. Laws 219, § 8-40-201(16.5)(a), as interpreted by Colorado case law, did not offend the equal protection guarantees of the U.S. and Colorado Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Panel.

People v. Gardner


No. 93CA1865


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


919 P.2d 850; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 319; 19 BTR 1639



November 24, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 28, 1995. Certiorari Denied June 24, 1996 (96SC54).
Released For Publication July 17, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable Gilbert Martinez, Judge. No. 92CR3351.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado), which convicted her of retaliation against a witness and third degree assault. Defendant contended that her constitutional right to equal protection of the law was violated by an unreasonable statutory scheme under which she was charged.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of retaliation against a witness and third degree assault. Defendant sought review and contended that her constitutional right to equal protection of the law was violated by an unreasonable statutory scheme under which she was charged. The court held that, in order to withstand an equal protection challenge, a statutory classification must have turned on reasonable intelligible standards and determined that harsher penalties for crimes committed under different circumstances were not in violation of equal protection guarantees if the classification was rationally based upon the variety of evil proscribed. The court determined that, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-8-706 (1995 Cum. Supp.), which proscribed retaliation against a witness, and further found that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-8-704 (1996 Repl.), which proscribed intimidating a victim or a witness, proscribed conduct against persons prior to any testimony. The court held that the statutes were factually distinguishable in their application and found that defendant's due process rights had not been violated. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of retaliation against a witness and third degree assault.
