Denver Classroom Teachers Ass'n v. School Dist. No. 1


No. 94CA1177


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


911 P.2d 690; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 325; 19 BTR 1656



November 24, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 11, 1996.
Released For Publication March 14, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable William G. Meyer, Judge. No. 93CV3848.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teachers' union appealed from the summary judgment issued by the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado) for defendant school district and its governing body in a suit for breach of a collective bargaining agreement. The union claimed the district breached the contract and violated policy by not implementing a salary increase and, to the extent relied on, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 22-32-110(5) (1995) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The union contended the school district violated the parties' multi-year collective bargaining agreement by not implementing the final phase of a salary increase for teachers as set forth in that agreement. The school board had asked the union to renegotiate across-the-board salary increases for the last school year of the agreement, due to changed financial circumstances. The union had refused. The parties' cross-motioned for summary judgment. The union's motion was denied. The district's motion was granted. The court affirmed, stating that interpretation of the agreement turned on construction of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 22-32-110(5), which it held was constitutional, as there was a rational relationship between the statute and the need for fiscally sound school districts. It rejected the union's interpretation of the agreement and affirmed the trial court's holding that to interpret the statute to encompass negotiation only on mutual consent would relegate it to a useless act, as all contracts could be reopened on mutual consent. As the union did not respond to the district's request, it had waived its right to renegotiate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The district's construction of the agreement was correct. Under statute, renegotiation of salaries and benefits had to be an available option when either party made a request under the agreement. The statute was not special legislation violating the state constitution.

 

1505 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Wecker v. TBL Excavating


No. 95CA0232


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


908 P.2d 1186; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 327; 19 BTR 1668



November 24, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 4177739.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of an order of respondent, the Colorado Industrial Claims Appeals Office (panel), affirming the denial of his claim for medical benefits by an administrative law judge (ALJ) in his workers' compensation case. He contended that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-43-301(8) denied him procedural due process because it prohibited the panel from altering the ALJ's findings that were supported by substantial evidence.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed a claim for medical benefits to be paid out of workers' compensation. An ALJ denied his claim. The panel affirmed the ALJ's determination. The employee filed an action to challenge the panel's conclusion. The court affirmed, finding that § 8-43-301(8) did not deny the employee procedural due process of law when he indisputably received adequate notice and a full adjudicatory hearing before an ALJ in which he was permitted to present evidence, cross-examine witnesses, examine the employer's evidence, and present argument. Further, in addition to his statutory right to pursue an administrative appeal, he also had the right to judicial review. The employee failed to meet his burden challenging the constitutionality of § 8-43-301(8), which required the panel to review the determination on a substantial evidence standard, because the limited administrative review avoided duplication of effort at the agency level. In addition, it was rationally related to the statutory goal of the Workers' Compensation Act to provide an expeditious method of compensating disabled workers with liability determined with some degree of certainty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the panel's conclusion, affirming the ALJ's denial of the employee's claim for medical benefits for workers' compensation in the employee's action challenging the constitutionality of the panel's limited administrative review of the ALJ's determination.

 

1506 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


U S West Communs. v. City of Longmont


No. 94CA1102


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


924 P.2d 1071; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 314



November 16, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 11, 1996. Certiorari Granted October 15, 1996 (96SC75). Certiorari Granted on the following issues: Whether the court of appeals erred when it found that Ordinance 9-93-02 is neither inconsistent with Tariff 4.6 nor preempted under the Filed Tariff Doctrine. Whether the court of appeals erred when it found that the general jurisdiction of the Public Utilities Commission over the facilities, services, rates, and charges of U S West does not preempt a municipal ordinance requiring U S West to replace, solely at its own cost, its existing overhead facilities with underground facilities. Whether the court of appeals erred when it found that an ordinance requiring the replacement of overhead telephone facilities underground was not a taking under either the United States or Colorado Constitutions. Cases Released for Publication on Tuesday, October 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Boulder County. Honorable Joseph J. Bellipanni, Judge. No. 93CV281.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff telephone company sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Boulder County (Colorado) which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant city upholding the validity of an ordinance which required owners and operators of existing overhead facilities used for distribution of electricity and transmission or distribution of communications to relocate such facilities underground at their own cost.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff telephone company brought suit pursuant to Colo. R. Civ. P. 106(a)(4) and for declaratory judgment challenging an ordinance enacted by defendant city. Defendant had enacted an ordinance that required the owners and operators of existing overhead facilities used for distribution of electricity and transmission or distribution of communications to relocate such facilities underground at their own expense. Plaintiff contended that the ordinance was preempted, that the application of the ordinance resulted in an unconstitutional taking, that defendant exceeded its jurisdiction and abused its discretion in enacting the ordinance, and that defendant breached a pole sharing agreement. The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant because the ordinance was a valid exercise of the defendant's police power. The court determined that the ordinance did not conflict with state law and was not preempted. The court concluded that the ordinance was not an unconstitutional taking of property and did not constitute a breach of the pole sharing agreement, and that defendant did not exceed its authority in enacting it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment against plaintiff telephone company. The court uphold an ordinance requiring the relocation of overhead facilities underground as a valid exercise of the defendant city's police power. The court concluded that state law or regulation did not preempt the ordinance and that the ordinance did not result in an unconstitutional taking or a breach of the pole sharing agreement.

 

1507 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hansen


No. 93CA1133


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


920 P.2d 831; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 310; 19 BTR 1574



November 9, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing of Defendant-Appellant DENIED.
Opinion Modified, and as Modified Rehearing Denied December 21, 1995. Certiorari Denied August 19, 1996.
Released For Publication August 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Henry E. Nieto, Judge. No. 92CR1422.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the District Court of Jefferson County (Colorado), which convicted him of sexual assault on a child as part of a pattern of sexual abuse.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with sexual assault on a neighbor girl, incest with his son, and a sexual assault as part of a pattern of sexual abuse for alleged sexual assaults on his son. Defendant was convicted of only the pattern of sexual abuse. Defendant contested the failure to require the state to elect a specific, predicate act on which to base the pattern of sexual assault and the admission of hearsay statements of his son. The court affirmed the judgment. Because the trial court instructed that jury that it had to unanimously agree on two or more of the same acts and the jury could have found acts of sexual assault other than the charged incest offense, the court concluded that the failure to require an election of the acts did not contribute to defendant's conviction and was not plain error. The court found no abuse of discretion in the admission of the son's hearsay statements when the trial court made findings on the reliability factors provided for in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-25-129 (1987) for the admission of such hearsay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against defendant for sexual assault as a part of a pattern of sexual abuse for acts of sexual assault upon his son.

 

1508 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Borquez v. Robert C. Ozer, P.C.


No. 93CA1805


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


923 P.2d 166; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 302; 11 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 496; 69 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1415; 19 BTR 1579



November 9, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 7, 1995. Certiorari Granted September 16, 1996 (96SC13). Certiorari Granted on the following issues: Whether the court of appeals erred in holding that the jury verdict on wrongful discharge based on sexual orientation was supportable as a violation of 24-34-402.5(a), 10A C.R.S. (1996 Supp.). Whether the court of appeals erred in recognizing an invasion of privacy tort claim based on Restatement (Second) of Torts 652D (1976) (unreasonable publicity given to the life of another). Whether the court of appeals correctly held that the jury was properly instructed on the invasion of privacy tort claim. Released For Publication September 25, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable J. Stephen Phillips, Judge. No. 92CV5806.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, former employers, challenged the judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver in favor of appellee former employee in a suit for wrongful discharge based upon sexual orientation. Former employee cross appealed the decision of the district court which denied his request for attorney fees and costs.


OVERVIEW: Former employee, an attorney, was discharged days after he notified his former employers that he was gay and that his companion had been diagnosed with AIDS. Former employee filed suit against former employers alleging wrongful discharge based upon sexual orientation and invasion of privacy. The jury entered a verdict in favor of former employee and former employers appealed. Former employee appealed the lower court's denial of his request for costs and attorney fees. The court held that the evidence supported the conclusion that former employers discharged defendant based upon lawful activity in which he engaged during his off-work hours in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-34-402.5. The court also found that there was sufficient evidence to support the claim for invasion of privacy in the form of unreasonable publicity given to the life of another. The court held that the district court erred in failing to award attorney fees and costs pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-102(1)(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in all respects except the portion of the judgment denying attorney fees and costs.

 

1509 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Donald B. Murphy Contrs. v. Industrial Claim Appeals Office


No. 94CA1597


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


916 P.2d 611; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 269; 19 BTR 1427



September 21, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified Rehearing Denied November 24, 1995. Certiorari Denied April 29, 1996 (95SC758).
Released For Publication May 21, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 3-101-889.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED IN PART, SET ASIDE IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appealed an order from respondent Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado (Panel), which affirmed the findings by the administrative law judge (ALJ) that respondent claimant was entitled to temporary total disability benefits.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners paid the claimant temporary total disability benefits after the claimant's physician determined that he had reached maximum medical improvement, and then paid permanent partial benefits to the limit set in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-42-107.5 (1994 Cum. Supp.). Subsequently, the claimant's condition worsened and he needed additional surgery. The claimant sought additional temporary total disability benefits. Petitioners objected, but the Panel affirmed the finding by the ALJ that the worsened condition was related to the admitted injury and determined that the claimant was entitled to temporary total disability benefits because a medical impairment rating in § 8-42-107.5 was prematurely applied. The court set aside part of the order. The court found that when further benefits were sought after the limit of § 8-42-107.5 had been applied, petitioners are entitled to offset any permanent partial benefits paid against temporary total disability benefits. The court held that there was substantial evidence to support the conclusion by the ALJ that the need for surgery was a direct result of the work-related injury.


OUTCOME: The court set aside that portion of the Panel's order that required petitioners to pay temporary total disability benefits and remanded with instructions to grant petitioners a credit for permanent partial disability benefits already paid against the temporary total disability benefits. The remainder of the order was affirmed.

 

1510 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Dewey v. Hardy


No. 94CA0490


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


917 P.2d 305; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 259; 19 BTR 1398



September 14, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 19, 1995. Certiorari Denied May 28, 1996 (95SC707).
Released For Publication June 12, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] THIS OPINION IS NOT THE FINAL VERSION AND IS SUBJECT .Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable David D. Parrish, Judge. No. 92CV2648.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART VACATED IN PART AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant litigants appealed the decision of the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado), which entered judgment upon a jury verdict in favor of plaintiff father for recovery under the solatium statute, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-203.5 (1994 Cum. Supp.). Prior to electing to proceed under the statute, the father had instituted a wrongful death action for his child's death. The father cross-appealed a post-verdict reduction in his damages.


OVERVIEW: After the father's motion to elect recovery of solatium was granted, a trial began to determine whether the litigants were liable. Prior to trial, the litigants had challenged the statute's constitutionality, however, the trial court did not rule on the issue. A jury found the litigants 65 percent at fault and the child 35 percent at fault, and the trial court denied the litigants' request to reduce the award in proportion to the amount of comparative negligence. The trial court did, however, reduce the father's award by half to reflect the mother's right to half of the award. The statute was constitutional because a full civil trial was required to determine liability, thus satisfying due process. The statutory fixed award of $ 50,000 was not an excessive amount offensive to the concept of due process. The comparative negligence statute, a general statute, was not applicable to the solatium statute, a specific statute. Therefore, a reduction to account for the child's negligence was not required. The court vacated the reduction of the father's award because two required, but absent, parties, the insurer and the child's mother, were not parties to the present action.


OUTCOME: The court vacated that portion of the judgment in favor of the father and parties not before the court. The cause was remanded to the trial court for joinder of all parties claiming an interest in the solatium and for further proceedings concerning the entitlement of any parties to such an award. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

Bell & Pollock, P.C. v. City of Littleton


No. 94CA0674


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


910 P.2d 69; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 226; 19 BTR 1316



August 10, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 7, 1995. Certiorari Denied February 20, 1996 (95SC642).
Released For Publication February 21, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Arapahoe County. Honorable Thomas Levi, Judge. No. 91CV1717.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Arapahoe County (Colorado), which upheld the constitutionality of defendant city's use tax ordinance, Littleton, Colo., City Code § 3-9-1-1 et seq., and dismissed the taxpayer's action challenging the city's collection of past due use taxes, interest, and penalties from the taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: When the city assessed the taxpayer for unpaid use taxes, penalties, and interest, the taxpayer protested the assessment and requested a hearing. After a hearing officer upheld the city's assessment, the taxpayer filed a complaint. The trial court dismissed all claims for relief except the taxpayer's constitutional challenge to the use tax ordinance. The trial court found that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague. On appeal the court affirmed, holding that the taxpayer failed to meet its burden of proving the unconstitutionality of the use tax ordinance under Colo. Const. art. II, § 25 on the ground of vagueness because: (1) the provisions of Littleton, Colo., City Code §§ 3-9-6-3, 3-9-1-4, 3-9-1-2 provided that the purchase or acquisition of personal property triggered the exercise of a taxable privilege and furnished the date that the liability for the tax arose; and (2) Littleton, Colo., City Code § 3-9-6-12 required a return to be filed at the time the tax was paid and Littleton, Colo., City Code § 3-9-3-5 required the simultaneous filing of a return and payment of the tax when the triggering event of purchase or acquisition of tangible personal property occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment upholding the constitutionality of the city's use tax ordinance and dismissing the claims asserted by the taxpayer.

 

1512 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Norsby v. Jensen


No. 93CA2158


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


916 P.2d 555; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 212; 19 BTR 1244



July 13, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 17, 1995. Certiorari Denied April 22, 1996 (95SC599). Released for Publication May 21, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Chaffee County. Honorable Kenneth M. Plotz, Judge. No. 93CV18.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner challenged a judgment by the District Court of Chaffee County (Colorado), which dismissed his negligence action to recover damages for personal injuries against appellees, Department of Corrections, the state, and prison officials (DOC), because the DOC was immune from liability under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-27.7-103(1).


OVERVIEW: A prisoner filed an action for negligence to recover damages for personal injuries he sustained while in the Regimented Inmate Discipline and Treatment Program (program). The district court dismissed the action on the grounds that the DOC was immune from liability for injuries sustained in the program under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-27.7-103(1). The prisoner appealed and the court affirmed. The court held that the immunity provision in § 17-27.7-103(1) was clear and prevailed in this case, even though the statute conflicted with the Governmental Immunity Act (GIA), Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-10-106(1)(b). The court held that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-27.7-103(1) prevailed because it was enacted after the GIA and it was the more specific statute. The court then rejected the prisoner's argument that § 17-27.7-103(1) was unconstitutional and violative of the Equal Protection Clause. The court held that because no fundamental right or suspect class was involved, under a "rational basis" test, the immunity provision, which limited tort recovery, was rationally related to the government's interest in fiscal certainty and at the same time, rehabilitating nonviolent offenders.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the prisoner's negligence action because the DOC was statutorily immune from liability.

 

1513 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Hill v. City of Lakewood


No. 94CA0856


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


911 P.2d 670; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 217; 19 BTR 1265



July 13, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 17, 1995. Certiorari Denied February 26, 1996 (95SC593).
Released For Publication March 14, 1996. Certiorari Granted February 24, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 1282.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Gaspar F. Perricone, Judge. No. 93CV1984.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff abortion protestors appealed a decision from the District Court of Jefferson County (Colorado) that granted summary judgment to defendants, city and state officials, and determined that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-9-122(3) (Cum. Supp. 1994) did not violate the abortion protestors' free speech rights under the First Amendment to the U.S. Constitution when it barred them from approaching a person within eight feet without prior consent.


OVERVIEW: The abortion protestors argued that they were counselors who offered abortion alternatives and that it was impossible to counsel from that distance and continue the protesting. On appeal, the court affirmed the entry of summary judgment for the city and the state officials. The court reasoned that the statute applied to public sidewalks and streets, which were areas protected by the First Amendment. The statute was content-neutral because the specific viewpoint of the protestor was not relevant to a determination of whether a violation occurred. The government was allowed to impose reasonable restrictions on the time, place, or manner of speech. The statute was not overbroad and did not infringe upon free speech rights any more than necessary to accomplish the goal of providing access to health care facilities. The statute was not constitutionally vague because a person of ordinary intelligence would understand what type of conduct was prohibited. The statute was not an unconstitutional prior restraint on speech because the doctrine applied to governmental authority to permit activities in a public authority and did not apply to impose limits on public citizens.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment for the city and the state officials in determining that the statute was constitutional.

 

1514 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Marez


No. 93CA0382


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


916 P.2d 543; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 196; 19 BTR 1153



June 29, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 7, 1995. Certiorari Denied May 20, 1996 (95SC643). Released for Publication May 21, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Edward A. Simons, Judge. No. 92CR104.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions from the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado) for second degree assault and reckless endangerment. Defendant contended that the district court erred in denying his several motions to suppress physical evidence, statements and identifications allegedly obtained as a result of his warrantless arrest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of four counts of second degree assault and one count of reckless endangerment and contended that the district court erred in denying his motions to suppress physical evidence and statements obtained as a result of his warrantless arrest. The evidence showed that defendant's brother was involved in a fight outside an apartment and at some point, defendant pulled out a gun and began firing into a crowd that had gathered, wounding one man. The court reversed defendant's convictions and remanded the case for a new trial. The court concluded that the district court erred in finding that an emergency situation existed prior to defendant's arrest since the circumstances did not demonstrate a colorable claim of an imminent crisis or danger to the public. As such, the warrantless arrest was unlawful and the gun found in defendant's motel room was inadmissible as evidence in the new trial. The court found that the mandatory sentencing provisions to defendant's second degree assault violated his right of equal protection because it punished him more severely than if he were convicted of attempted first degree assault, a crime requiring a more culpable intent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgments of conviction against defendant for second degree assault and reckless endangerment. The court remanded the cause for a new trial with directions that the district court prohibit the gun found in defendant's motel room from being admitted into evidence.

Colorado AFL-CIO v. Donlon


No. 93CA1118, No. 93CA1392


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


914 P.2d 396; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 184; 19 BTR 1019



June 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified, Petition for Rehearing of Defendant-Appellee Colorado Compensation Authority DENIED.
Petition for Rehearing of Defendants-Appellees Departments of Labor & Employment and Administration DENIED.
Petition for Rehearing of Plaintiffs-Appellants DENIED.
Opinion Modified, and as Modified Rehearing Denied July 13, 1995. Certiorari Denied April 1, 1996 (95SC478). Released for Publication April 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable John N. McMullen, Judge. No. 92CV1889.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, employees and union (employees), challenged the decision from the District Court for the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which dismissed their consolidated declaratory judgment actions seeking a declaration that various provisions of the 1991 amendments to the Workers' Compensation Act (Act), Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-41-401(1)(1994), unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: One of the employees had been employed by a contractor who was building a new home and was seriously injured. Prior to its amendment in 1991, the Act provided that an owner of property, who contracted for work to be done on that property, was to be considered a statutory employer of the contractor and of his employees, and it provided that the owner of a "private home" would be excepted from this provision. The 1991 amendments to the Act, § Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-41-402(1)(1994), changed the term "private home" to "residential real property." The employees argued that this amendment violated equal protection guarantees by distinguishing between properties that were encumbered and those that were not and by providing workers' compensation benefits only to those workers who were employed upon unencumbered residences. The court disagreed and affirmed the dismissal. However, the court held that the other employees' request for a declaratory judgment should have been granted because the provision of the amendment that created an age cap of the disability payments, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-42-111(5), violated the employees' right to equal protection by discriminating against the older worker.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the district court judgment determining that the statute was constitutional and the cause was remanded to that court for the entry of an appropriate declaratory decree. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

Celebrity Custom Builders v. Industrial Claim Appeals Office


No. 94CA1937


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


916 P.2d 539; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 192; 19 BTR 1057



June 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified. Rehearing Denied October 12, 1995. Certiorari Denied April 22, 1996 (95SC657). Released for Publication May 21, 1996. Opinion Modified, and As Modified. Petition for Rehearing Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 4150406.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, employer and insurer, sought review of an order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado (panel), which reversed an order of the Administrative Law Judge (ALJ) and ordered that respondent claimant's average weekly wage, and therefore his temporary disability benefits, should be increased to reflect the cost of the health insurance that the claimant had purchased.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was awarded temporary benefits after suffering a work-related injury but was terminated from his employment when he refused an employment offer. He required more surgery, so his benefits resumed. He sought an increase in his average weekly wage because he had to pay for health insurance. The ALJ determined that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-40-201(19) (1994 Cum. Supp.) was unconstitutional because it was preempted by Employee Retirement Income Security Act (ERISA), 29 U.S.C.S. §§ 1001, et seq., and denied the claimant's request. The panel reversed the ruling and ordered an increase in benefits. Petitioners sought review, and the claimant filed a motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court affirmed the panel's order, holding that there was no preemption and denying the motion to dismiss because the proper forum to challenge the validity of the Workers' Compensation Act was in the district court and that an administrative agency had no authority to determine constitutional issues. The court concluded that the prevailing wage law was not preempted by ERISA and that the cost of the replacement health plan should be included in the calculation of the claimant's average weekly wage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the panel's order, which increased the claimant's benefits, in petitioner's appeal asserting an ERISA preemption of statute in the Workers' Compensation Act.

 

1517 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. City of Central


No. 94CA0943


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


907 P.2d 701; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 168; 19 BTR 919



June 1, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 29, 1995. Certiorari Denied December 4, 1995 (95SC493).
Released For Publication December 21, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Gilpin County. Honorable Kenneth E. Barnhill, Jr., Judge. No. 94CV7.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a special use permit zoning applicant, challenged the judgment from the District Court of Gilpin County (Colorado), which dismissed his claims against defendant city for regulatory taking and inverse condemnation. He claimed that the city's interim moratorium on development in its gaming district resulted in a compensable temporary taking of his real property.


OVERVIEW: In a dispute over a special use permit zoning application, the trial court had dismissed the entire action for failure to state a claim for relief. The trial court reasoned that the temporary suspension of special use permits was not a compensable temporary taking under the Fifth Amendment and that, because the moratorium had been repealed, the inverse condemnation claim would not have been ripe until the applicant had attempted unsuccessfully to obtain a special use permit. The court agreed with the trial court on both issues and held that: 1) because the zoning applicant's claim for inverse condemnation, to the extent that it was based on a permanent regulatory taking, was not ripe for review, the trial court had correctly dismissed his claims against the city; and 2) the city's temporary limitation on property use, resulting from the otherwise good faith, reasonable institution of a moratorium in order to bring about effective governmental decisionmaking, did not result in a categorical taking.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, because the city had not committed a compensable temporary taking of the applicant's real property.

 

1518 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Partridge v. State


No. 93CA2224


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


895 P.2d 1183; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 115; 19 BTR 638



April 20, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 13, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Colorado Racing Commission. No. 9338.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant horse owner challenged an order of appellee Colorado Racing Commission, which ordered that the funds that the horse owner placed in escrow be forwarded to the judgment creditor and that the suspension of the horse owner's owner/trainer license for his violation of 4 Colo. Codes Regs. § 724-1 (1994) be rescinded on the release of the escrowed funds.


OVERVIEW: The Colorado Racing Commission issued an order that required the horse owner to transfer the funds that he placed in escrow to the judgment creditor and based the rescission of the suspension, which resulted from a violation of 4 Colo. Codes Regs. § 724-1 (1994), on that transfer. The court affirmed that order on appeal. The court concluded that the commission validly acted under its authority pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-60-507(1)(a) (1994 Cum. Supp.), which provided for disciplining a licensee for disregarding or violating any rule such as 4 Colo. Codes Regs. § 724-1 (1994) that the commission promulgated in the interests of the public and in conformance with the provisions of the applicable law. The court also held that 4 Colo. Codes Regs. § 724-1 (1994) fostered honesty and fair dealing in the racing industry by requiring the financial integrity of licensees and that it enhanced the sport's commercial benefits by mandating licensees to operate in a businesslike manner. The court further found that the record as a whole supported the commission's ruling.


OUTCOME: The trial court affirmed an order of the Colorado Racing Commission that required the horse owner to give the judgment debtor the funds that the horse owner placed in escrow and that made the recission of the suspension of the horse owner's license contingent on that transfer.

 

1519 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Cespedes


No. 94CA0711


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


895 P.2d 1172; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 121; 19 BTR 651



April 20, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 13, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Morris B. Hoffman, Judge. No. 78 00 D76342.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado) entered an order, in a post-dissolution of marriage action, directed to appellant father for increased child support, postsecondary education support, and attorney fees payable to appellee mother. The father appealed the order.


OVERVIEW: The father contended that the mother could not properly file her motions for increased child support because she was receiving public assistance for families with dependant children and had thus assigned all her rights to receive support for her children to the department of human services. The court affirmed. The court found that the mother was the real party in interest because: (1) only part of the mother's right to receive child support had been assigned; (2) Colo. Rev. Stat. § 14-14-104(2) allowed a custodial parent to seek an increase in child support which included the amount of public assistance received, provided that any such increase was subject to the state's right to subrogation; and (3) Colo. Rev. Stat. § 26-13-121(8) provided specific statutory authorization for a custodial parent receiving public assistance to seek an increase in child support. The court further found that: (1) the mother was the real party in interest concerning the motion for postsecondary education support because either the parent or the child may move for such an order; and (2) the trial court made adequate findings in regard to that order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order directed to the father for increased child support, postsecondary education support, and attorney fees payable to the mother. The cause was remanded for further proceedings on the mother's request for attorney fees incurred in the appeal.

 

1520 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Deskins


No. 93CA0750


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


904 P.2d 1358; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 92; 19 BTR 482



March 23, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 4, 1995. Certiorari Granted October 30, 1995 (95SC360). Certiorari Granted on the following issues: Whether the defendant who faced both substantive charges and habitual criminal charges, was adequately advised of his right to testify. Whether the court of appeals erred in holding that reckless child abuse does not require an awareness by the accused that his conduct could result in injury to a child rather than an adult.
Released for Publication November 16, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Garfield County. Honorable Thomas W. Ossola, Judge. No. 92CR135.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the District Court of Garfield County (Colorado), which convicted defendant of child abuse resulting in death, vehicular homicide; vehicular assault, driving under the influence, and child abuse resulting in serious bodily harm. The trial court also adjudicated defendant a habitual criminal.


OVERVIEW: Three children were killed, and another child and a woman were seriously injured, when defendant's car collided with a vehicle occupied by the victims. Defendant was convicted of child abuse resulting in death, vehicular homicide, vehicular assault, driving under the influence, and child abuse resulting in serious bodily harm. He was adjudicated a habitual criminal. The court held that sufficient evidence supported the child abuse convictions because, when a person acted recklessly and when that conduct by happenstance injured or killed a child, criminal liability attached under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-401(7)(a)(I), (III) (Repl. Vol. 1986). However, the trial court did not advise defendant that his prior convictions were admissible only for the limited purpose of credibility. Thus, absent an adequate advisement of his right to testify, defendant's waiver of that right could not be considered voluntary, knowing, and intentional, and defendant's convictions could not stand. Further, defendant was not barred from challenging the constitutionality of a pertinent prior conviction. Finally, the evidence was insufficient to support two of the six habitual criminal counts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision convicting defendant of various forms of child abuse, vehicular homicide, vehicular assault, and driving under the influence. The cause was remanded for a new trial on all charges except two of the habitual criminal counts. The trial court was directed to review defendant's collateral attack on the validity of his allegedly unconstitutional prior convictions in light of Colorado case law.

 

1521 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Finer


No. 94CA0178


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


893 P.2d 1381; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 78; 19 BTR 515



March 23, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended April 13, 1995.
Released For Publication May 18, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Arapahoe County. Honorable Michael L. Bieda, Judge. No. 92DR2324.



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order of the District Court of Arapahoe County (Colorado), which refused to hold a hearing to modify the temporary injunction imposed by Colo. Rev. Stat. § 14-10-107(4)(b)(I) (1987) that prevented removal of her minor child from the state.


OVERVIEW: The temporary injunction was automatically imposed upon the filing of the mother's petition for dissolution of marriage and she sought to modify it in order to accept employment in another state. The court found that the automatic creation of the temporary injunction by statute was an appealable order because it was equivalent to a preliminary injunction. Pursuant to Colo. App. R. 1(a)(3), the court had jurisdiction over judgments of district courts where appeals could lie, including orders that granted or denied preliminary injunctions. Although the temporary injunction had expired, the appeal was not moot because the underlying substantive question concerning the district court's authority required adjudication of constitutional issues that could recur yet escape judicial review. The court held that the trial court's refusal to hold the hearing violated the mother's right to due process because the risk of an erroneous deprivation of her interest in her rights to travel and to pursue employment opportunities was substantial. Overcrowded dockets did not justify the denial because the hearing would not have been a significant burden.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed.

 

1522 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bowring


No. 93CA1672


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


902 P.2d 911; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 89; 19 BTR 503



March 23, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Bowring v. People, 1995 Colo. LEXIS 874 (Colo., Sept. 25, 1995)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by, Certificate of appealability denied Bowring v. Zavaras, 172 F.3d 878, 1999 U.S. App. LEXIS 11492 (10th Cir. Colo., 1999)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Bowring v. Milyard, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 67067 (D. Colo., June 23, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] THIS OPINION IS NOT THE FINAL VERSION AND IS SUBJECT .Appeal from the District Court of Larimer County. Honorable John-David Sullivan, Judge. No. 92CR424.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, SENTENCE VACATED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a conviction from the District Court of Larimer County (Colorado) for sexual assault on a child as a pattern of sexual abuse and aggravated incest. He also appealed the sentence imposed, which, in addition to being sentenced to two concurrent terms in the Colorado Department of Corrections, was ordered to pay sex offender surcharges on each count pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 18-21-103 (1994 Cum. Supp.), 24-4.2-104.


OVERVIEW: The offenses for which defendant was convicted were based on evidence of defendant's sexual contact with his 13-year-old daughter. The court affirmed the judgment The pattern sexual abuse statute, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-405(2)(c) (1994 Cum. Supp.) did not violate defendant's due process rights because the evidence, multiple incidents of sexual abuse, formed an internal part of the offense with which defendant was charged, so no limiting instructions were required. The statute did not violate defendant's equal protection rights, by reclassifying the offense for sentence enhancement purposes, because the classification had a rational basis. First, it acknowledged the difficulty young children had referencing time. Second, defendant's pattern of conduct merited greater punishment because of its greater social consequence. Because defendant's conduct occurred after the pattern sexual abuse statute's effective date, the statute was not retroactive and did not violate the ex post facto prohibition. The court vacated that part of defendant's sentence that imposed surcharges under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-21-103 because the statute's effective date predated the date of the offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for pattern sexual abuse and aggravated incest, but vacated the sentence in part and remand with directions.

Sundheim v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 93CA1324, No. 93CA1891


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


904 P.2d 1337; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 75; 19 BTR 387



March 9, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 20, 1995. Certiorari Granted November 14, 1995 (95SC330). Certiorari Granted on the following issues: Whether Colorado's Constitution affords remedies similar to 42 U.S.C. 1983, and if so, whether petitioners' state constitutional claims should be treated similarly to their 1983 claims. Whether the court of appeals correctly ruled that money damages claims under 42 U.S.C. 1983 may be brought separately regardless of the status of a C.R.C.P. 106(a)(4) action.
Released for Publication November 16, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Douglas County. Honorable Thomas J. Curry, Judge. No. 91CV720.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Douglas County (Colorado), which dismissed their claims and granted summary judgment for defendants, county officials and adjoining property owners, for civil rights violations of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1985 and for invasion of privacy, claiming that defendant county officials arbitrarily and capriciously denied their application for a special use permit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant adjoining property owners opposed, and defendant county officials denied, plaintiff property owners' application for a special use permit to operate a horse training business. Plaintiffs filed an action alleging due process, equal protection, and privacy violations, and a conspiracy to deprive them of their civil rights. The court affirmed the trial court for the most part, however, it reversed the dismissal of plaintiffs' substantive due process claim. The validity of the claim depended on a strong likelihood that the permit would have been granted absent the conduct complained of. Plaintiffs claimed that defendant county officials applied an unusual standard of review to their permit application and that but for the arbitrary and capricious refusal to follow an existing administrative standard, the application would have been granted. The court concluded that the complaint alleged both an entitlement to a favorable outcome and an arbitrary and irrational government action and, accordingly, dismissal of that claim was not warranted. The court also remanded for a redetermination on the issue of attorney's fees on their claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the grant by the trial court of summary judgment for defendants, county officials and adjoining property owners, in plaintiff property owners' action for constitutional and civil rights violations, but it reversed the dismissal of plaintiffs' substantive due process claims because a claim that defendant county officials arbitrarily and capriciously denied their special use permit raised issues of fact for a jury.

People v. Hilton


No. 94CA0457


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


902 P.2d 883; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 53; 19 BTR 321



February 23, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] THIS OPINION IS NOT THE FINAL VERSION AND IS SUBJECT .Appeal from the District Court of Arapahoe County. Honorable James F. Macrum, Jr. Judge. No. 87CR1367.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the District Court of Arapahoe County (Colorado), which denied defendant's motion for release from the Colorado Department of Institutions (DOI) after defendant was found not guilty by reason of impaired mental condition and was committed to the custody of the DOI.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that defendant was not eligible for release because he had an abnormal mental condition that was likely to cause him to be dangerous if released. On appeal the court affirmed, holding that: (1) the trial court did not err in concluding that defendant suffered from an abnormal mental condition because the phrase "abnormal mental condition," as used in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-8-120(4), was construed to include a severe antisocial personality disorder; (2) § 16-8-120 was not unconstitutionally vague because the word "dangerousness," as used in the statute, was specific enough to satisfy due process; (3) the trial court properly determined that defendant was likely to be a danger to himself or the community because the determination was supported by the record; and (4) the trial court properly shifted the burden of proving eligibility for release to defendant because Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-8-115(2) provided for a burden shift once any evidence was introduced that a defendant was not eligible for release and the State introduced evidence that defendant was not eligible for release due to an abnormal mental condition that was likely to cause him to be dangerous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying defendant's request for release from the DOI.

 

1525 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Cuny v. Vail Assocs.


No. 93CA1869


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


902 P.2d 881; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 66; 19 BTR 308



February 23, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] THIS OPINION IS NOT THE FINAL VERSION AND IS SUBJECT .Appeal from the District Court of Eagle County. Honorable William L. Jones, Judge. No. 93CV124.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bobsledder appealed an order from the District Court of Eagle County (Colorado), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant ski resort in the bobsledder's personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: The bobsledder was injured while riding on a bobsled furnished by the ski resort. Prior to the ride, the bobsledder signed a release exculpating the resort from any injuries suffered as a result of the resort's negligence. The release did not exculpate "gross negligence or willful misconduct." The bobsledder brought a personal injury action against the ski resort. Prior to filing an answer to the complaint, the ski resort filed a motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim or, in the alternative, for summary judgment, arguing that the claims were barred by the release and the Colorado Ski Safety and Liability Act (Act), Colo. Rev. Stat. § 33-44-101 et seq. (1984 Repl.). Before responding to that motion, the bobsledder filed a motion to amend his complaint. The trial court granted summary judgment for the resort and denied the bobsledder's motion to amend his complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the Act applied to a bobsled run operated as part of a ski resort and because crashing was an inherent risk of bobsledding, the claims were not actionable under the Act. Because summary judgment was proper, the trial court did not err in denying the motion to amend.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment dismissing a bobsledder's negligence action against a ski resort as well as the trial court's order denying the bobsledder's motion to amend his complaint.

 

1526 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gardenhire


No. 93CA0221


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


903 P.2d 1159; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 35; 19 BTR 185



February 9, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] THIS OPINION IS NOT THE FINAL VERSION AND IS SUBJECT .Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Richard T. Spriggs, Judge. No. 92CR629.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the District Court, City and County of Denver (Colorado), which convicted defendant for first degree murder, second degree murder, first degree kidnapping, second degree assault, and the crime of violence. Alleged errors included a Batson challenge, the denial of a motion to sever, a claim of publicity influencing the jury, and the admission of a co-defendant's statements.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried with the co-defendant, his father. Defendant and his co-defendant were first granted 15 peremptory challenges. After exercising one, they could not agree so the trial court gave them seven each. Defendant contended that his equal protection rights were violated because he did not receive as many peremptory challenges as if he were tried alone. On appeal, the court found no errors. Peremptory challenges were not a constitutional right, and the State could have passed a statute dividing up such challenges in a manner to equalize the challenges offered both sides. There was no error in failing to grant defendant 12 challenges. Defendant's motion to sever was denied because his co-defendant's statement that they were going to "take care of" a thief was admissible as the statement of a co-conspirator. The Batson claim failed because defendant failed to make a prima facie case, and even if he did, the State rebutted it. Failing to poll the jury on pre-trial publicity was not an error when only one juror mentioned reading an article, the report did not concern defendant, and there was no reason to believe that polling would have been helpful.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

Guest Mansions v. Arapahoe County Bd. of Equalization


No. 93CA1094


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


899 P.2d 944; 1995 Colo. App. LEXIS 6; 19 BTR 4



January 12, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 9, 1995. Certiorari Denied August 14, 1995 (95SC177).
Released For Publication August 14, 1995.
As Amended September 28, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Arapahoe County. Honorable Michael J. Watanabe, Judge. No. 90CV3834.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review from a judgment of the District Court (Colorado), which held that the corporation's leasehold interest in property owned by the Arapahoe County Public Airport Authority was subject to a possessory interest tax under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 39-3-135 (1994).


OVERVIEW: The corporation leased a hotel and realty at an airport from the Authority. In 1988, the Board of Equalization determined that the corporation's possessory interest was exempt from taxation. In 1990, the Board determined that the possessory interest was taxable under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 39-3-135 (1994). The trial court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed. Collateral estoppel did not bind the Assessor to the Board's tax decision made in a prior tax year. Although there was some support for the corporation's argument that it was exempt from taxation because its use of the hotel facilities was "directly related to the ordinary function" of the airport, the corporation did not meet its burden to overcome the strong presumption against exemptions. There was no clear indication in the legislative history that hotels were exempt as directly related to the ordinary function of the airport. The court further held that taxation of a possessory interest in publicly-owned, tax-exempt property did not violate Colo. Cons. art. X, § 4.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Kiewit W. Co. v. City & County of Denver


No. 93CA1160


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


902 P.2d 421; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 392; 18 BTR 2236



December 29, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 9, 1995. Certiorari Denied September 25, 1995 (95SC233). Released for Publication September 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable H. Jeffrey Bayless, Judge. No. 92CV8100.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractor appealed from a judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which dismissed its complaint for declaratory and other relief against defendants, city, county, the Department of Public Works, and its acting manager. Plaintiff asserted 14 claims for relief. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss pursuant to Colo. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(5), which the trial court granted based on the parties' submissions.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff contractor bid and won two major contracts with defendants, city, county, Department of Public Works, and its acting manager. The contracts included provisions allowing plaintiff to receive additional compensation subject to time limits for submitting change orders. If denied, the contract set out a dispute resolution process, including an administrative hearing. Plaintiff could request managerial review of the hearing officer's decision, and if approved, judicial review was available under Colo. R. Civ. P. 106. Plaintiff contractor asserted 14 claims against defendants, whose motion to dismiss under Colo. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(5) was granted. The court affirmed. Contract estoppel barred the claims that the dispute resolution procedures were ultra vires, and neither Colo. Const. art. XX, § 1 nor the Denver City Charter expressly precluded them. Further, the procedures were valid and binding absent fraud or bad faith by the government, and they did not violate due process. Finally, the court held that the contract provisions were unambiguous and that the claims of fraudulent inducement and breach of good faith and fair dealing should have been resolved under those procedures.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that contract estoppel barred plaintiff contractor's claim that the contractual procedures were unauthorized, and that plaintiff failed to state a claim for violation of due process. The court held that the contract was not ambiguous, and that plaintiff's claims for fraud in the inducement and breach of good faith and fair dealing should have been resolved pursuant to the contract's dispute resolution procedures.

People v. Method


No. 93CA1512


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


900 P.2d 1282; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 370; 18 BTR 2105



December 15, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended.
Opinion Modified, and as Modified Rehearing Denied February 9, 1995. Certiorari Denied July 31, 1995 (95SC181).
Released For Publication August 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable James D. Zimmerman, Judge. No. 89CR1467.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the District Court of Jefferson County (Colorado), which denied his motion to withdraw his guilty plea to felony theft.


OVERVIEW: As part of the plea agreement, the prosecution stipulated that defendant be placed on deferred judgment for two years. In addition to other conditions, his deferred judgment was to be supervised by the Jefferson County District Attorney's Adult Diversion Program (ADP). He was convicted of felony theft when he violated the condition of his deferred judgment. At the hearing on the motion to withdraw his guilty plea, defendant argued that the condition in the plea agreement, which provided for supervision by ADP, was illegal. The court disagreed. The court found that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-7-403 provided a means of resolving a criminal prosecution short of entering a judgment of conviction. Thus, the district attorney could supervise the conditions under which deferred judgment was granted. In the court's view, ADP's supervision of defendants on deferred judgment did not violate the doctrine of separation of powers, and therefore, defendant was not illegally induced to enter the plea agreement. The trial court properly denied defendant's motion to withdraw his plea of guilty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Rodriguez v. Schutt


No. 93CA1194


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


896 P.2d 881; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 374; 18 BTR 2093



December 15, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected. Opinion Modified, and as Modified. Rehearing Denied January 26, 1995. Certiorari Granted May 22, 1995 (95SC97). Certiorari Granted on the following issues: Should 13-21-101, 6A C.R.S. (1987), be interpreted to establish a floor on interest on judgments at nine percent (9%) when the personal injury judgment creditor has been subjected to an appeal? Alternatively, is an appeal-reduced interest rate pursuant to 13-21-101, 6A C.R.S. (1987), a constitutionally prohibited denial of equal protection to personal injury judgment creditors subjected to appeal? Released for Publication June 13, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Warren O. Martin, Judge. No. 92CV4110.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMEDAND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord challenged the judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado) in favor of appellee tenants in a negligence action to recover damages for personal injuries. The tenants challenged the trial court's calculation of interest on the damage award.


OVERVIEW: The landlord asserted that the trial court erred by not excluding any reference to evidence lost by the tenants or, alternatively, by not giving an adverse inference instruction. The court reviewed the general concept of destroyed or spoiled evidence and, in particular, the best evidence rule under Colo. R. Evid. 1004(1). The court noted that there was no evidence that the tenants had intentionally destroyed the evidence, that they had acted in bad faith, or that the evidence would have been contrary to their interests. The court found that the trial court acted within its discretion when it allowed the admission of secondary evidence and declined to give an adverse inference instruction. With regard to the calculation of interest on the damage award, the court observed that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-101 (1987 repl. vol. 6A) clearly required the use of a variable interest rate in the event of an appeal. The court found that § 13-21-101 was rationally related to a legitimate state interest and, therefore, was not unconstitutionally violative of the tenants' equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the tenants on the negligence claim was affirmed but the cause was remanded to the trial court for recalculation of interest on the damage award.

Zaner v. City of Brighton


No. 94CA0139


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


899 P.2d 263; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 356; 18 BTR 2041



December 1, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified. Rehearing Denied January 19, 1995. Certiorari Granted June 30, 1995 (95SC123). Certiorari Granted on the following issues: Whether the ballot issue election date provision of Colo. Const. art. X, sec. 20, ("TABOR") applies to all ballot issue elections, or only to those involving "fiscal matters." Whether the use of the ballot title for TABOR, or its placement in the constitution, was properly relied upon to discern the meaning of art. X, sec. 20(3)(a). Whether the General Assembly may define the application of section 1-41-103, 1B C.R.S. (1994 Supp.) to certain listed "fiscal matters" even though TABOR is self-executing. Is approval of a utility franchise which will result in substantial revenues to a city a "fiscal matter?" Released for Publication July 12, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Adams County. Honorable John E. Popovich, Jr., Judge. No. 93CV906.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff electors appealed an order from the District Court of Adams County (Colorado), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, city and power company, in the electors' action that challenged the city's authority to hold a special election.


OVERVIEW: Registered electors brought an action to challenge a referendum election held by the city to obtain voter approval for the transfer of the city's electric utility franchise from one utility to another. They maintained that the election was in violation of Colo. Const. art X, § 20, known as "The Taxpayer's Bill of Rights" (TABOR), an initiated constitutional amendment approved by the electors in the 1992 general election. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of the city. The electors appealed, argued that Colo. Const. art. X, § 20, required that all elections were to have been held on specified dates. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that TABOR applied only to issues of government financing, spending, and taxation, and not to all issues regardless of subject matter nor even to all issues which could have been characterized as fiscal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the district court, which held that the city's special election concerned a ballot issue which did not fall within the scope of the election provisions of the state constitution.

Rose Medical Ctr. v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


No. 93CA2071


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


903 P.2d 15; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 360; 18 BTR 2033



December 1, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified. Rehearing Denied January 12, 1995. Certiorari Denied August 28, 1995 (95SC109). Released for Publication September 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Morris B. Hoffman, Judge. No. 92CV7735.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of a judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which granted appellee hospital summary judgment in its action against the insurer to enforce a statutory hospital lien under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-27-103 (1982 Repl. Vol. 16A). The trial court found the insurer liable for the full amount of the hospital lien plus reasonable attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The wife was injured in a two-vehicle accident while a passenger in a vehicle driven by her husband. She filed an action against her husband seeking damages for bodily injuries she sustained. The insurer was the bodily injury insurer for the husband and also provided personal injury protection (PIP) coverage for the wife apparently under the same policy. The hospital filed a notice of hospital lien in the then pending litigation, gave notice to the wife's counsel on that date, and to insurance counsel, all in a manner provided by Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-27-102 (1994 Cum. Supp.) The wife then received an arbitration award from the insurer, settled her suit against her husband for a nominal amount, but did not satisfy the lien. The insurer argued that it dealt separately with bodily injury claims, and, therefore, notice in one proceeding was not effective with regard to other proceedings or coverages. The court affirmed the judgment and rejected this position in the situation were both coverages were provided by the same carrier presumably under the same policy. The court also held that while the means of notice was not optimum, any deficiency did not rise to constitutional dimensions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the hospital finding the insurer liable for the entire amount of the hospital lien.

City of Colorado Springs v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 93CA0386, No. 93CA0412


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


895 P.2d 1105; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 340; 18 BTR 1952



November 17, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 15, 1994. Certiorari Denied June 5, 1995 (94SC765). Released for Publication June 13, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Eagle County. Honorable William L. Jones, Judge. No. 88CV142.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county board of commissioners and related officials (board), challenged the decision from the District Court of Eagle County (Colorado), which vacated the board's order denying land use permits to appellee cities.


OVERVIEW: Cities held water rights in a certain wilderness area. The cities applied to the county board for a special use permit to conduct a major extension of an existing water collection system. The board denied the permits and the cities appealed. The trial court vacated the denial and remanded with instructions. The board appealed, challenging the trial court's decision. The court held that the trial court was permitted to reverse an administrative decision under Colo. R. Civ. P. 106 only if there was no competent evidence to have supported the decision. The court held that the trial court erred by remanding on the ground that it was unable to ascertain what the board's decision would have been had the preempted criteria not been considered. The court determined that the trial court should have focused solely upon whether the record contained any competent evidence to have supported the determination that any one of the remaining criteria had not been met.


OUTCOME: The judgment vacating the board's order was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with directions to reinstate the decision of the county board.

Van Dorn Retail Management v. City & County of Denver


No. 93CA1966


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


902 P.2d 383; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 338; 18 BTR 1996



November 17, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 22, 1994. Certiorari Denied August 28, 1995 (95SC60). Released for Publication September 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable J. Steven Phillips, Judge. No. 92CV5576.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retailer appealed an order from the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, the City and County of Denver and the State of Colorado, thereby rejecting the retailer's contention that certain tax lien provisions of Denver and the state were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Under an agreement with a Colorado clothing store, the retailer, a New York corporation, provided the store with certain goods on consignment for sale. The store was responsible for collecting and remitting city taxes, including sales tax and business and employee occupational privilege tax. The store was also subject to personal property taxes assessed under the state statute. After notice, the state and the city seized and held the consigned goods as a result of the delinquent sales, occupational, and personal property taxes. Following an administrative hearing, the seizure was upheld. On the retailer's action seeking to declare Denver, Colo., Rev. Mun. Code §§ 53-59, 53-63, and Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 39-26- 117(1)(b), 39-22-604(7)(a) (1994 Repl.), unconstitutional, the district court granted summary judgment in favor of the city and state. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that the challenged ordinances and statutes neither violated guarantees of equal protection established by the U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Colo. Const. art. II, § 25, by treating similarly situated persons differently nor violated the retailer's right to substantive and procedural due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the retailer did not meet its burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that the ordinances and statutes providing for the seizure of property for delinquent taxes were unconstitutional.

 

1535 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


DeBose v. Bear Valley Church of Christ


No. 92CA1929


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


890 P.2d 214; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 341; 18 BTR 1937



November 17, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and As Modified, Petitions for Rehearing Denied January 5, 1995. Davidson, J., would GRANT petition of Plaintiffs-Appellees and Cross-Appellants. Released for Publication in error Certiorari pending January 24, 1995 (95SC42). Certiorari Granted June 19, 1995 (95SC42).
As Amended June 20, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Herbert L. Stern, III, Judge. No. 91CV4346.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, mother and minor, filed an action against defendants, counselor and church, to recover damages for injuries sustained due to alleged sexual abuse of the minor by the counselor. The District Court for the City and County of Denver (Colorado) granted judgments on jury verdicts to the mother and minor. The counselor and church filed an appeal; the mother and minor filed a cross-appeal of the jury's finding of comparative negligence.


OVERVIEW: The counselor and church asserted that the trial court erred in refusing to give any instruction upon the significance of the counselor's belief in the efficacy of massage, the verdicts resulted in the award of duplicate damages, and allowing expert testimony on the standards that should be applied in a pastoral setting was error. The minor and mother asserted that the trial court erred in reducing the damages award by the amount of the minor's comparative negligence. The court concluded that the lack of an instruction on the significance of the counselor's belief in the efficacy of massage was error. It further concluded that the verdicts could not be sustained because they either constituted duplicate awards or were inherently inconsistent. The court held that the trial court erred in allowing testimony with respect to the standards to be applied to a pastoral counselor because it was improper under the First Amendment to attempt to impose any standard of professional care upon a pastoral counselor. It concluded that the issue of comparative negligence was improperly submitted to the jury because there was no evidence that the minor unreasonably subjected himself to the risks.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments in favor of the mother and minor and remanded the case.

Hibbard v. County of Adams


No. 93CA0593


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


900 P.2d 1254; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 335; 18 BTR 1818



November 3, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified Rehearing Denied December 1, 1994. Certiorari Granted August 14, 1995 (94SC757). Certiorari Granted on the following issues: Whether the court of appeals erred in holding the county liable for destruction of property under 42 U.S.C. 1983. Whether the court of appeals erred in holding the county attorneys liable for destruction of property under 42 U.S.C. 1983.
Released For Publication August 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Adams County. Honorable Michael A. Obermeyer, Judge. Honorable Cindy H. Bruner, Judge. No. 89CV2876.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the county, county attorney, and assistant county attorney, appealed the judgment of the District Court of Adams County (Colorado), which awarded damages and attorney fees under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1988 to plaintiffs, a property owner and resident, for violation of their civil rights. The property owner and resident cross-appealed the denial of their challenge to a county ordinance and the amount of damages and fees awarded.


OVERVIEW: Based on a local ordinance adopted by the county, the county attorney approved the destruction of two buildings located on the property owner's land; someone resided in one of the buildings. The property owner and the resident filed an action for violation of their civil rights and sought a declaratory judgment that the ordinance invoked was invalid. On appeal, the court held that the trial court should have declared the ordinance invalid because there was no statute authorizing the county to adopt such a regulation in order to destroy and remove buildings that did not present a neat and orderly appearance. The trial court properly found the county liable under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for the destruction of the buildings, and while prosecutorial immunity did not protect the individual county attorneys from liability, they should have enjoyed qualified immunity based on the ordinance's invalidity. The property owner and the resident were entitled to attorney fees as prevailing parties under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, but as the trial court failed to properly calculate the amount of fees, the court vacated the award and remanded for redetermination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against the county and county attorneys for violation of the property owner's and resident's civil rights, but reversed the trial court's finding as to the validity of the county ordinance. The court also vacated the award of attorney fees for the property owner and the resident and remanded for a new calculation.
