Board of County Comm'rs v. Dougherty, Dawkins, Strand & Bigelow


No. 94CA0132


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


890 P.2d 199; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 330; 18 BTR 1855



November 3, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified Rehearing Denied December 1, 1994. Released for Publication February 14, 1995.
As Modified. Petition for Rehearing Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Boulder County. Honorable Morris W. Sandstead, Jr., Judge. No. 93CV805.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant investment banking firm (firm) appealed the order of the District Court of Boulder County (Colorado), which granted summary judgment to plaintiff Board of County Commissioners of the County of Boulder (county) in the county's declaratory judgment action to determine the rights of the parties with respect to an equipment lease-purchase agreement and related instruments under the Taxpayer's Bill of Rights, Colo. Const. art. X, § 20.


OVERVIEW: The firm had an agreement to purchase certificates of participation in the right of a bank trustee to receive lease revenue from the county in an equipment lease-purchase transaction, under which terms the county leased equipment for eight months with four additional one-year renewal options. Unsatisfied that the certificates of participation could be enforced as a future years contract, the firm sought a declaration of the parties' rights thereunder. The county contended that a multiple-year debt was not created by the agreement, as it was free to terminate the agreement without penalty; therefore, the agreement did not violate Colo. Const. art. X, § 20, the Taxpayer's Bill of Rights (TABOR). The firm countered that the agreement was void under TABOR absent an election, as it was a multiple-fiscal year financial obligation. The court granted the county specific performance because the agreement did not require funds to be appropriated, nor did it obligate future commissioners to tax for it or even to perform the contract, as there was no remedy against the county or its future revenues for a failure to perform. Therefore, the agreement did not violate the plain language of TABOR.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the county.

Lewis v. Keim


No. 93CA0731


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


883 P.2d 610; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 286; 18 BTR 1603



September 22, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 15, 1994.
As Amended December 12, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Boulder County. Honorable Richard C. McLean, Judge. No. 90CV559



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nonresidents sought review of an order from the District Court of Boulder County (Colorado), that dismissed the nonresidents' personal injury action against defendant Colorado resident on the basis of the failure of the nonresidents to post a cost bond pursuant to under Colo. Rev. Stat. 13-16-102 (1987 Repl. Vol. 6A). The nonresidents contended that the trial court erred in requiring them to file a cost bond.


OVERVIEW: The nonresidents filed a personal injury suit against the Colorado resident. The Colorado resident subsequently sought a cost bond under Colo. Rev. Stat. 13-16-102 (1987 Repl. Vol. 6A), on grounds that the nonresidents were no longer residents of Colorado to cover costs the Colorado resident anticipated he would incur. The nonresidents filed a motion pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-16-103 (1994 Cum. Supp.) to permit the nonresidents to proceed without giving security for the payment of cost. Following the trial court's order that a bond be filed, the Colorado resident filed a motion to dismiss. The nonresidents argued that the trial court erred in requiring that they file a cost bond. The court affirmed the order, holding that there was no error in the dismissal of the action for failure to file a cost bond. The court determined that even if the trial court had granted the nonresidents relief under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-16-103(1), security for costs was still required under § 13-16-102, which also obligated the trial court to require that security be provided if the trial court was satisfied that the nonresidents were unable to pay the costs of suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed the nonresidents' personal injury suit against the Colorado resident for failure to post the cost bond.

People v. Urrutia


No. 92CA0966


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


893 P.2d 1338; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 287; 18 BTR 1592



September 22, 1994, Decided

Released For Publication May 18, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Pueblo County. Honorable Richard D. Robb, Judge. No. 89CR366



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the District Court of Pueblo County (Colorado), which convicted him of second degree murder, first degree sexual assault, and second degree kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contested the granting of a mistrial in his first trial and various errors in his retrial. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in granting the mistrial based on its ex parte conversation with the jury and without further instruction and inquiry. The court affirmed the judgment. The court found that the trial judge's ex parte conversation with the jury during their dismissal for the weekend was improper, but was harmless because it was in no way coercive. Based on the information ascertained during the ex parte conversation, the subsequent note from the jury indicating a deadlock, and the fact that the jury had already deliberated for three days, the court agreed that there was a manifest necessity for declaring a mistrial without further inquiry and instruction. As to the retrial, the court found no error in the failure to excuse a federal security officer as a employee of a public law enforcement agency, to instruct on a lesser sexual assault offense, and to find inconsistent verdicts between the felony murder acquittal and sexual assault verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's judgment on retrial for second degree murder, first degree sexual assault, and second degree kidnapping after a mistrial in the first trial because of a deadlocked jury.

Campbell v. Meyer


No. 93CA1565


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


883 P.2d 617; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 288; 18 BTR 1608



September 22, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable John H. McMullen, Judge. No. 93CV4343



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed an order of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which granted summary judgment to defendants, state and secretary of state, on the taxpayers' suit alleging that the ballot title for Colo. House Bill 93-1330 was improper and that Colo. House Bill 93-1330 was unconstitutional. The state cross-appealed a summary judgment for plaintiff requiring the entire ballot to be capitalized.


OVERVIEW: Colo. Const. art. X, § 20, known as the Taxpayer's Bill of Rights (TABOR), was approved by the state's voters. The legislature then passed, subject to voter approval, Colo. House Bill 93-1330, which provided for a tourism subsidy tax. The taxpayers sued defendants, arguing that Colo. House Bill 93-1330 violated TABOR and thus was unconstitutional, that the ballot title for Colo. House Bill 93-1330 was improper, and that the ballot title violated TABOR because it was not printed in capital letters. The voters defeated Colo. House Bill 93-1330, and the trial court granted summary judgment to defendants on the taxpayers' claims that Colo. R. House Bill 93-1330 was unconstitutional and that the ballot title was improper. However, the trial court granted summary judgment to the taxpayers on their claim alleging that the entire ballot should have been capitalized. The court dismissed the parties' cross-appeals as moot because the voters defeated Colo. House Bill 93-1330. Because the voters did not approve the measure, there was no existing controversy and a determination of the substantive issues presented would have had no practical legal effect.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed as moot the taxpayers' appeal of the grant of summary judgment to defendants on the taxpayers' suit claiming that legislation that provided for a tourism subsidy tax was unconstitutional and that the ballot title for the legislation was improper. The court also dismissed as moot the state's appeal of the grant of summary judgment to the taxpayers requiring the entire ballot to be capitalized.

People v. Black


No. 93CA0808


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


894 P.2d 767; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 275; 18 BTR 1468



September 8, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified. Rehearing Denied October 6, 1994. Certiorari Granted on the following issue: Whether the court of appeals erred in remanding this case to the trial court to determine whether the parole eligibility scheme as applied to sex offenders violates the Equal Protection Clause. Released for Publication April 18, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Frank Martinez, Judge. No. 83CR1850.



DISPOSITION: CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the District Court, City and County of Denver (Colorado), which denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief based upon his claims that he was entitled to immediate release from a sentence for first-degree sexual assault and a crime of violence.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of first-degree sexual assault and a crime of violence, the attorney general's office issued an opinion that made him subject to discretionary rather than mandatory parole. Defendant filed a motion for post-conviction relief in which he claimed that his sentence violated equal protection and due process and that it was illegal. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court remanded the case for consideration of defendant's equal protection claims. The court concluded that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-11-310 (1986) was not facially unconstitutional based on equal protection grounds because it did not create a classification that resulted in unequal treatment of some of the offenders who had committed a sexual assault offense. The court also concluded, however, that remand was necessary for resolution of defendant's argument that § 16-11-310 violated equal protection as applied to him. Defendant's allegations that he was aware of instances in which disparate treatment of offenders had occurred raised material questions of fact that could have provided a basis for relief on equal protection grounds, and a hearing was required to address his claims.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for the trial court to consider defendant's equal protections claims. The court provided that, if the trial court determined that the sentence did not reflect a denial of equal protection, then defendant's sentence would stand affirmed. The court further provided that, if the trial court determined that defendant was denied equal protection, then it should order his immediate release.

Nye v. Industrial Claim Appeals Office


No. 94CA0113


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


883 P.2d 607; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 277; 18 BTR 1493



September 8, 1994, Decided [**1] 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC Nos. 3-629-804, 3-830-720, 3-958-958, & 4-115-353



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant appealed an order from respondent Industrial Claim Appeals Office (Colorado), which allowed the employer and respondent Subsequent Injury Fund to offset the claimant's workers' compensation benefits by amounts paid to him under the employer's pension plan.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was found permanently and totally disabled as a result of an industrial injury and was awarded permanent total disability benefits. He was also receiving social security retirement benefits and retirement benefits from the employer's completely funded pension plan. The Office rendered an order that allowed the employer and the Fund to offset the claimant's workers' compensation benefits by amounts paid to him under the employer's pension plan under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-42-103(1)(c)(II)(B) (1993 Cum. Supp.). On appeal, the claimant contended that the offset should have applied only to non-vested retirement benefits, and Colo. Const. art. II, § 11 prohibited ex post facto application of the offset. The Officer' order was affirmed. The court held that the rights and liabilities of the parties were determined by the statute in effect at the time of the claimant's injury, and it operated to allow an offset for employer funded retirement payments against workers' compensation benefits. The statute at issue did not retrospectively alter the claimant's substantive rights. It held that there was no constitutionally protected civil right in workers' compensation benefits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Office's order that allowed the employer and the Fund to offset the claimant's workers' compensation benefits by amounts paid to him under his employer's pension plan.

People v. Moore


No. 93CA0003


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


902 P.2d 366; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 259; 18 BTR 1410



August 25, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 20, 1994. Certiorari Granted September 25, 1995 (94SC700). Certiorari Granted on the following issues: Whether the court of appeals erred in ruling that the charge of extreme indifference murder in the first degree is established when the conduct which causes death is directed at a particular person. Whether the court of appeals erred in ruling that the petitioner was not entitled to a jury instruction on the lesser non-included offense of third-degree assault. Whether the court of appeals erred in ruling that murder in the second degree is a lesser included offense of extreme indifference murder in the first degree. Whether the court of appeals properly considered the petitioner's appellate issues concerning extreme indifference murder in the first degree when the petitioner was acquitted of that charge and convicted of manslaughter. Released for Publication September 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable Gilbert A. Martinez. No. 91CR2587 and Appeal from the District Court of Larimer County. Honorable William F. Dressel, Judge. No. 92CR334.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado), which convicted defendant of manslaughter. Defendant also sought review of the 12-year sentence imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court committed reversible error by denying his motion for judgment of acquittal on the extreme indifference murder charge because there was insufficient evidence. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to support the charge. Specifically, the court held that the jury could have concluded that defendant had indiscriminately shoved, hit, kicked, and threatened one or more persons without provocation near the time of the victim's death, thus indicating excessively reckless conduct. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that viewing the evidence in a light most favorable to the prosecution, the jury could well have found defendant guilty of the charge beyond a reasonable doubt. The court further rejected defendant's contention that the trial court erred when it failed to instruct the jury on the misdemeanor charge of third degree assault. The court held that there was no rational basis upon which the jury could have convicted defendant of assault and acquitted him of manslaughter. The court affirmed the sentence, holding that the trial court considered appropriate factors and made sufficient findings to support the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for manslaughter. The court further affirmed the 12-year sentence imposed.

People ex rel. A.D.G.


No. 93CA1009


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR

August 11, 1994, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Juvenile Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Orelle R. Weeks, Judge. No. 92JD1360.



DISPOSITION: RULINGS APPROVED IN PART AND DISAPPROVED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision of the Juvenile Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which refused to waive jurisdiction over appellee juvenile, for lack of "clear and convincing" evidence, refused to compel a psychological examination of the juvenile, and held that the juvenile's refusal to be psychologically examined could not have been considered as part of the transfer decision.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was charged in a delinquency petition with manslaughter and prohibited use of a weapon. The state requested that the juvenile court transfer the case to district court pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-2-806 (1993) and sought a court-ordered psychological evaluation. The juvenile court found the transfer statute constitutional but concluded that procedural due process required a standard of clear and convincing evidence. The juvenile court concluded that it could not have ordered a psychological examination over the juvenile's objection. The court held that it disapproved of the juvenile court's ruling that due process required a standard of proof by clear and convincing evidence but because the juvenile had been adjudicated a delinquent the court could not remand for reconsideration.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the juvenile court, which refused to waive jurisdiction over the juvenile, refused to compel a psychological examination of the juvenile, and held that the juvenile's refusal to be psychologically examined could not have been considered as part of the transfer decision.

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND ORDER REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenant challenged a judgment by the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado) entered on a jury verdict in favor of defendant landlords in the tenant's personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: The tenant rented and lived in an apartment facility owned or managed by the landlords, a limited partnership and management company. The tenant was injured when she slipped and fell on some ice in the apartment parking lot. The tenant commenced proceedings urging that she was an invitee on the premises. At a pre-trial hearing, the trial court concluded that the tenant was a licensee and trial to a jury was conducted on that basis. On review, the court reversed the judgment for the landlords, concluding that the tenant was an invitee. The court noted that the landlords were in the business of renting property and that the tenant was a customer of the landlords in a continuing business relationship that was mutually beneficial. The court rejected the argument that the status of a tenant changed with the particular activity engaged in by the tenant at the time of the injury. The court held that the order requiring the tenant to pay the cost of the preparation and transmittal of those portions of the record on appeal designated by the landlords constituted error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the landlords in the tenant's personal injury action and remanded for a new trial.

Department of Corrections Employees Coalition v. Romer


No. 93CA0096


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


879 P.2d 485; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 215; 18 BTR 1335



July 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] THIS OPINION IS NOT THE FINAL VERSION AND IS SUBJECT .
Released For Publication September 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable J. Stephen Phillips, Judge. No. 91CV3017.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corrections employees challenged a judgment by the District Court, City and County of Denver (Colorado), which granted appellees, the governor, the executive director of the Colorado Department of Personnel, and the State, summary judgment in the employees' action for declaratory judgment that Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 24-50-104(5)(a) (1988 Repl. Vol. 10B) and 24-50-104(4)(d)(III) (1993 Cum. Supp.) were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After a study conducted by the Department, the director decided to reduce the salary grade of corrections employees. The employees challenged the decision by filing an action for declaratory judgment. The employees alleged that two statutes that related to how the Department determined salaries and how those determinations were implemented violated the separation of powers requirements of Colo. Const. art. III and the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The trial court granted summary judgment to the State and its officials. The court affirmed on appeal. The court first found that the director conducted the study pursuant to the director's responsibility to revise and maintain a classification system under § 24-50-104(3) and (4). The court found no violation of the separation of powers clause because the Colorado Constitution contemplated elaboration of the personnel system by the legislature and implementation by the director. Next, the court held that there was no equal protection violation because the director's classification of the employees was rationally related to the State's interest in maintaining fiscal integrity in the personnel system.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Squire Rest. & Lounge v. City & County of Denver


No. 93CA0541


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


890 P.2d 164; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 208; 18 BTR 1299



July 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified. Rehearing Denied August 11, 1994. Certiorari Denied March 6, 1995 (94 S.C. 553). Released for Publication March 16, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Frank Martinez, Judge. No. 92CV1439



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lounge appealed a judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which affirmed the decision of defendant license department (department) denying the lounge's request to renew its liquor license, claiming that the denial violated its due process rights and that the statutory standard of good cause for refusing to renew a liquor license constituted an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority.


OVERVIEW: The department refused to renew the lounge's liquor license, concluding that local inhabitants did not require or want there to be a liquor license of the lounge's type in the area. The lounge brought an action against defendants, department, city, county, department director, and state revenue agency. The trial court affirmed the department's decision, finding that due process was satisfied, but the court reversed the judgment below. The court held that the delegation of legislative authority to the department in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-47-106(1)(b) (1991) was not unconstitutional. The court concluded, however, that because the department had not enacted regulations defining the good cause standard in the statute, denial of the request to renew the license violated the lounge's due process rights. Such a standard, without more, provided no way for a licensee to know in advance what evidence was relevant to a request for a renewal. There were also no meaningful limits on each hearing officer's selection of criteria. The court held that the department was required to provide some limit to guide discretion in determining whether there was good cause for refusing to renew the license.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded with directions that the trial court enter a judgment mandating renewal of the lounge's liquor license.

 

1548 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Atencio


No. 93CA0979


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


878 P.2d 147; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 199; 18 BTR 1163



June 30, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 23, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable David D. Parrish, Judge. No. 92CR3076



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado), which convicted him of five counts relating to the possession of or possession with intent to sell or distribute cocaine and marijuana. He was sentenced as a "special offender" under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-407(1)(f) (1993 Cum. Supp.) for possessing or having available for use a deadly weapon during the commission of one or more of the offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced as a special offender under § 18-18-407(1)(f) for possessing or having available a deadly weapon during the commission of one or more drug offenses. On appeal, defendant attacked the constitutionality of § 18-18-407(1)(f) on due process grounds and on the basis that it violated his right to bear arms guaranteed by Colo. Const. art. II, § 13. The court affirmed defendant's sentence and concluded that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-407(1)(f) (1993 Cum. Supp.) was constitutional. Because of the increased risk of injury or death to private citizens and law enforcement personnel from the combination of drugs and weapons, the state, pursuant to its police powers, had a right to reasonably regulate and sanction such activities. Also, there was a sufficient nexus between the drug offenses and defendant's possession or availability for use of a deadly weapon. Defendant had a loaded 9-millimeter handgun in a bedroom in close proximity to the drugs and to where he was arrested, which was sufficient for the jury reasonably to infer that he had a deadly weapon available for use.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence as a special offender for possessing or having available for use a deadly weapon during the commission of one or more of his drug possession offenses.

 

1549 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Lawson v. Safeway, Inc.


No. 93CA0860


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


878 P.2d 127; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 168; 18 BTR 1071



June 16, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 23, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Warren O. Martin, Judge. No. 91CV7967



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant store appealed the judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado) that was entered on a jury verdict in favor of plaintiff customer in the customer's negligence cause of action alleging that she slipped and fell in the store.


OVERVIEW: The customer slipped and fell on spilled milk in the store. The store argued that the jury should have been instructed that the customer was required to prove that the store unreasonably failed to exercise reasonable care. The court affirmed and held that there had been no substantial, prejudicial error even if its instruction was erroneously given because, read as a whole, the instruction adequately informed the jury of the applicable standard of care. The court also dismissed the store's argument that the trial court erred in instructing the jury that it could award damages for permanent injury and that the customer could recover for her medical expenses as there was no expert testimony in regard to either. By its instructions, the trial court did not direct the jury to find that the customer had been injured as she claimed or that her medical expenses were reasonable and necessary; rather, the jury could have found so pursuant to the customer's testimony. Finally, an instruction on damages for aggravation of a preexisting condition was proper because that issue was raised by the store in its opening statement and evidence was thereafter introduced on the issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court entered upon a jury verdict in favor of the customer.

Newport Pac. Capital Co. v. Waste


No. 93CA0635


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


878 P.2d 136; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 176; 18 BTR 1055



June 16, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 23, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Eagle County. Honorable William L. Jones, Judge. Nos. 93CV10 and 93CV12



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mobile home owner sought review from a judgment of the District Court of Eagle County (Colorado), which was entered in favor of plaintiff mobile home park operator in its unlawful detainer action alleging violations of plaintiff's rules. Defendant contended that the rule prohibiting the rental of mobile homes and the subleasing of spaces was unreasonable under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-12-203(1)(c) and that attorney fees were excessive.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff mobile home park operator brought an unlawful detainer action against defendant mobile home owner for violations of plaintiff's rules regarding the prohibition on rental of mobile homes and subleasing of spaces. Defendant contended that the rule was prima facie unreasonable under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-12-203(1)(c). The trial court held that the rule was not economically unreasonable and entered judgment in favor of plaintiff and awarded attorney fees. Defendant sought review, and the court affirmed in part, holding that the rule was not unreasonable and that there was no violation of due process or equal protection. The court noted that the trial court's findings on the issue of reasonableness were not patently erroneous and affirmed that part of the judgment. The court reversed the award of attorney fees and remanded for further proceedings. The court held that it was unclear whether the trial court had allocated the attorney fees between this case and another case, which should have been done, and remanded on that issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of plaintiff mobile home park operator in its unlawful detainer action against defendant mobile home park owner for violations of plaintiff's rules against the rental of mobile homes and subleasing of spaces, holding that the trial court's findings as to reasonableness were not erroneous. The court reversed and remanded the award of attorney fees for determination as to allocability with another case.

Ablin v. Richard O'Brien Plastering Co.


No. 93CA0880


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


885 P.2d 289; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 154; 18 BTR 952



June 2, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 7, 1994. Certiorari Denied December 5, 1994 (94SC468). Released for Publication on December 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Warren O. Martin, Judge. No. 93CV0701



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff siblings appealed a decision from the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, truck driver and corporate entities, in the siblings' wrongful death cause of action to recover damages for the death of their brother. The siblings asserted that the trial court erred in interpreting the Wrongful Death Act to preclude siblings from maintaining wrongful death actions.


OVERVIEW: The siblings' brother was riding his bicycle when he was struck by a truck driven and owned by defendants and killed. The siblings, as the decedent's only living relatives, filed a wrongful death cause of action against defendants. Defendants filed a motion for summary judgment, arguing that the siblings lacked standing to bring a suit under the state Wrongful Death Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-201 et seq. The trial court granted the motion and the siblings asserted that the trial court erred in finding they lacked standing to file the suit. The court affirmed the trial court's ruling holding that the Wrongful Death Act was designed to serve the legitimate governmental purpose of giving the right to sue to those who would be most directly affected by a wrongful death and the statute's failure to confer standing upon relatives other than spouses, descendants, and parents did not render it irrational or unconstitutional. The court concluded that the trial court's interpretation of the Wrongful Death Act was not a constitutional violation of the equal protection clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of defendants and dismissing the siblings' suit holding that they lacked standing to file a wrongful death cause of action for their deceased brother's death.

People v. Dunkin


No. 93CA0325, No. 93CA0326


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


888 P.2d 305; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 121; 18 BTR 797



May 5, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 7, 1994. Certiorari Denied January 30, 1995 (94SC478). Released for Publication February 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Park County, Honorable Kenneth M. Plotz, Judge, No. 91CR10, No. 91CR11



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated case, defendants each appealed a judgment of conviction for cultivation of marihuana from the District Court of Park County (Colorado) .


OVERVIEW: Based on evidence provided in a sworn affidavit, a warrant was issued to search a residence owned and occupied by defendants. Following the search, defendants were arrested and charged with cultivation of marihuana and other offenses. After hearing testimony, the trial court denied the defendants' joint motion to suppress the seized evidence. The court reviewed the circumstances surrounding the issuance of the warrant, which was supported in significant part on information that the investigating officer was furnished by the rural electric association about the unusual amount of electricity used in the residence as reflected by a record of the monthly billings. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that defendants had no reasonable expectation of privacy in the utility records such that the investigating officer's conduct in obtaining the information would constitute a search in violation of the U.S. Const. amends. IV and XIV as well as Colo. Const. art. II, §§ 7 and 25.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction, concluding the trial court properly denied the motion to suppress the evidence seized from a residence under a search warrant obtained after an investigating officer was apprised of an unusual amount of electricity used in the residence.

People v. Bergen


No. 91CA1629


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


883 P.2d 532; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 120; 18 BTR 664



April 21, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 2, 1994. Certiorari Denied November 15, 1994 (94SC396). Released for Publication November 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Christopher J. Munch, Judge. No. 90CR1342, No. 91CR721



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant reporter sought review of judgments of conviction entered upon jury verdicts in the District Court of Jefferson County (Colorado), which found defendant guilty on charges of dogfighting, conspiracy to commit dogfighting, and accessory to dogfighting.


OVERVIEW: Defendant reporter videotaped dog fights for purposes of televising stories about dogfighting. The district attorney's office brought the matter before a grand jury to investigate violations of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-9-204 (repealed 1986), which prohibited knowing attendance at a dogfight held for profit or entertainment. Defendant received a grand jury subpoena advising her of her rights under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-5-204(4)(a) (repealed 1986), but the subpoena was cancelled and defendant testified voluntarily. After an indictment was returned by the grand jury, defendant was convicted on dogfighting charges. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions. The court held that (1) Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-5-204(4)(b) (repealed 1986) did not bar defendant's prosecution because she voluntarily testified before the grand jury without written advice of her rights; (2) absent a showing that the indictment's validity was affected, the trial court was not required to conduct a hearing to explore grand jury irregularities; (3) the media did not have a right to engage in illegal activities for the purpose of news reporting; (4) the statutory prohibition against dogfighting was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction on dogfighting charges was affirmed because defendant voluntarily testified before the grand jury and had waived statutory written advice of her rights. The court also held that absent a showing that the indictment's validity was affected, the trial court was not required to conduct a hearing to explore grand jury irregularities, and that defendant did not have a right to engage in illegal activities to report the news.

Stoorman v. Greenwood Trust Co.


No. 93CA0224


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


888 P.2d 289; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 101; 18 BTR 610



April 7, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 26, 1994. Certiorari Granted January 30, 1995 (94SC382). Certiorari Granted on the following issues:
Whether the terms "interest" and "rate" in 12 U.S.C. 1831d(a) (1988) include contingent penalty charges (late fees), which were not considered "interest" at common law, so as to preempt, under the Supremacy Clause of the United States Constitution, Colorado's prohibition and regulation of late charges on revolving credit accounts.
Whether Congress intended Delaware's legislative definition of "interest" to preempt Colorado's protection and common laws limiting contractual charges on revolving credit accounts.
Whether 12 U.S.C. 1831d(a) (1988) is unconstitutional under Article IV of the United States Constitution because it delegates Congress' power to preempt state law to the home states of federally insured banks.
Released for Publication February 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable J. Stephen Phillips, Judge. No. 92CV1789



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Class action plaintiff appealed from an order of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado) granting summary judgment in favor of defendant in a claim for violation of the Colo. Consumer Credit Code §§ 5-3-203 and 5-5-202.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was a Colorado resident and holder of a "Discover" credit card. Defendant was a Delaware bank that offered the card. Under the terms of the card agreement, defendant assessed a late fee on cardholders who were late in their monthly payments. In a class action complaint, plaintiff alleged that the late fees violated Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 5-3-203 and 5-5-202 and alleged various additional state claims. The trial court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment finding that plaintiff's claims seeking a refund of all late fees charged were preempted by section 521 of the Depository Institutions Deregulation and Monetary Control Act of 1980 (DIDA), 12 U.S.C.S. § 1831d (1988). The court of appeals affirmed holding that the late fees were interest under section 521, that section 521 preempted state common law, and that Colorado's opt-out provision, if valid, did not apply because the loan was made in Delaware.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment affirmed; DIDA preempted Colorado state statutory and common law on the issue of late fees because the late fees were interest and because Colorado's opt-out provision, if valid, did not apply because the loan was made in Delaware.

Board of County Comm'rs v. E-470 Pub. Highway Auth.


No. 93CA1292


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


881 P.2d 412; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 84; 18 BTR 535



March 24, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 28, 1994. Certiorari Granted October 11, 1994 (94SC307). Released for Publication October 18, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Arapahoe County. Honorable Kenneth K. Stuart, Judge. No. 93CV1418



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, AND REVERSED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, Board of County Commissions and officials, appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Arapahoe County (Colorado), which held that amendment's to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 43-4-501 et seq., were constitutional, and although defendants, highway authority and officials, were subject to Colo. Const. art. X, § 20, they were not required to hold an election before remarketing bonds or implementing a finance plan. Defendants' cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: After defendants issued bonds, the General Assembly passed the Public Highway Authority Law, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 43-4-501, et seq., which authorized the formation by intergovernmental agreement of political subdivisions known as "public highway authorities," to finance, construct, operate, or maintain a beltway or other transportation improvements in a metropolitan region. Later amendments expanded the authority of defendants. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment to the extent that it found that the statute's amendments constitutional. However, because defendants were an "enterprise" and not a "district," the court held that defendants were not subject to the election provisions of Colo. Const. art. X, § 20, and reversed that portion of the trial court's judgment to the contrary. The court found that the act of releasing the bond proceeds from escrow did not create any new debt, impose any tax, or expose the taxpayers to any new liability or obligation that required voter approval in advance. Further, the revenues and expenditure agreements between plaintiffs and defendants were outside the scope of Colo. Const. art. X, § 20.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the trial court's judgment that held that defendants were subject to the constitutionally mandated election provisions for "districts," but affirmed the judgment in all other respects.

Malmgren v. Copper Mountain


No. 93CA0328


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


873 P.2d 44; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 86; 18 BTR 531



March 24, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Summit County. Honorable W. Terry Ruckriegle, Judge. No. 92CV189



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Summit County (Colorado), which dismissed their petition for incorporation of a municipality and for initiation of proceedings for the adoption of a city home rule charter filed pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 31-2-209 (1986 Repl. Vol. 12B).


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed an action seeking the incorporation of a municipality and simultaneously sought to initiate proceedings for the adoption of a home rule charter pursuant to § 31-2-209. The trial court dismissed the petition. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court found that petitioners failed to state a sufficient claim where they failed to allege that they were landowners within the area they sought to incorporate. The court held that a petition for incorporation, whether filed alone under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 31-2-101(1) (1986 Repl. Vol. 12B) or with a home rule charter under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 31-2-209 (1986 Repl. Vol. 12B), needed to contain allegations that the signatories were landowners within the territory sought to be incorporated. The court concluded that the landowner requirement was not an unconstitutional limitation on the ability of an unincorporated municipality to obtain a home rule charter where the requirement was applicable to signatories to petitions for incorporation, not to signatories to petitions for the initiation of home rule proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that dismissed a petition for incorporation of a municipality and for initiation of proceedings for the adoption of a municipality home rule charter.

People v. Fernandez


No. 91CA1732


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


883 P.2d 491; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 72; 18 BTR 425



March 10, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reharing Denied May 5, 1994. Certiorari Denied October 24, 1994 (94SC330). Released for Publication November 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Federico C. Alvarez, Judge. No. 90CR3261



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the District Court, City and County of Denver (Colorado) for first degree murder. During trial, defendant unsuccessfully moved for acquittal on the ground that the element of "universal malice" could not be established because his conduct was directed against a single individual. After trial, defendant's motion for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict, on the same ground, was denied.


OVERVIEW: The 17-year-old defendant and some friends went to a bar but were told to leave because some were minors. Defendant stayed in the parking lot, while others reentered and got into a brawl. When customers, including the victim, chased the friends out, defendant fired twice toward the open door, killing the victim, and three times through a window. The court rejected the contention that the trial court erred in not instructing the jury on non-retreat and "apparent necessity," which applied to self-defense and were inconsistent with extreme indifference murder. The court opined that a guilty verdict precluded finding defendant's actions reasonable because "universal malice" required the jury to conclude that he acted with aggravated recklessness. The court found no reversible error in the denial of defendant's mistrial motion after the prosecutor asked a witness whether defendant or his friends associated with gangs because when defendant objected to the question, the trial court sustained the objection, and the witness did not answer. The court concluded, as a matter of law, that a life sentence without possibility of parole was not disproportionate to first degree murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which had convicted defendant of first degree murder.

People v. Hood


No. 92CA0540


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


878 P.2d 89; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 77; 18 BTR 432



March 10, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 7, 1994. Certiorari Denied August 8, 1994 (94SC263).
Released for Publication August 23, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Morgan County. Honorable Joseph J. Weatherby, Judge. No. 91CR79



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the District Court of Morgan County (Colorado), which convicted him, upon a jury's verdict, of conspiracy to commit first degree murder under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-2-201 (Repl. Vol. 1986) and two counts of criminal solicitation under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-2-301 (Repl. Vol. 1986).


OVERVIEW: Defendant talked to his girlfriend and friend about killing his wife. The girlfriend killed his wife but claimed that defendant had manipulated her to do so. Defendant was acquitted of first degree murder based on a complicity theory, but he was convicted of conspiracy to commit first degree murder and two counts of criminal solicitation. On appeal, defendant argued, among other things, that his acquittal on the first degree murder charge and his conviction on the conspiracy charge were inconsistent, that the evidence did not support his criminal solicitation conviction, and that solicitation merged into the conspiracy offense. The court rejected his arguments and affirmed. The court held that there was ample evidence for the jury to infer that there was an agreement between defendant and his girlfriend to murder his wife that was completely independent from the evidence that linked defendant to the murder as a complicitor. There was sufficient evidence to convict defendant of solicitation even though the friend did not commit the murder. Solicitation and conspiracy did not merge because each crime required proof of at least one fact that was not required by the other.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of conspiracy to commit first degree murder and two counts of criminal solicitation.

Ranger v. Fortune Ins. Co.


No. 92CA1748


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


881 P.2d 394; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 61; 18 BTR 330



February 24, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended March 3, 1994. Rehearing Denied April 14, 1994. Certiorari Denied September 19, 1994 (94SC283). Released for Publication October 18, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable Steven T. Pelican, Judge. No. 86CV2973



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On the parties' cross motions, plaintiff injured person appealed the judgment of the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado), which granted summary judgment to defendant insurer in the injured person's action for punitive and treble damages for the insurer's alleged bad-faith refusal to pay personal injury protection benefits. The injured person argued that the trial court erred in concluding that Florida law was applicable.


OVERVIEW: The injured person was hurt while in Colorado as a passenger in an automobile that was insured by the insurer, a Florida corporation. The insurer admitted coverage of the driver and for the accident but refused to pay the injured person's medical bills. The injured person filed an action. Following remand, the insurer filed a motion for summary judgment claiming that it was not liable under Florida law for treble damages and 18 percent interest on the unpaid medical bills. The trial court granted the motion. The injured person appealed. The court reversed and held that the trial court should have applied Colorado law, specifically, the Colorado Auto Accident Reparations Act, particularly Colo. Rev. Stat. § 10-4-711(a) (1987 repl. 4A). The driver of the car was visiting Colorado, and the injured person was a Colorado resident. Accordingly, Colorado had the most significant relationship with the occurrence and the parties. Under the express terms of § 10-4-711(a), the insurer was required to provide personal injury protection to the injured person. The insurer's liability arose from § 10-4-711(a), not from the insurance contract. Remand was necessary to determine damages.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the insurer in the injured person's action to recover punitive and treble damages for the insurer's alleged bad-faith refusal to pay personal injury protection benefits. The injured person was entitled to a remand for a damages determination under Colorado law.

February 24, 1994, Decided

Opinion Modified, and As Modified, Petition for Rehearing DENIED.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the State Personnel Board. Nos. 912B074, 912B075, 912B076, 912B078, 912B079, 912B080, 912B081, 912B082, 912B083, 912B084, 912B085, 912B086, 912B087, 912B088, 912B089, 912B090, 912B091, 912B092, 912B096

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainant former employees sought review of the decision of the State Personnel Board (Colorado), which approved the order of an Administrative Law Judge (ALJ) in the nature of a summary judgment dismissing the employees' petition for relief.


OVERVIEW: The employees were employed by the state in the Division of Disaster Emergency Services (DODES), which was a division of the Department of Public Safety (DPS). The governor abolished DODES and laid off all of its employees. The governor transferred all of DODES' functions to a new office, the Office of Emergency Management (OEM) in the Department of Local Affairs (DOLA). Const. art. XII, § 13. The court found that there was evidence that the governor's actions violated the Civil Service Amendment. The court determined that the statutes did not authorize the governor to abolish a statutorily created agency of state government such as DODES without prior legislative authorization.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Board's dismissal of the employees' action and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

People v. Stevenson


No. 92CA1745


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


881 P.2d 383; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 3; 18 BTR 118



January 13, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 17, 1994. Certiorari Denied September 19, 1994 (94SC154). Released for Publication October 18, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Michael C. Villano, Judge. No. 91CR294



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the District Court of Jefferson County, Colorado that convicted him, following a bench trial, of criminal possession of four financial transaction devices.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of criminal possession of four financial transaction devices and the court affirmed. The court found the trial court did not err in granting leave to the prosecution to amend the information to charge only the strict liability alternative under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-5-703(1). The amended charge sufficiently apprised defendant of the nature and elements of the charged offense and the conduct upon which the charge was based. The court also found no merit in defendant's claim that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-5-703(1) was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague. Defendant did not argue that possession of a stolen credit transaction device was either a fundamental right or constitutionally protected conduct so the law was not facially overbroad. The statuary scheme defines the strict liability alternative of unlawful possession of a financial device in a manner that allows persons of reasonable intelligence to distinguish between lawful and unlawful conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that convicted defendant of criminal possession of four financial transaction devices.

People v. Graham


No. 91CA1984


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


876 P.2d 68; 1994 Colo. App. LEXIS 10; 18 BTR 90



January 13, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 3, 1994. Petitioner & Cross-Petitioner for Certiorari Denied July 18, 1994 (94SC169).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Henry E. Nieto, Judge. No. 91CR296



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of Jefferson County (Colorado), which, upon the a jury verdict, entered a conviction finding him guilty of sexual assault on a child as a part of a pattern of abuse and sentenced him as a class 3 felon under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-405(2) (1993 Cum. Supp.).


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of sexual assault on a child as a part of a pattern of abuse. On appeal, defendant argued that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-405(2)(c) (1993 Cum. Supp.), which elevated the crime of sexual assault on a child from a class 4 to a class 3 felony when the offense was committed as a part of a pattern of sexual abuse, was unconstitutionally vague; that, as applied to him, it allowed improper introduction of similar transaction evidence; and that it was an ex post facto law prohibited by U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, and Colo. Const. art. II, § 11. The court found no constitutional defect in the statute itself, but ruled that the application providing for an enhanced punishment was ex post facto. Under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-405(2), a trial court sentenced defendant as a class 3 felon because the jury found that he had committed two or more sexual assaults within a specified 10 year period. However, several of the assaults took place before the enactment of the statute and several took place afterwards. Because the jury's verdict could have been based on an act which preceded the passage of the statute, the court reversed the enhancement portion of the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for sexual assault on a child but reversed the enhancement portion of the conviction, and remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Padilla


No. 92CA1227


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION C


878 P.2d 4; 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 322; 17 BTR 1903



December 2, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 10, 1994. Certiorari Granted August 15, 1994 (94SC144). Cross-Petn. for Certiorari Denied August 15, 1994. Certiorari Granted on the following issues: Whether, during a discretionary sentencing proceeding, a defendant is entitled to an unlimited evidentiary hearing under the pleading and evidentiary standards applicable to a collateral attack under Crim. P. 35(c) to attack prior convictions listed in a presentence report. Whether the requirement that a defendant plead justifiable excuse or excusable neglect in his motion challenging prior convictions is purely prospective under People v. Wiedemer, 852 P.2d 424 (Colo. 1993).
Released for Publication August 23, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Federico C. Alvarez, Judge. No. 91CR1421



DISPOSITION: CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which, at sentencing, denied defendant's motion to suppress prior convictions and refused to allow him to offer evidence on the issue of excusable neglect or justifiable excuse for his failure to attack the convictions within the time imposed by statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of guilty to first degree assault. Prior to sentencing, defendant filed a motion to suppress two prior convictions. At sentencing, the trial court denied the motion to suppress, finding that it was time barred, and refused to allow defendant to present evidence on the issues of excusable neglect or justifiable excuse. On appeal, the court remanded for a hearing at which defendant could present evidence on the issues of excusable neglect or justifiable excuse. The court found that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-5-402 applied to defendant's prior convictions because the legislature intended to avoid the problem of attacks on stale convictions. The court found that it was error for the trial court to deny defendant the opportunity to present evidence on the issue of excusable neglect or justifiable excuse.


OUTCOME: The court remanded for a hearing at which defendant could present evidence in support of his assertions of excusable neglect or justifiable excuse.

 

1564 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


In re Custody of C.C.R.S.


No. 92CA1142


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


872 P.2d 1337; 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 311; 17 BTR 1847



November 18, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 16, 1993. Certiorari Granted May 9, 1994 (94SC23). Certiorari Granted on the following issues: Whether the court of appeals erred in concluding that respondents had standing to seek custody of CCRS under section 14-10-123, 6B C.R.S. (1987) of the Uniform Dissolutio of Marriage Act. Does a biological parent have a statutory right to the return of her child when she changes her mind several months after purportedly relinquishing her child for adoption, where the mother's relinquishment fails to meet statutory requirements. Whether the court of appeals erred in holding that due process does not require a showing of parental unfitness prior to applying the best interest of the child standard to determine custody of a child under section 14-10-123, 6B C.R.S. (1987) of the Uniform Dissolution of Marriage Act. Released for Publication May 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Delta County. Honorable Robert A. Brown, Judge. No. 90-DR-117



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent biological mother voluntarily placed her child at birth with petitioner, would-be adoptive parents, in anticipation of formal relinquishment and adoption proceedings. The adoptive parents sought legal and physical custody of the child pursuant to the Uniform Dissolution of Marriage Act, specifically Colo. Rev. Stat. § 14-10-123 (1987). The District Court of Delta County, Colorado, awarded the parents custody. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother entered a custody agreement for placement of her infant with the parents. Six months later, they initiated a custody proceeding and were granted temporary custody. The mother then renounced the agreement and requested custody. She claimed that the parents lacked standing to seek custody under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 14-10-123 and that § 14-10-123 could not be used to obtain custody of a child placed with non-parents in contemplation of adoption. The parents claimed that the best interests of the child mandated that they have custody. The court held that the mother's lack of physical custody gave the parents standing to seek legal custody. Custody proceedings under § 14-10-123 were not preempted by any adoption or other proceedings. Due process did not require a showing of the mother's unfitness, as termination of parental rights was not involved and the mother consented to place the child with the parents, never took steps to regain physical custody, and made little effort to establish a relationship with the child. The presumption of the biological parent's first right to custody was rebutted by evidence that awarding custody to another would promote the child's welfare.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the trial court did not err in determining that the parents had standing to seek custody, in determining the issue of custody under the "best interests of the child" standard, or in refusing to require a showing of the mother's parental unfitness. The court affirmed the award of custody.

 

1565 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Boehmer


No. 91CA1608


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


872 P.2d 1320; 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 289; 17 BTR 1693



November 4, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 16, 1993. Certiorari Denied April 18, 1994 (94SC33). Released for Publication May 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Arapahoe County. Honorable Thomas C. Levi, Judge. No. 90CR575



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court, Eighteenth Judicial District (Colorado), which convicted him of aggravated robbery and adjudicated him to be a habitual criminal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that his right to testify was not properly waived because the trial court failed to advise him that the same jury would hear the habitual criminal trial. The trial court also failed to explain that if defendant testified in the substantive trial and admitted prior felony convictions, those admissions could not be used to prove the habitual criminal charge. The court found that the waiver was valid. Defendant was represented by counsel, and there was no evidence that he was not properly advised. Nothing in the advisement given by the trial court was inaccurate. Defendant also claimed that his right to a fair trial was violated by the introduction of evidence concerning his arrest. The court disagreed and held that evidence that defendant was wearing multiple layers of clothing did not indicate criminal activity. However, it was relevant because the victim had described the robber in those terms. Testimony concerning the victim's description of the robber was given by the victim and by a police officer. Although the evidence may have been cumulative and hearsay, the issue was not raised in the trial court, and it did not rise to the level of plain error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Schenck v. Minolta Office Sys.


No. 92CA1524


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


873 P.2d 18; 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 271; 17 BTR 1613



October 21, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 26, 1993. Certiorari Denied May 2, 1994 (93SC761). Released for Publication May 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Christopher J. Munch, Judge



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney challenged an order of the District Court of Jefferson County (Colorado), which denied his motion to foreclose an attorney's lien upon an award of one-third of exemplary damages made to the state pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-102(4) (Repl. Vol. 6A 1987).


OVERVIEW: The attorney represented plaintiff in an action against defendants for malicious prosecution. Following trial, the jury awarded plaintiff actual and exemplary damages. The trial court then awarded one-third of the exemplary damages to the state pursuant to § 13-21-102(4). The attorney did not challenge the award to the state. However, the attorney claimed an attorney's lien against the award to the state. Eight months later, the attorney filed a motion to foreclose on the lien, after § 13-21-102(4) was declared unconstitutional. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which denied the attorneys' motion, because the attorney never challenged the award to the state. The court further declined to award the attorney fees from the state upon the common fund doctrine. In so ruling, the court noted that: 1) plaintiff did not pay any fees upon that part of the judgment awarded to the state; and 2) because the state had no legal interest in any award until after judgment between plaintiff and defendants was entered, it had no right to intervene in the malicious prosecution action and assert any claim on its own behalf.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that denied the attorney's motion to foreclose an attorney's lien upon an award of exemplary damages made to the state.

Leek v. City of Golden


No. 92CA1951


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


870 P.2d 580; 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 246; 17 BTR 1554



October 7, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified Rehearing Denied November 12, 1993. Certiorari Denied April 11, 1994 (93SC725).
Released For Publication April 12, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Gaspar F. Perricone, Judge. No. 92CV2531



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed from a decision of the District Court of Jefferson County (Colorado), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant city on their claims regarding a misleading ballot statement, improper issuance of sales and use tax revenue bonds, and improper consolidation of their preliminary injunction hearing with the trial. The city cross-appealed and claimed mootness.


OVERVIEW: The city electorate approved a ballot proposal, enacted an ordinance, and authorized the issuance of sales and use tax revenue bonds. The bond proceeds were to be used to build a community center. The taxpayers challenged these actions, but the trial court ruled in the city's favor. On appeal, the court affirmed. The issue was not moot, as argued by the city, because meaningful relief was still possible. The court found that the ballot question presented to the electorate was not misleading as contended by the taxpayers. The ballot tracked the language of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 29-2-111 (1986 Repl. Vol. 12A) and demonstrated the city's intent to create a sales and use tax capital improvement fund as contemplated by the statute. Thus, the ballot fairly apprised voters of the issues involved. The court found that there was no conflict between the city's charter and Colo. Rev. Stat. § 29-2-112 (1986 Repl. Vol. 12A). Thus, the constitutional supersession doctrine did not apply. The issuance of the sales and use tax revenue bonds was within the city's authority. The trial court did not prejudice either party by consolidating the injunction hearing with a trial on the merits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in the city's favor regarding the taxpayers' challenge to the city's ballot statement and issuance of sales and use tax revenue bonds. There was no error in the trial court's consolidation of the preliminary injunction hearing with the trial.

Delta Sales Yard v. Patten


No. 92CA1449


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


870 P.2d 554; 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 245; 17 BTR 1396



September 9, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 4, 1993. Certiorari Granted March 21, 1994 (93SC699).
Certiorari Granted on the following issue: Whether an action against a Deputy Brand Inspector, employed by the the State Board of Stock Inspection of the Colorado Department of Agriculture, should the one-year statute of limitations found in section 13-80-103(1)(c), 6A C.R.S. (1987), pertaining to "police enforcement authority", apply to the cause of action or should the two-year statute of limitation, found in section 13-80-102(1)(h), 6A C.R.S. (1987), pertaining to all actions against "any employee of a public or governmental entity", applies to the cause of action.
Released For Publication April 12, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Lincoln County. Honorable Norman L. Arends, Judge. No. 91CV5



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the order of the District Court of Lincoln County (Colorado), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant brand inspector. Plaintiff had filed a complaint against the brand inspector, who worked for the State, and another defendant, who was not a party to the appeal, asserting that the brand inspector negligently permitted the resale of cattle without the proper title clearance and that plaintiff was injured thereby.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted the brand inspector summary judgment by concluding that the state board of stock inspection was a law enforcement authority within the meaning of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-80-103(1)(c) (1987 Repl.), that the brand inspector was a law enforcement officer within the scope of that provision, and that plaintiff's claim was barred by the one-year statute of limitations period contained in § 13-80-103(1)(c). Plaintiff contended on appeal that § 13-80-103(1)(c) violated due process by being unconstitutionally vague for its failure to incorporate a definition of the term "any other law enforcement authority." The court disagreed and held that § 13-80-103(1)(c) was not void-for-vagueness and was sufficiently clear to permit an individual of ordinary intelligence to ascertain the meaning of "other law enforcement authority" by reference to the peace officer classification statute of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-901 (1992 Cum. Supp.). The court further held that the one year limitation in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-80-103(1)(c) (1987 Repl.) was reasonable and related to the legitimate governmental objective of establishing time limitations within which to file a claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Spradling v. Colorado Dep't of Revenue


No. 92CA1253, No. 92CA1279


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


870 P.2d 521; 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 203; 17 BTR 1202



July 15, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 26, 1993. Certiorari Denied April 4, 1994 (93SC575).
Released For Publication April 12, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable L. Stern, III, Judge. No. 91CV3345



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of a judgment from the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which dismissed an action that was brought after Colo. Rev. Stat. § 39-22-104(4) (Supp. 1992) limited the tax exemption for beneficiaries receiving disability retirement payments from the Public Employees' Retirement Association (PERA). The taxpayers claimed that the statute unconstitutionally reduced disability benefits.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers received disability retirement payments from PERA. At the time these payments commenced, the benefits were not subject to state income tax. However, the general assembly amended Colo. Rev. Stat. § 39-22-104(4) (Supp. 1992), limiting the tax exemption for such benefits to beneficiaries over 55. Consequently, the taxpayers brought an action, claiming § 39-22-104(4) was unconstitutional insofar as it reduced the benefits to which the taxpayers were entitled. The trial court held that even though the taxpayers enjoyed a right to the benefits, no corresponding right existed to the tax exemption covering those benefits. Accordingly, the taxpayers sought review, and the court affirmed. The court rejected the contention that § 39-22-104(4) had violated the constitutional prohibition against contractual impairment. The court held § 39-22-104(4) was not constitutionally invalid insofar as it subjected the taxpayers' benefits to state income tax because § 39-22-104(4) had not reduced the statutory benefits to which the taxpayers were contractually entitled and because there was no contractual right to a tax exemption for such benefits.


OUTCOME: In affirming a judgment which dismissed the taxpayers' action that was brought after the tax exemption for beneficiaries receiving disability retirement payments from the PERA was statutorily limited, the court upheld the constitutionality of the statutory limitation.

Freedom from Religion Found. v. State


No. 92CA0107


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


872 P.2d 1256; 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 166; 17 BTR 972



June 17, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 19, 1993. Certiorari Granted May 2, 1994 (93SC554). Certiorari Granted on the following issues: Whether the Court of Appeals opinion engaged in impermissible appellate fact finding, for instance in determining the context of the monument - in State park - contrary to the explicit finding of the trial court. Whether the Court of Appeals opinion improperly relied on school setting cases. Whether the Court of Appeals opinion improperly relied on school setting cases. Whether the Court of Appeals opinion contravenes precedent by concluding that it is axiomatic that the religious nature of the monument - in a State park - makes it unconstitutional. Whether the Court of Appeals' opinion misapplied the holdings in Ston v. Graham, 449 U.S. 39 (1980); and Lynch v. Donnelly, 456 U.S. 668 (1984). Released for Publication May 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Warren O. Martin, Judge. No. 89CV4275



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, non-profit corporations and citizens, appealed a judgment from the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which was entered for defendants, state and its officials, in plaintiffs' action seeking the removal of a stone monument containing the Ten Commandments.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed the action against defendants seeking the removal of the stone monument containing the Ten Commandments, which was located in a park near the state capitol. Plaintiffs alleged that the stone's existence violated the "establishment clause" of the First Amendment and the comparable provision of the state constitution. The trial court entered a judgment for defendants. Because the court concluded that the monument offended against the controlling constitutional provisions, the court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment. The court concluded that, contrary to the state's assertion, no other monument in the capitol complex served to interpret the Ten Commandments outside its essential religious context. The court concluded further that the monument conveyed an essential religious message that would have appeared to the reasonable observer to be endorsed and approved by the state because of its contents and its location on the property of the state, which was clearly identified as such.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment, which was entered for defendants in plaintiffs' action seeking the removal of the stone monument containing the Ten Commandments.
