Stamm v. City & County of Denver


No. 92CA0265


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


856 P.2d 54; 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 157; 17 BTR 867



June 3, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 18, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Frank Martinez, Judge. No. 89CV16665



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND ORDER REINSTATED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city, a county, the department of public works, the airport, the career authority (the authority), and a hearing officer, sought review of an order of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which vacated the authority's termination of plaintiff employee. The employee was reinstated with back pay and benefits.


OVERVIEW: The employee was terminated for working while under the influence of alcohol. An executive order and a career service rule provided for the termination, however, the employee filed a suit for judicial review of the termination. The trial court vacated the termination order and reinstated the employee with back pay and benefits. But on appeal, the court reversed the trial court's order and reinstated the termination order holding, against the employee's contentions, that the executive order was not unconstitutionally vague. The court further held that the executive order provided persons of ordinary intelligence sufficient notice as to what type of conduct constituted a violation. The court also held that the hearing officer correctly gave the language being under the influence or impaired by alcohol, as used in the executive order, its generally accepted meaning. Finally, the court held that the record contained ample support for the employee's termination for his violation of the executive order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order of the trial court, which vacated the authority's termination of the employee and reinstated him with back pay and benefits. The authority's order was reinstated.

People v. Turley


No. 90CA1513


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


870 P.2d 498; 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 140; 17 BTR 806



May 20, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified Rehearing Denied August 5, 1993. Certiorari Denied March 21, 1994 (93SC539).
Released For Publication April 12, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable H. Jeffrey Bayless, Judge. No. 89CR1651, No. 89CR1652



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction in the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), after a jury verdict finding him guilty of first degree sexual assault, second degree kidnapping, and three counts of habitual criminal. Defendant argued in part that he should have been given the victim's address and access to her mental health records and that the trial court did not advise him of the consequences of testifying.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of first degree sexual assault, second degree kidnapping, and charges of habitual criminal. On appeal he claimed that the trial court made numerous errors, in part by refusing him the victim's address and access to her mental health records and by failing to advise him of the consequences of testifying. The court affirmed the convictions, holding that the rule allowing defendant to have the victim's address did not apply when the witness legitimately feared reprisal from defendant. Here, defendant made multiple, express threats against her and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the information. The court also ruled that defendant failed to meet his initial burden of showing a necessity for the victim's mental health records. He failed to establish that the records contained material evidence. The court also held that when facing a habitual criminal charge, defendant was entitled to notice that admissions to prior felonies were not used as substantive evidence at trial. Here, defendant was explicitly advised that the prior convictions could have been used for impeachment and the jury considered them with regard to credibility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for first degree sexual assault, second degree kidnapping, and being a habitual criminal.

Donn v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office


No. 92CA0863


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


865 P.2d 873; 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 142; 17 BTR 827



May 20, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 15, 1993. Released for Publication September 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. UR No. 118



DISPOSITION: ORDER SET ASIDE AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner worker challenged an order of respondent Industrial Claim Appeals Office (Office) (Colorado) requiring her to change her authorized health care provider in her action for workers' compensation benefits based on an injury in the scope of her employment.


OVERVIEW: The worker was injured in an automobile accident that occurred during the course of her employment. The worker filed a claim for benefits, and the Office ordered her to change her authorized health care provider. The worker sought review, and the court set aside and remanded the order. The court held that the Office erroneously excluded evidence related to the necessity of the worker's treatment by her authorized provider without considering whether there was justification for the failure to timely present the evidence. Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-43-501(2)(a) (1992 Cum. Supp.). Also, the worker was entitled to judicial review of the Office's ruling in the medical utilization review proceeding under § 8-43-207; therefore, the procedure did not violate her due process rights. The Office did not retroactively apply § 8-43-501 when denying payments to the worker's authorized provider because the payments were denied under the law as it existed at that time. Finally, only the authorized provider could challenge the denial of benefits because the worker was not liable for the payment of the costs of the services; therefore, the worker lacked standing to assert that issue.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the order requiring the worker to change her authorized health care provider and remanded her workers' compensation action to the Office.

First Bank v. State, Dep't of Regulatory Agencies, Div. of Banking


No. 92CA0386


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


852 P.2d 1345; 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 110; 17 BTR 662



April 22, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable Donald E. Campbell, Judge. No. 90CV3458



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bank challenged the decision of the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado), which affirmed the order of the Colorado State Banking Board (Board). In its order, the Board denied the bank's request to rescind the Board's earlier order for possession and liquidation of the bank's assets.


OVERVIEW: An investigation of the bank disclosed that the bank was inadequately capitalized. Pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 11-3-104, the Board issued a notice of impairment and order to levy an assessment. The bank than applied to the Board seeking rescission of the Board's order. However, Board denied the bank's request. On appeal of the trial court's decision, the bank contended that the Board exceeded its statutory authority by failing to provide proper notice and a hearing prior to seizing and liquidating the bank. The court held that the bank filed its application within 10 days and no claim was made that the Board failed to provide a prompt hearing. Therefore, the court held that the Board did not violate the applicable statutes by going forward with the liquidation of the assets of the bank and then providing the requested hearing. Moreover, the court held that the Board did not fail to make the "extraordinary circumstances requiring immediate action" finding required by the statute. Additionally, the court held that there was sufficient evidence to constitute "extraordinary circumstances".


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision which affirmed the Board's order that had denied the bank's request to rescind the Board's earlier order for possession and liquidation of the bank's assets.

Warren v. Southern Colo. Excavators

COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE

March 25, 1993, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 3-576-332



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant sought review of an order by respondent Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado (Panel), which dismissed his petition to review an order by of respondent Division of Workers' Compensation denying his application for a lump sum award.


OVERVIEW: The Panel concluded that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-43-406(1) precluded review of a director's denial of a lump sum distribution for abuse of discretion and dismissed claimant's petition for lack of jurisdiction. The Panel also concluded that, if it had jurisdiction, it would affirm the director's order on the merits. Claimant contended that because § 8-43-406(1) contained no detailed standard for determining whether an application for lump sum distribution should be granted or denied, it was unconstitutionally vague and represented an unconstitutional delegation of power. The court disagreed and affirmed. The court perceived no constitutional violation, especially because claimant did not have an absolute right to a lump sum award. The statute did not constitute an unconstitutional delegation of power to an administrative agency. Because the petition challenged only the director's exercise of discretion, the decision was not subject to appellate review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Panel.

DeMarco v. Colorado Ltd. Gaming Control Comm'n


No. 92CA0329


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


855 P.2d 23; 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 132; 17 BTR 719



March 18, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Selected for Publication May 6, 1993. Released for Publication July 13, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Colorado Limited Gaming Control Commission. No. GAD91000



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant sought review of a decision by Colorado Limited Gaming Control Commission (commission) to deny the applicant's request for a limited gaming support license pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-47.1-501(1)(d) (1991 Repl.)


OVERVIEW: The commission denied the applicant's request for a gaming support license pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-47.1-501(1)(d) (1991 Repl.). The commission denied the request on the ground that the applicant had been convicted of a gambling-related misdemeanor more than twenty years before his request. The commission was permitted to deny the license on that ground pursuant to § 12-47.01-501(1)(d). On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that because § 12-47.1-501(1)(d) was reasonably related to the proper goal of assuring both honest gaming and the public perception that such gaming was honest, it did not offend against any principle of due process. The court further held that because the group of persons having been convicted of the crimes listed in § 12-47.01-501(1)(d) did not constitute a "suspect class" and the "right" to engage in gambling was not a fundamental one, the statute could not have been considered to be invalid so long as it was reasonably related to a legitimate state interest. The court held that the concern for public confidence in regulated gambling was a legitimate interest; therefore the statute did not offend equal protection principles.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commission's decision to deny the applicant's request for a gaming support license based on the applicant's misdemeanor conviction for a gambling-related offense.

Barrett v. University of Colo. Health Sciences Ctr.


No. 92CA0061


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


851 P.2d 258; 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 60; 8 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 753; 61 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 369; 17 BTR 390



March 11, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 24, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the State Personnel Board. No. 901 B 158



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a judgment of appellee State Personnel Board (Colorado), which affirmed the decision of the hearing officer, which determined that the employee had committed wilful misconduct in violation of appellee employer's rule, 4 Colo. Code Regs. § 801-1 (1986).


OVERVIEW: The hearing officer determined that the employee had committed wilful misconduct in violation of the employer's rule, 4 Colo. Code Regs. § 801-1 (1986). The board affirmed the officer's decision, and the employee sought review. Pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-4-105(15)(b) (1988), the board was not entitled to disturb the officer's findings of evidentiary fact unless contrary to the weight of the evidence. The court held that the determination of whether conduct constituted "willful misconduct" was a finding of ultimate fact and could only have been disturbed on appellate review only if it was unsupported by any competent evidence. The court found that a finding of willful misconduct was not limited to a violation of specific rules or standards. The court further determined that there need not be actual intent to wrong the employer in order to constitute willful misconduct and further found that a reckless disregard of the employee's duties to the employer was sufficient. The court held that the employee's speech was not protected by the First Amendment because it failed to touch a matter of public concern. The court affirmed the judgment of the board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the board, which affirmed a decision of the officer, which determined that the employee had committed wilful misconduct in violation of the employer's rule.

 

1578 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Peister v. State, Dep't of Social Servs., Office of Appeals


No. 91CA1833, No. 92CA0215


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


849 P.2d 894; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 470; 17 BTR 19; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P17,251A



December 31, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected. Rehearing Denied February 25, 1993. Released for Publication April 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Robert S. Hyatt, Judge. Honorable Herbert L. Stern, III, Judge. No. 91CV4000



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, plaintiff applicants for social security benefits appealed from the judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which affirmed defendant department of social services' (department) denial of benefits under the Old Age Pension Program. The applicants had filed actions against defendants, state and county departments of social services, and employees.


OVERVIEW: The applicants believed that the use of social security numbers threatened their future spiritual well being because the numbers represented the "mark of the beast," and the applicants returned their social security cards to the federal Social Security Administration and resigned from the system. When they applied for Colorado Old Age Pension benefits, the county department denied their applications based on their refusal to provide social security numbers. The state department affirmed the denial, which the trial court also affirmed. On further appeal, the court affirmed the denial of benefits. 9 Colo. Code Regs. 2503-3,3.110.25 (1983) required the applicants to provide their social security numbers so the county department could determine their need for assistance. The regulation was uniformly applied to all applicants and promoted a legitimate and important public interest by allowing the departments to determine and verify the applicants' eligibility for benefits. Thus, the regulation did not discriminate against the applicants' religious beliefs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments that affirmed the department's denial of Old Age Pension benefits to the applicants for their failure to provide their social security numbers.

 

1579 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


D.C. Burns Realty & Trust v. Jefferson County Bd. of County Comm'rs


No. 91CA2062


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


849 P.2d 900; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 473; 17 BTR 32



December 31, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended January 14, 1993. Rehearing Denied February 4, 1993. Released for Publication April 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Colorado State Board of Assessment. Appeals Nos. 14588, 14589, 14590, 14591, and 14592



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer appealed a decision from respondent Board of Assessment Appeals of the State of Colorado (BAA), which dismissed the taxpayer's appeals from adverse rulings from appellee Jefferson County Board of County Commissioners. The Board had denied the taxpayer's petitions for an abatement or refund of a portion of its 1989 property taxes.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer filed petitions under a protest and adjustment procedure for an abatement or refund of a portion of its 1989 property taxes. After an arbitrator rendered a decision the taxpayer filed petitions under an abatement and refund procedure with the Board. The Board denied the taxpayer's petitions under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 39-10-114(1)(a)(I) (1990). The taxpayer appealed to the BAA, and the Board filed a motion to dismiss. The BAA denied the motion but thereafter granted the motion to dismiss upon the Board's motion for reconsideration. The taxpayer appealed, and the court reversed the decision of the BAA and remanded. The court held that the BAA was required to consider the merits of the taxpayer's overvaluation claims concerning the 1989 tax year. Pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 39-10-114(1)(a)(I)(D) (Cum. Supp. 1992) the taxpayer had the right to assert overvaluation claims concerning the 1989 tax year under the abatement and refund procedure notwithstanding what occurred under the protest and adjustment procedure. The BAA should have conducted de novo evidentiary proceedings on the merits in the matter. The law was not given unconstitutional retroactive effect.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the BAA and remanded the case with directions to conduct a new hearing to consider the merits of the taxpayer's overvaluation claims concerning the 1989 tax year.

 

1580 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Magness v. State by Dep't of Highways


No. 91CA1892


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


844 P.2d 1304; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 435; 16 BTR 1940



December 3, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable William G. Meyer, Judge. No. 90CV5889



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a decision of the District Court, City and County of Denver (Colorado), which upheld the determination of the Administrative Law Judge that appellee Department of Highways properly approved a limited access permit to the landowner.


OVERVIEW: The landowner argued that the Highway Access Code violated Colo. Const. art. V, § 39 because it unlawfully delegated the law-making function to an administrative agency. The court lacked jurisdiction to review the contention. The landowner also argued that the Code violated the principles of equal protection by dividing access permit applications into private and public categories. Any distinction created by the Highway Access Code for private direct access as applied in the case was rationally related to the objectives of the Code. The Department was not precluded from addressing whether the village properly evaluated the application. The administrative law judge was entitled to weigh the state of the evidence for its persuasive value against the landowner's argument that the issuance of the permit alone was sufficient to establish that the right turn only plan had been found unacceptable by the village. There was substantial record support for the finding that the landowner failed to satisfy his burden of proof under the Code, and therefore the court could not overturn that finding on review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1581 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Rather v. Conte


No. 91CA1848


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


849 P.2d 884; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 442; 16 BTR 1938



December 3, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended December 31, 1992. Rehearing Denied December 31, 1992. Certiorari Denied April 19, 1993 (93SC69). Released for Publication April 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Crowley County. Honorable M. Jon Kolomitz, Judge. No. 91CV2



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmates appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Crowley County (Colorado), which dismissed their action alleging claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against defendant corrections facility officials.


OVERVIEW: The inmates were terminated from their jobs in the correctional facility dishroom and physical plant for being absent from their work assignments in violation of certain operational rules, although none of them were charged with a violation of the penal code. The inmates each filed grievances which were denied. They thereafter brought the instant action which claimed that they were denied notice of the charges and a hearing prior to their terminations. The trial court granted the officials' motion to dismiss and on appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the inmates failed to state a claim under § 1983. The court concluded that the inmates had no legitimate expectation of continued employment in their prison work assignments. The operational rules provided that charges did not need to be filed prior to termination of an inmate's employment position. They additionally provided that an inmate could be terminated from his employment for failure to report to his work assignment. The court concluded that the inmates had no protected right to continued employment in their prison work assignments. Accordingly, dismissal of the action was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of dismissal of the inmates' action alleging failure to receive notice and a hearing prior to their prison work assignment terminations by the prison officials.

 

1582 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Walgreen Co. v. Charnes


No. 92CA0730


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO


859 P.2d 235; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 429; 16 BTR 1949



December 3, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 31, 1992. Ceritorari Denied September 27, 1993. Released for Publication October 13, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable H. Jeffrey Bayless, Judge. No. 89CV11049



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the judgment of the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado), which concluded that the corporation's purchase of advertising supplements that were distributed in a newspaper constituted a taxable privilege as contemplated by Denver Revised Municipal Code § 53.96 and as assessed by appellees, city, county, and manager of revenue.


OVERVIEW: The advertiser had advertising supplements that were distributed in the newspaper, and defendants assessed taxes on the supplements under Denver Revised Municipal Code § 53.96. The trial court ruled in favor of defendants, and the court affirmed as to all but the advertiser's equal protection claim. The court affirmed because (1) the advertiser did not purchase its advertising to sell the supplements themselves; (2) the supplements were not purchased to become an integral component part of the newspapers and were not wholesale transactions; (3)when Denver Manager of Revenue Rules Regarding the Assessment and Collection of Sales and Use Taxes 4 was read in conjunction with Denver Manager of Revenue Rule 1, it created a separate taxable liability for an advertiser; and, (4) application of the use tax to its purchase of the supplements did not violate the guarantees of freedom of speech because there was no attempt to regulate the content of the advertiser's commercial speech. The court remanded so that the trial court could determine whether the supplements were subject to a tax, while other advertising was not, and whether a violation of equal protection occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which concluded that the corporation's purchase of advertising supplements that were distributed in a newspaper constituted a taxable privilege. However, the court remanded the cause so that the trial court could make findings as to the corporation's equal protection claims.

 

1583 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hampton


No. 91CA1057


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


857 P.2d 441; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 416; 16 BTR 1797



November 19, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 7, 1993. Second Rehearing Denied January 28, 1993. Certiorari Granted September 7, 1993 (93SC77). Released for Publication September 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable Richard V. Hall, Judge. No. 83CR2245



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado), which denied his Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c) motions to set aside his conviction for habitual criminality.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of first degree sexual assault and habitual criminality. Defendant filed a Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c) motion alleging erroneous jury instruction in the habitual criminal phase of the trial. The trial court found that the motions were untimely under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-5-402 (1986) and rejected the motions on the merits. The court held that defendant's motions were timely and affirmed. The instructional error, if any, had not so undermined the basic fairness of the trial as to cast serious doubt on the reliability of the judgment of conviction. The jury was instructed on the presumption of innocence during the sexual assault phase of the trial. Although it was not repeated at the habitual criminal phase, the trial court reminded the jury that all earlier instructions applied. The failure to submit separate verdict forms on each prior conviction did not cast serious doubt on the reliability of the jury's finding of habitual criminality. The verdict form was adequate to demonstrate that the jury unanimously agreed that defendant was the same person identified in the prosecution's documents and that he was previously convicted of each of the subject felonies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying defendant's motions to set aside his conviction for habitual criminality.

 

1584 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Lehman v. City of Louisville


No. 91CA1259


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


857 P.2d 455; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 417; 16 BTR 1805



November 19, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified Rehearing Denied January 7, 1993. Certiorari Denied August 23, 1993 (93SC75). Released for Publication September 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Boulder. Honorable Richard C. McLean, Judge. No. 90CV1483



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed a judgment from the District Court of Boulder (Colorado), which dismissed their claim against defendant city based upon the Colorado Governmental Immunity Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-10-106(1) (1988 Repl.), and refused to grant leave to amend their amended complaint.


OVERVIEW: After communicating their intended use of an historic church as a residence and as a business that was to be operated by persons other than family members, landowners alleged that city's development director informed them that such use was permitted under the existing zoning code and, relying upon the director's representations, they purchased and renovated the property. Later, they were told by the city's administrator that the intended business by non-family members violated the zoning ordinance, Louisville, Colo., Municipal Code § 17.08.225. In response to that determination, the landowners filed this action, grounded in estoppel, seeking damages and injunctive relief. The district court dismissed the complaint based on the Colorado Governmental Immunity Act (Act), Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-10-106(1) (1988 Repl.), and refused to grant leave to amend their amended complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the estoppel claim, the essence of which was either a negligent or intentional misrepresentation, was either a tort or could lie in tort. The court further held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying a motion to amend a futile complaint.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment dismissing an estoppel claim against the city as barred by the Colorado Governmental Immunity Act.

 

1585 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Tomsha v. City of Colorado Springs


No. 92CA0603


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


856 P.2d 13; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 423; 16 BTR 1826



November 19, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 31, 1992. Certiorari Denied July 26, 1993. Released for Publication August 18, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 3-974-156



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant sought review of an order from respondent Colorado Industrial Claim Appeals Office (appeals office), which denied and dismissed his claim for benefits based on work-related stress. The claimant also challenged the constitutionality of the work-related stress statute, 1990 Colo. Sess. Laws ch. 62, § 8-41-301(2).


OVERVIEW: The claimant, a patrol officer, alleged that he developed temporomandibular joint condition as a result of job stress. The appeals office found that the claim was not supported by the testimony of a licensed physician or psychologist as required by 1990 Colo. Sess. Laws ch. 62, § 8-41-301(2)(a). The court affirmed the denial of benefits, rejecting the claimant's contention that the appeals office erred in interpreting the term "physician" as not including a dentist. The court also held that the statute was constitutional, rejecting the claimant's contention that the statute violated equal protection guarantees. The court concluded that requiring verification of the mental component of a stress claim by a physician or psychologist was rationally related to the purpose of the statute, which was to establish the proof requirements to prevent frivolous and unnecessary claims. The court also rejected the claimant's contention that the stress statute deprived him of his federal civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1981.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that denied and dismissed the claimant's request for benefits based on work-related stress. The court also held that the work-related stress statute was constitutional.

 

1586 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Rosa v. Warner Elec. Contracting


No. 91CA1523


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


849 P.2d 845; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 343; 16 BTR 1457



September 10, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 8, 1992. Certiorari Granted April 12, 1993 (92SC689). Released for Publication April 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Order from the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 3-868-948



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the dependents of a deceased employee, sought review of an order of the Industrial Claims Appeals Office of the State of Colorado, which determined that respondents, an employer and the Colorado Compensation Insurance Authority, were entitled to offset 100 percent of the dependent's workers' compensation dependency benefits against their social security benefits.


OVERVIEW: Because the dependents' combined social security death benefits exceeded the amount of workers' compensation benefits awarded, the entire amount of the workers' compensation benefits was offset by the social security benefits. The dependents challenged the constitutionality of the Colorado workers' compensation offset statute. On appeal, the court held that the Colorado workers' compensation offset statute did not violate the supremacy clause because the offset mandated by Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-50-103 did not exceed the scope of such an offset permitted by the Federal Social Security Act. Because the dependents were entitled to benefits on the basis of wages, the state offset did not exceed the scope of the state offset permitted by the Federal Social Security Act and there was no violation of the supremacy clause. In addition, the offset did not constitute an equal protection violation even though benefits of disabled workers were offset by only 50 percent, while benefits of dependents of deceased workers were offset by 100 percent because there was no evidence showing a suspect classification. The court concluded that § 8-50-103 was without constitutional defect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order below.

People v. Aldrich


No. 90CA0871


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


849 P.2d 821; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 319; 16 BTR 1360



August 13, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 10, 1992. Certiorari Denied March 22, 1993 (92SC674). Released for Publication April 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Teller County. Honorable Jane Looney, Judge. No. 89CR0045



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction entered by the District Court of Teller County (Colorado) on jury verdicts finding him guilty of three counts of sexual assault on a child.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred, inter alia, by refusing to admit evidence of one of the victim's prior sexual assault. The court noted that pursuant to Col. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-407 (1986), the rape shield statute law in effect at the time of the crime, there was a statutory presumption of the irrelevance of prior sexual conduct. The court held that prior sexual conduct included prior sexual assaults. Because defendant failed to comply with the statutory requirement of a pretrial hearing on such evidence, the trial court properly refused to admit evidence of the alleged prior sexual assault. Defendant also claimed that hearsay statements made by another of the victims to a therapist were improperly admitted into evidence. The court held that the content of the statements were not important; rather the significance of the therapist's testimony was to explain the scientific data in the area of child abuse and to assist the jury by relating how the victim's statements fit into that criteria.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction.

 

1588 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mershon


No. 90CA2030


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


844 P.2d 1240; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 287; 16 BTR 1255



July 16, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended July 17, 1992. Rehearing Denied August 13, 1992. Certiorari Granted February 8, 1993. Released for Publication February 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of El Paso County. Honorable Steven T. Pelican, Judge. No. 90CR142



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision by the District Court of El Paso County (Colorado), which convicted defendant of distribution and possession of a controlled drug and conspiracy to distribute a controlled substance. The prosecution appealed the trial court's order entered after a proportionality review of defendant's habitual criminal conviction reducing defendant's sentence from life to 35 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judgments of conviction. The prosecution asserted that the trial court erred in reducing the sentence to 35 years. Under the circumstances in the case, the court found no error in the trial court's denial of enforcement of the plea agreement. Defendant presented no factual circumstances, which would have constituted excusable neglect. Defendant's argument that he had no present need to collaterally attack his previous convictions until habitual criminal charges were filed was without merit. Hence, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's collateral attack of his prior felony convictions. Defendant's affirmative defense of entrapment was accurately and correctly set forth in the instructions given the trial court. Thus, the trial court did not err in refusing defendant's instructions on entrapment. The court perceived no abuse of discretion in the conclusion of the trial court that, as to defendant, the imposition of a life sentence was unconstitutional. The court found no abuse of discretion in the trial court's reduction of defendant's life sentence to 35 years imprisonment. Hence, the court affirmed the judgments of conviction and the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for distribution and possession of a controlled drug and conspiracy to distribute a controlled substance and defendant's sentence reduction from life to 35 years imprisonment.

People v. Coleman


No. 89CA1523


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO


844 P.2d 1215; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 269; 16 BTR 1148



July 2, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 20, 1992. Certiorari Denied February 1, 1993 (92SC616). Released for Publication February 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Arapahoe County Honorable Jack F. Smith, Judge. No. 87CR900.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the District Court, Eighteenth Judicial District (Colorado), which entered a jury verdict convicting him of second degree burglary, misdemeanor theft, and four counts of prior felony convictions to invoke the habitual offender statute. On appeal, defendant contested the denial of his challenge for cause of a juror and the trial court's refusal to suppress evidence of his four prior felony convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of his burglary and theft convictions that, in combination with his prior felony convictions, invoked the habitual criminal statute and resulted in the imposition of five concurrent life sentences. After its review of defendant's challenges and the record, the court affirmed the trial court's decision, concluding that (1) the trial court was correct in finding that the challenged juror was not an "employee" under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-10-103(1)(k) and was not disqualified from jury service; (2) the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to dismiss because a delay in trial proceedings resulted from the prosecution's discovery of new information regarding defendant's four prior felony convictions, and there was no violation of defendant's speedy trial right; and (3) the trial court did not err in refusing to suppress evidence of those four prior convictions because the sentencing court properly advised defendant of the potential penalties resulting from defendant's pleas and assured defendant's knowing and voluntary acceptance. The court remanded the matter, however, to allow correction of the mittimus to reflect a single life sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and the cause was remanded for correction of the mittimus to show one life sentence.

People v. Slusher


No. 90CA1106


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO


844 P.2d 1222; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 272; 16 BTR 1156



July 2, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 13, 1992. Certiorari Denied February 1, 1993 (92SC568). Released for Publication February 17, 1993.
Later proceeding at Slusher v. People, 1993 Colo. LEXIS 79 (Colo., Feb. 1, 1993)
Writ of certiorari denied Slusher v. Colorado, 509 U.S. 928, 113 S. Ct. 3050, 125 L. Ed. 2d 735, 1993 U.S. LEXIS 4556 (1993)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Slusher v. Gabler, 36 F.3d 1105, 1994 U.S. App. LEXIS 33587 (10th Cir. Colo., 1994)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Ruthanne N. Polidori, Judge. No. 89CR406.
People v. Kibel, 701 P.2d 37, 1985 Colo. LEXIS 454 (Colo., 1985)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Jefferson County (Colorado) convicted defendant on three counts of sexual exploitation of a child and one count of being an habitual offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and convicted of three counts of sexual exploitation of a child in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-403. This occurred after defendant, who was on probation and being investigated for the crimes charged, had his home searched by probation officers without a warrant. This turned up nude photos of a child with whom police had already made contact and, based on the photos found, a warrant was issued which allowed the police to search defendant's home as well. Defendant challenged both searches as unlawful but the court, when affirming defendant's convictions, found defendant's claims meritless. The parole officers had reasonable grounds to believe defendant might be sexually exploiting a child and, thus, that defendant had violated parole. Thus, a parole search was appropriate and the information obtained there provided probable cause for the later police search. While the police's warrant was invalid because it did not particularly describe the items to be seized, this was cured by the particularity of the corresponding affidavit, upon which the search warrant was based.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

1591 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. T.S.R.


No. 91CA0987


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO


843 P.2d 105; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 283; 16 BTR 1185



July 2, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 30, 1992. Certiorari Denied January 4, 1993 (92SC545). Released for Publication January 19, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Routt County Honorable Richard P. Doucette, Judge. No. 90JV2.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed from a judgment of the District Court, Fourteenth Judicial District, (Colorado), which denied his motion to allow him credit for 311 days he spent in pre-adjudicatory detention.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile shot his step-father in the back of the neck with a rifle and spent 311 days in pre-adjudicatory detention. He was found guilty of first degree assault committed under a heat of passion. He was committed to the Department of Institutions for two years and the trial court refused to give him credit for the 311 days he had already spent in detention. The juvenile sought post-conviction relief. The court denied the juvenile's motion and affirmed. The court found that the sentence and the denial of credit did not violate the state or federal prohibitions against cruel and unusual punishment because there was nothing unfair or shocking to the conscience either in the trial court's imposition of a two-year commitment as provided by Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-2-704(3) or in its refusal to grant credit for pre-dispositional detention. Additionally, there was no statutory provision that allowed for pretrial detention credit. As for the juvenile's assertion that that the statutory scheme was unconstitutionally applied, there was ample evidence in the record to support the commitment decision made by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court found that the trial court's sentence and the denial of credit did not violate the state or federal prohibitions against cruel and unusual punishment and affirmed the trial court's two-year commitment of the juvenile.

 

1592 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Colorado State Bd. of Medical Examiners v. Slonim


No. 91CA0998


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


844 P.2d 1207; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 260; 16 BTR 1057



June 18, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Colorado State Board of Medical Examiners. No. ME-89-03



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent doctor appealed an order from the Colorado State Board of Medical Examiners, which issued to him a letter of admonition for substandard care with regard to one of his patients under the Medical Practice Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-36-101 et seq. (1991).


OVERVIEW: After diagnosing his patient with depression, a doctor prescribed a certain stimulant, in violation of an administrative rule promulgated by the state Board of Medical Examiners. Based upon this treatment, the board filed a formal complaint charging him with unprofessional conduct. The administrative law judge (ALJ) determined that such prescribing constituted an act which failed to meet generally accepted standards of medical practice. However, because the doctor had committed only one act of substandard care, even though he had written seven prescriptions over 18 months, the ALJ determined that there was no unprofessional conduct under the Medical Practice Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-36-101 et seq. (1991). On review of the initial decision, the board reversed the ALJ and, finding "two or more" acts, the board issued a letter of admonition. On appeal, the court held that the language of the rule was specific enough to withstand a vagueness attack. However, the court reversed, holding that the renewal of the prescription was part of a single act of medical practice, which did not constitute unprofessional conduct, notwithstanding that the events were not limited to a single date.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the order of admonition against the doctor and remanded with directions to dismiss the charges of unprofessional conduct.

 

1593 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Martinez


No. 91CA1266


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


844 P.2d 1203; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 249; 16 BTR 999



June 4, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 16, 1992. Certiorari Denied February 1, 1993 (92SC532). Released for Publication February 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Morgan County. Honorable Joseph Weatherby, Judge. No. 91CR9



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the sentence imposed by the District Court of Morgan County (Colorado) following the entry of defendant's guilty pleas to one class 6 felony, two misdemeanors, and a traffic offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with various felony and misdemeanor offenses as the result of an incident in which defendant, while intoxicated, stole two motor vehicles and broke into a third. He entered guilty pleas to a class 6 felony, two misdemeanor counts, and one traffic offense, and the remaining charges were dismissed. The district court sentenced defendant to a 10-year term of probation for the class 6 felony and one-year probation on each of the misdemeanor counts, which were ordered to run concurrently. The court affirmed, finding that the district court did not exceed its jurisdiction in imposing a 10-year sentence of probation. The court held that the sentencing limitations in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-105 (1986 Repl. Vol. 8B) did not apply to sentences to probation and that the statute in no way limited the duration of the probationary term. The court found that the district court did not abuse its discretion in imposing sentence and that the imposition of a 10-year probationary term did not deny defendant equal protection under the laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence of a 10-year term of probation for the class 6 felony and one-year probation on each of the misdemeanor counts, which were imposed by the district court following the entry of defendant's guilty pleas.

 

1594 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wilson


No. 90CA2001


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


841 P.2d 337; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 217; 16 BTR 820



May 21, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 30, 1992. Certiorari Denied December 14, 1992 (92SC558). Released for Publication December 23, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Teller County. Honorable Matt M. Railey, Judge. No. 90CR16



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Teller County (Colorado) that convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree, second degree burglary of a dwelling, sexual assault on a child, aggravated robbery, assault in the second degree, four counts of crimes of violence, and three habitual criminal counts. Defendant also challenged his four consecutive life sentences.


OVERVIEW: The evidence revealed that defendant, inter alia, unlawfully entered the home of his girlfriend and victimized her daughter at knifepoint. Blood and hair samples found in the girl's bedroom matched those provided by defendant, and a jury convicted him as charged. In affirming the judgments of conviction, the court held that a statement made to a police officer while the blood and hair samples were being obtained from defendant was properly admitted because the statement was voluntarily made, it had not been made pursuant to interrogation, and defendant had initiated the conversation. The court also ruled that the trial court properly admitted testimony that the victim had been receiving rape counseling, had suffered from post-traumatic stress syndrome, and would require another year of treatment. Finally, the court concluded that it was appropriate for the trial court to have imposed consecutive sentences under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-11-309(1)(a) (Cum. Supp. 1991).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and his four consecutive life sentences.

 

1595 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Anderson


No. 91CA1818


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


837 P.2d 293; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 251; 16 BTR 854



May 21, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 21, 1992. Rehearing Denied June 25, 1992. Certiorari Denied October 13, 1992 (92sc451). Released for Publication October 15, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Jefferson County. Honorable Henry E. Nieto, Judge. No. 88CR428



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the District Court of Jefferson County (Colorado) for conspiracy to distribute a controlled substance and of special offender status under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-107 (1986 Repl. Vol. 8B) for importing a controlled substance into Colorado.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of conspiracy to distribute a controlled substance as a special offender based on undercover transactions arranged by a confidential informant. The court affirmed, finding that it was not error to refuse to suppress the booking slip setting forth his address in Arizona because, although it was relevant to his special offender status for importing a controlled substance into Colorado, § 18-18-107, the routine booking questions did not constitute interrogation for Miranda purposes. Denial of defendant's motion to disclose the confidential informant was proper because she was not present during the actual transaction, other witnesses were available to testify as to the preceding discussions, defendant could have discovered her identity where she was a co-defendant's girlfriend, and her concern for her safety supported withholding the information. The police did not fail to preserve evidence where the information regarding defendant's gym membership and flight from Arizona was not lost or destroyed. The failure to reduce oral witness interviews to writing did not constitute prosecutorial misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for conspiracy to distribute a controlled substance and of special offender status for importing a controlled substance into Colorado.

 

1596 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rowe


No. 90CA1742


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


837 P.2d 260; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 149; 16 BTR 699



April 23, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 21, 1992. Certiorari Granted October 13, 1992 (92SC396). Released for Publication October 15, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the City and County of Denver. Honorable Robert P. Fullerton, Judge. No. 89CR1558



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the District Court of the City and County of Denver (Colorado) of first degree assault committed under the heat of passion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant managed a bar where an altercation occurred. Police, who entered the bar with the consent of its employees, recovered inculpatory evidence from the portion of the bar open to the public. Prior to defendant's trial on assault charges, the trial court ruled that defendant lacked standing to challenge the search of the bar. During trial, the trial court refused to permit defendant's investigator to testify as to the character of the victim, and also denied defendant's request that the jury be charged only as to second degree assault, and not first degree assault also. The jury convicted defendant of first degree assault committed under the heat of passion. On appeal, the court ruled that defendant did not have standing to challenge the search because the bar was open to the public and police were consensually admitted by its employees; the investigator was properly barred from giving character testimony because he had no personal knowledge of the victim; and a jury charge including instructions on first degree assault was proper because second degree assault was also included in the charge and the evidence was sufficient to support a conviction of first degree assault.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree assault committed under the heat of passion.

 

1597 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Goetz v. Gunter


No. 90CA1770


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION A


830 P.2d 1154; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 143; 16 BTR 701



April 23, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Fremont County. Honorable John Anderson, Judge. No. 90CV211



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate challenged a judgment of the District Court of Fremont County (Colorado), which denied the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus based on a claim that the inmate was denied due process of law when the Colorado State Board of Parole revoked his parole on a charge that he failed to give notice of a change of address. The inmate argued that his due process rights were denied by the delay in holding his revocation hearing.


OVERVIEW: The inmate also argued that the Board lacked jurisdiction to revoke his parole on a second charge. On appeal, the court agreed. A parolee's due process rights entitled him to a revocation hearing within a reasonable time; consideration was given to whether delay was due in part to the parolee's request for postponement. In the case at bar, a first charge resulted in the inmate's summons to appear before the Board, but because there was no arrest on that charge, the 30-day hearing requirement of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-2-103(7) (1986) did not apply. Further, the inmate requested continuances of the hearing on both charges. Thus, the delay between the filing of the first complaint and the final revocation hearing did not violate due process. However, although the filing of the first charge tolled the expiration of the inmate's parole, when that charge was dismissed, the inmate's parole status was reinstated as if no tolling had occurred, and the Board's continuing jurisdiction pending investigation of the charge ended. Finally, the inmate's parole term expired before the second charge was filed. As such, the Board lacked jurisdiction to revoke parole on that charge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter with directions to vacate the parole revocation.

 

1598 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Colorado State Bd. of Medical Examiners v. Hoffner


No. 90CA1938


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


832 P.2d 1062; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 108; 16 BTR 483



March 26, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 7, 1992. Released for Publication July 20, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Colorado State Board of Medical Examiners. No. ME-90-03



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent physician appealed from an order of complainant, the Colorado State Board of Medical Examiners (board), which revoked the physician's license to practice medicine based on the finding of the administrative law judge (ALJ) that the physician's conduct was unprofessional within the meaning of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-36-117(1)(i) (1991 Repl. Vol. 5B), which subjected physicians to discipline for habitual intemperance.


OVERVIEW: After the ALJ found that the physician's conduct fell within the prohibition against habitual intemperance and recommended that the physician be placed on probation, the board affirmed the ALJ's findings but rejected the recommendation as to the appropriate sanction. Contending that the term "habitual intemperance," as set forth in § 12-36-117(1)(i), was unconstitutionally vague and that she was denied due process, the physician appealed from the board's order revoking the physician's license to practice medicine. On appeal, the court affirmed the board's order because the term "habitual intemperance" gave the physician notice that the repeated, uncontrolled, excessive consumption of alcohol constituted unprofessional conduct that subjected physicians to discipline by the board. Although the ALJ found that the physician's conduct had not had a harmful effect on the physician's medical practice, the court ruled that the board did not abuse its discretion by revoking the physician's license because the evidence before the board supported the conclusion that allowing the physician to continue to practice medicine would not be in the public interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order revoking the physician's license to practice medicine.

 

1599 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Breniman v. Agricultural Consultants, Inc.


No. 90CA1088


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


829 P.2d 493; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 66; 16 BTR 382



March 12, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 20, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Adams County. Honorable Donald W. Marshall, Judge. No. 84CV1457



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation sought review of an order from the District Court of Adams County (Colorado), which entered a judgment ordering defendant to pay plaintiff stockholder the fair market value of his preferred stock.


OVERVIEW: Defendant corporation challenged the trial court's order, which entered a judgment ordering defendant to pay plaintiff stockholder the fair market value of his preferred stock. Defendant contended that the fixed redemption value of its preferred stock was a contractually agreed upon amount, which prevented plaintiff from obtaining a higher or fair market value. The court affirmed the order. The court found that the evidence in the record supported the trial court determination that adequate notice was provided to defendants. The court also found that state's interest in fairly compensating a dissenting shareholder, who under contemporary corporate statutes no longer had the power to prevent fundamental changes of the corporation, provided a rational basis for requiring fair value payment to all shareholders, including those with preferred stock.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which entered a judgment ordering defendant corporation to pay plaintiff stockholder the fair market value of his preferred stock. The court found that the statute provided that a dissenting shareholder was entitled to fair value of his stock where he was unable to prevent fundamental changes of defendant.

 

1600 of 1794 DOCUMENTS


Black v. First Federal Sav. & Loan Ass'n, F.A.


No. 90CA0227


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


830 P.2d 1103; 1992 Colo. App. LEXIS 52; 16 BTR 275



February 27, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion Modified, and as Modified Rehearing Denied April 30, 1992. Certiorari pending June 16, 1992 (92SC352). Certiorari Granted December 1, 1992 (92SC352).


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of La Plata County. Honorable Al H. Haas, Judge. No. 85CV454, No. 85CV456



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, limited partnership and a general/limited partner, appealed a judgment of the District Court of La Plata County (Colorado) in favor of plaintiffs, lenders and taxpayers, holding the partnership and partner liable to lenders for a deficiency on a promissory note and fraud in an action resulting from the partnership's default on a loan for a building leased to a government entity.


OVERVIEW: Limited partnership defaulted on a note obtained for a building leased by limited partner county hospital district (district), subject to a rental credit. The trial court rendered judgment on the note and on fraud claims in favor of the lenders. On appeal, the court affirmed. It held that the lease violated Colo. Const. art. XI, § 6's prohibition against governmental debt by loan because it contained no provision for cancellation and because appropriation of monies by the district to meet the rental obligation was nondiscretionary. Because it could not maintain its position as a limited partner and at the same time protect itself from becoming a party to an ultra vires contract, the district's participation in the limited partnership was void. General partners were jointly and severally liable when they executed the note and deed of trust for the limited partnership, and they were estopped from denying their acts. They were not relieved of personal liability for the partnership's obligations by the limited partnership's dissolution. The rental credit agreement was deliberately concealed from lenders to induce them to make the loan, and the loan was secured by inadequate collateral.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments in favor of the lenders and taxpayers were affirmed.
